1 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lucas


No. 65579


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 399; 548 N.E.2d 1003; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 162; 139 Ill. Dec. 447



December 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. James K. Robinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which entered convictions on counts of murder and of concealment of a homicidal death and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on four counts of murder and of concealment of a homicidal death and ultimately sentenced to death. The court held that, while defendant's convictions were proper, the sentence of death was error. The court held: (1) defendant was not in custody at the time of the challenged statements and, thus, was not entitled to Miranda warnings; (2) the circuit court properly denied defendant's motion for a change of venue on the basis of pretrial publicity because voir dire revealed that none of the jurors had specific knowledge about the case or had formed opinions as to his guilt; (3) evidence that defendant was involved in prior incidents in which the decedent suffered similar injuries was admissible to show the presence of intent and the absence of accident; (4) the autopsy photographs were probative of the extent and severity of the decedent's injuries; (5) the instruction on the burden of proof on the involuntary manslaughter charge was proper; and (6) there was no conclusive evidence that the decedent's death was either premeditated, prolonged, or tortuous to warrant imposition of the death penalty under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(7) (1985).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the cause.

 

2 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kirwan v. Welch


No. 68709


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 163; 549 N.E.2d 348; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 167; 139 Ill. Dec. 836



December 21, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding for mandamus or supervisory order.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied; motion for supervisory order denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus or supervisory order directing the justices of the Appellate Court Fifth District (Illinois) to grant petitioner's motion to withdraw as counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of battery following a bench trial and sentenced to 12 months of court supervision. Defendant filed a timely notice of appeal and the circuit court appointed the office of the State Appellate Defender to represent defendant on appeal. Petitioner filed a request for writ of mandamus to withdraw as counsel on the basis that the circuit court did not have authority to appoint petitioner to represent defendant in an appeal form a disposition of supervision. The court denied the requested writ. The court held that the disposition of supervision is not a final judgment and that the State Appellate Defender can represent indigent defendants in such appeals.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for writ.

 

3 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Castaneda v. Illinois Human Rights Com.


Nos. 68119, 68121 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 304; 547 N.E.2d 437; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 158; 138 Ill. Dec. 270; 55 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P40,600



November 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on petition for review of an order of the Human Rights Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for review of an order of appellant Illinois Human Rights Commission for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The Commission's order, issued by a three-member panel, had dismissed with prejudice employee's complaint alleging that his termination by appellee employer had violated his civil rights.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, employee and Commission contended that an order by a three-member panel of the Commission was a final order reviewable by the appellate court. The court found, however, that to allow judicial review of three-member panel decisions of the Commission without first requiring that an aggrieved party file an application for rehearing by the entire Commission, and that the Commission deny that application, would thwart the legislative intent both to adopt the common law exhaustion of remedies doctrine in the Administrative Review Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 3-101 (1987), and to vest the Commission with the authority to decide all matters regarding civil rights violations under the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 7-101 et seq. (1987). The court held, therefore, that an application for rehearing was required pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 8-107(F) (1987), before a party aggrieved by a Commission decision could obtain judicial review. The court declined to give the judgment only prospective application because employee's and Commission's claim that employee had not had a fair opportunity to argue the merits of his case was absurd.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

4 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cooper


No. 68196


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 347; 547 N.E.2d 449; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 157; 138 Ill. Dec. 282



November 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. John C. Layng, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the appellate court (Illinois), which reversed and remanded the trial court's revocation of his conditional release and recommitment to prison under the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 105-1.01 et seq. (1979). The appellate court held that defendant did not have notice of a hearing and was denied procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to be a sexually dangerous person. The trial court granted a conditional release to defendant, who moved to Colorado where he was directed to live near his brother. After two years, defendant's counsel filed a petition seeking defendant's discharge. Three days later, defendant was charged in Colorado with committing a sexual assault. The state filed a motion to revoke the conditional release. The trial court ordered a public defender to notify defendant of a hearing on the motion, which defendant failed to attend. The trial court revoked the release and recommitted defendant to prison. The appellate court entered an order reversing the revocation. The court affirmed the order because there was no evidence that defendant was notified of the revocation hearing as required by § 9 of the Act and § 5-6-4 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-4 (1979). Thus defendant's due process rights were denied. The court also held that: (1) the trial court had jurisdiction and authority under the Act to grant a revocation order based on defendant's offense in Colorado; (2) defendant waived his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order reversing and remanding the trial court's revocation of defendant's conditional release and recommitment to prison under the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act.

 

5 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lake Forest Chateau, Inc. v. Lake Forest


Nos. 68382, 68450 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 129; 549 N.E.2d 336; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 156; 139 Ill. Dec. 824



November 22, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Charles F. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) that reversed the trial court's grant of judgment on the pleadings to the city in appellee developer's action for a declaration that certain increased building permit fees did not apply to the developer's project.


OVERVIEW: The developer argued that the increased fees were enacted because the developer had prevailed in previous litigation against the city concerning the project. The court disagreed and reversed the decision of the appellate court. The court noted that the purpose of charges such as building permit fees were to help defray the cost the city had for providing services to the developer and that it was not uncommon for the city to raise those fees when the cost of providing services rose. Therefore, absent some proof on the part of the developer that the city's action in increasing building permit fees and other construction costs was improper, the developer had no right to lower fees. The court found that, despite the seemingly purposeful timing of the fee increase, there was nothing in the record to show that the city used the higher fees to discriminate against or defraud the developer. The court held that there was no proof of a causal connection between the higher fees and the improper denial of developer's request for rezoning, or the judgment rendered against the city in that case. Therefore, the court saw no reason to declare that the city's higher fees were improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

6 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wade


No. 67028


Supreme Court of Illinois


131 Ill. 2d 370; 546 N.E.2d 553; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 147; 137 Ill. Dec. 608



October 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The stated filed a petition for leave to challenge the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for armed violence and vacated his sentence, holding that intimidation could not serve as the predicate felony for the offense of armed violence.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of armed violence, predicated on the felony of intimidation, and attempted armed robbery. The trial judge entered judgment on the more serious charge, armed violence, and sentenced defendant to seven years' imprisonment. The appellate court reversed the conviction, holding that intimidation could not have served as the predicate felony for armed violence because the existence of different penalties for offenses based on the same conduct resulted in an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentencing scheme. The state petitioned for leave to appeal pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 315(a) (107 Ill. 2d R. 315(a). The court reversed the appellate court's judgment. Intimidation was not a less serious offense than attempted robbery, nor was the commission of intimidation while armed a less serious offense than attempted armed robbery. Thus, defendant's argument that identically classified offenses may not be enhanced by the same circumstances to offenses of different classifications lacked merit. Having failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality, the court declined to interfere with the sentencing classifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment reversing defendant's conviction and sentence, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

7 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ferguson


Nos. 67652, 67674, 67761


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 86; 547 N.E.2d 429; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 145; 138 Ill. Dec. 262



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 67652. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. William R. Penn, Judge, presiding.

No. 67674. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jasper County, the Hon. Richard Brummer, Judge, presiding.

No. 67761. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County, the Hon. C. Howard Wampler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 67652. -- Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded. No. 67674. -- Judgment affirmed. No. 67761. -- Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants had been convicted of committing a felony against a person under the age of 12. They appealed the affirmance of their respective enhanced sentences by the Appellate Court for the Third District and Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) contending that in cases in which the age of the victim was an element of the offense, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 38, par. 1005-5-3.2(b)(3)(i) constituted an impermissible double enhancement.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue of these consolidated appeals was whether a victim's age may be considered as an aggravating factor under § 1005-5-3.2(b)(3)(i) where the victim's age was also an element of the offense for which the defendant's were being sentenced. The court held that it could not, and affirmed in part and reversed in part. In reviewing the scope of § 1005-5-3.2(b)(3)(i) the court found it to be ambiguous. The legislature, by establishing specific offenses in cases where the victim was under 13 years of age, had already made the youth of the victim an element of the offense. The court ruled that the application of the rule of lenity was appropriate and held that the age of the victim should not be considered for the imposition of an additional penalty, where the penalty for the underlying offense had already been enhanced based on the age of the victim. The court determined that each case should be remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendants convictions, but reversed as to their enhanced sentences, and remanded for resentencing.

 

8 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Holman


No. 63771


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 128; 547 N.E.2d 124; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 135; 138 Ill. Dec. 155



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Robert R. Buchar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of felony murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(3), intentional murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(1), armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 38, para. 33A--2, and home invasion, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 38, para. 12--11(a)(1). After resentencing, defendant was found to be eligible for the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's convictions because it determined that it was not necessary to remand the case for a hearing in light of Batson regarding whether blacks had been improperly excluded from the jury because defendant had been convicted originally two years before Batson was decided. The court determined that the sentencing judge did not err in refusing to excuse three venireperson for cause because the determination of whether or not to allow a challenge for cause was within the sound discretion of the trial judge. The court found that even if evidence of a juvenile delinquency adjudication was improperly admitted, its admission was harmless because the state had also established that defendant had two prior felony convictions. The court found that the prosecutor's comments about the victim of a 1966 incident were invited because defense counsel first made a comment about the victim in his closing statement. The court determined that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because counsel's strategic decisions were entitled to deference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

9 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Terrell


No. 64113


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 178; 547 N.E.2d 145; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 142; 138 Ill. Dec. 176



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1989.
Writ of certiorari denied Terrell v. Illinois, 493 U.S. 959, 495 U.S. 959, 110 S. Ct. 2567, 109 L. Ed. 2d 749, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 2745 (1990)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Fred Suria, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; sentences vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of murder and aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant then filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant elected sentencing by the trial court and not by a jury and at sentencing the trial court imposed a death sentence. Defendant challenged both his conviction and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court's conclusion that defendant's confession was voluntary was not against the weight of the evidence and the totality of the circumstances showed that the statements were voluntary. The court next held that the State's failure to call certain witnesses at the suppression hearing was not plain error. The court also held that evidence showed, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant acted with the mental state necessary to sustain a murder conviction. The court determined that the criminal sexual assault statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13 (1985), and the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14 (1985), did not violate due process. The court held that it was error for the trial court to consider the victim impact statement in this case. The court decided that the extensive statement admitted and the trial court's statement that it expressly considered the victim impact statement in sentencing defendant to death established that the court could not have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that the error did not contribute to the trial court's decision to impose the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and vacated the sentences imposed and remanded the case back to the trial court for resentencing in front of a different trial court judge.

 

10 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kokoraleis


No. 65229


Supreme Court of Illinois


132 Ill. 2d 235; 547 N.E.2d 202; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 139; 138 Ill. Dec. 233



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his murder conviction and the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois). Defendant claimed he was denied his constitutional right of confrontation under U.S. Const. amends. VI, XIV, and that the Illinois death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1981), was invalid under U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder and the death sentence imposed. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. The court held that the jury properly considered evidence of two unrelated murders as relevant to the issues of intent, design, and knowledge, because there were substantial similarities among the three crimes. The court ruled that the state properly elicited from the defendant information that he had acknowledged to authorities his participation in 16 different murders before the time he said he was beaten because such testimony tended to cast doubt on defendant's claim that his statements were coerced. The court held that defendant was not denied his right to confrontation when the state introduced testimony that a codefendant had implicated defendant because no objection was raised by defendant and such was consistent with the theory of defense. The court ruled that the jury's determination of the felony murder circumstance did not undermine the reliability of the eligibility determination. The court held that the Illinois death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1981), was not invalid under U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Illinois death penalty statute was not invalid as cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments. The court affirmed defendants conviction for murder and the death penalty imposed, and set a date for execution.

 

11 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Eyler


No. 65371


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 173; 549 N.E.2d 268; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 149; 139 Ill. Dec. 756



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Urso, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was entered after a jury trial, that convicted defendant of murder, kidnapping, aggravated kidnapping, unlawful restraint, and concealment of a homicidal death, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9 -- 1(a)(1), 10 -- 1(a)(3), 10 -- 2(a)(3), 10 -- 3(a)(9), and 9 -- 3.1(a), and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's victim was a young male prostitute. Defendant dismembered the boy, placed his body parts in garbage bags, and put the bags in a dumpster. The court found sufficient evidence to prove defendant guilty of murder, including (1) that defendant was often seen at his apartment with young males, (2) the physical evidence, (3) defendant's fingerprints on the garbage bags, and (4) the testimony of witnesses. The court held that a jury could find defendant guilty of aggravated kidnapping because (1) the boy's confinement was not incidental to the murder, (2) the boy was induced to go from one place to another by deceit or enticement, and (3) the boy was confined against his will because his wrists were bound. The court also held that defendant was not entitled to a Franks hearing and that the search warrant was supported by probable cause. The circuit court did not abuse its discretion in allowing expert testimony based on the supergluing technique of lifting fingerprints and expert testimony on electrophoretic testing of dried bloodstains was admissible. There were no mitigating factors and the imposition of the death penalty by the circuit court was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of the circuit court and the imposition of the death penalty.

 

12 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barrow


No. 65070


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 226; 549 N.E.2d 240; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 133; 139 Ill. Dec. 728



October 25, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1990.
Writ of certiorari denied Barrow v. Illinois, 497 U.S. 1011, 110 S. Ct. 3257, 111 L. Ed. 2d 767, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 3403, 58 U.S.L.W. 3818 (1990)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Barrow, 195 Ill. 2d 506, 749 N.E.2d 892, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 8, 255 Ill. Dec. 410 (2001)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by United States ex rel. Barrow v. Walls, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8072 (N.D. Ill., May 12, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Barrow, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1790 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County, the Hon. Alexander T. Bower, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois) of murder, armed robbery, residential burglary, and burglary. The jury found that there existed one of the aggravating factors and that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a sentence of death. The trial court sentenced defendant to death and consecutive terms of imprisonment. Defendant's sentence of death was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stalked and murdered an 86-year-old man and burglarized his home. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence several pieces of mail that defendant, while in custody in Maryland, sent to his brother, that tape recorded conversations of defendant with an informer should have been suppressed, and that testimony in the aggravation hearing that defendant was seen with a box containing "white powder" in his possession, apparently to suggest possession of drugs, was unreliable as evidence. The court affirmed. Whatever probative value the exhibits might have had was clearly outweighed by their prejudicial impact, and their admission was improper. However, given the fully convincing evidence of guilt, defendant was not denied a fair trial by the admission of the exhibits. Because the electronic eavesdropping was conducted legally outside of Illinois, the recording of defendant's statements was admissible. Given the strong evidence in aggravation and the slight mitigation, the isolated testimony about the purported drug possession did not so prejudice defendant as to deny a fair sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, armed robbery, residential burglary, and burglary, and his death sentence.

 

13 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. R.G.


Nos. 66929, 66999, 67184 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


131 Ill. 2d 328; 546 N.E.2d 533; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 140; 137 Ill. Dec. 588



October 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Margaret O. Coffin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois challenged the decisions of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that the Juvenile Court Act relating to Minors Requiring Authoritative Intervention, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 803-1 et seq. (1987), was unconstitutional pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and dismissed appellant's petitions, which asked the trial court to adjudge two minors as wards of the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant State of Illinois filed several petitions under the Juvenile Court Act relating to Minors Requiring Authoritative Intervention (MRAI), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 803-1 et seq. (1987), which sought declarations that two minors were wards of the trial court. The trial court held that the MRAI was unconstitutional, and the court reversed after holding that the MRAI did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The court overruled In re J.M., 170 Ill. App. 3d 552 (1988) to the extent that it held that the "immediate danger" phrase modified MRAI, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 803-3(1)(a) (1987). The MRAI did not violate substantive due process because appellant had a compelling interest to intercede on the behalf of minors who were absent from home without parental consent and was narrowly tailored to achieve appellant's purposes. The court also held that the MRAI did not violate procedural due process and was not void for vagueness. Finally, the MRAI survived strict scrutiny and did not violate equal protection because parents under the MRAI could be treated differently because they were not similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court and held that the Juvenile Court Act relating to Minors Requiring Authoritative Intervention (MRAI) did not violate the substantive due process, procedural due process, and equal protection clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The court also overruled In re J.M to the extent that it held that the "immediate danger" phrase modified the MRAI.

 

14 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Triple A Servs. v. Rice


Nos. 67723, 67748 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


131 Ill. 2d 217; 545 N.E.2d 706; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 115; 137 Ill. Dec. 53



September 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Charles Freeman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city officials challenged the judgment from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which held in favor of appellant vendors and found a city ordinance invalid as violative of due process and equal protection principles.


OVERVIEW: A city ordinance prohibited vendors from a section of the city. The city officials sought review after the appellate court found the ordinance overbroad and not reasonably related to a legitimate governmental purpose. The court reversed the judgment and found that the ordinance was rationally related to legitimate governmental objectives that enhanced professional appearance and ambience of the district. Unless an enactment impinged on a fundamental personal right or was drawn upon an inherently suspect classification, it was presumptively valid and survived constitutional scrutiny. The city had the power to regulate or prohibit the use of its streets for private gain. Chicago was a home rule unit of local government under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6 and could perform any home rule function concurrently with the state to the extent that the general assembly did not limit concurrent exercise. The court held that it was only the invidious discrimination, the wholly arbitrary act, which could not stand consistently with the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the vendors that found the city ordinance violative of due process and equal protection principles. The court held that city officials had the power to regulate and that the ordinance was a rational means of obtaining the city's legitimate objectives.

 

15 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rogers


No. 67703


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 1; 549 N.E.2d 226; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 117; 139 Ill. Dec. 714



September 27, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with child abduction in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10 -- 5(b)(10) (1987). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declared the statute unconstitutional because it relieved the state of its burden of proof as to one of the elements of the offense. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The testimony showed that defendant approached a game room and asked two boys if they would have helped him unload some newspapers that were in a nearby alley. The boys agreed and went with defendant in his car to the alley. During the ride the defendant offered to pay them each $ 5.00 for their help. While waiting, defendant told the boys that he was going to move their seat back. In his attempt to do so, his hand touched one of the boy's private parts. The boy pushed the defendant's hand away. Defendant then claimed that he wanted to fix the seatbelt and he briefly placed his elbow on the same boy's groin area. Defendant then said that he would have paid them $ 5.00 if they would let him suck them. The two boys left the car and ran across the street to a policeman. The policeman had been watching the truck. The trial court found that the statute was unconstitutional and the state appealed. The court reversed the trial court and held that defendant did not have standing to challenge the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court that found the statute unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings.

 

16 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kidd


No. 62476


Supreme Court of Illinois


129 Ill. 2d 432; 544 N.E.2d 704; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 103; 136 Ill. Dec. 18



September 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state constitution required direct review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which imposed the death sentence upon defendant after he pleaded guilty to armed robbery, aggravated arson, four counts of concealment of homicidal deaths, and nine counts of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to armed robbery, aggravated arson, concealment of homicidal deaths, and murder. Three days later, defendant made a motion to withdraw his guilty pleas, and the court denied the motion. After the death penalty was imposed, the court on direct review vacated the judgment and remanded the case. The court found that although defendant was informed that the death penalty was the maximum sentence, the trial court did not properly admonish defendant of the minimum sentence prescribed by law as required by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402. Nowhere in the record did the trial court inform defendant, before accepting his pleas, that the trial court had to sentence him, at a minimum, to mandatory natural life imprisonment. The court held, therefore, that the defendant did not make a knowing and intelligent decision to plead guilty. The court further held that because the trial court did not comply with the requirements of Rule 402, the denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his pleas was an abuse of discretion. The court held that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel was violated by a pretrial interrogation, which garnered evidence about a prior crime.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the trial court's judgment that imposed the death sentence upon defendant after he pleaded guilty to armed robbery, aggravated arson, four counts of concealment of homicidal deaths, and nine counts of murder.

 

17 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boclair


No. 63917


Supreme Court of Illinois


129 Ill. 2d 458; 544 N.E.2d 715; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 105; 136 Ill. Dec. 29



September 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County, the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder of a fellow inmate and conspiracy by a jury in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois). The trial court, at a separate sentencing hearing, found that the necessary aggravating factors existed and that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death penalty, and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him to death. The court affirmed the convictions but vacated the sentence and remanded. The trial court erred in its finding as to defendant's mental state at the time of the commission of the offense. Under the trial court's standard any prisoner who suffered from a paranoid personality disorder would be unable to plead or prove an extreme mental or emotional disturbance, because in the trial judge's opinion all inmates who had been before him suffered from a paranoid personality disorder. The trial court's statement demonstrated a prejudice against incarcerated defendants, rather than a reasoned and informed judgment based upon the evidence contained in the record. The trial court's belief was at odds with the unrebutted expert evidence that not all prisoners had paranoid personality disorders. Nevertheless, the trial court relied upon its irrelevant and unsupported assertion to deny defendant's motion for a new sentence and affirmed the death sentence. The trial judge's comparison was not an appropriate consideration nor did it insure rationality, consistency, and evenhandedness in the imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions but vacated the death sentence and remanded the cause to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.

 

18 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Broeckl v. Chicago Park Dist.


No. 67466


Supreme Court of Illinois


131 Ill. 2d 79; 544 N.E.2d 792; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 99; 136 Ill. Dec. 106



September 20, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, nonresidents of the city, and defendant park district appealed from the order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the trial court's holding that the park district was permitted to generate a profit by charging fees that exceeded its costs. The appellate court reversed the trial court's holding that the park district's practice of imposing higher mooring fees upon nonresidents was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The nonresidents filed a class action challenging the park district's practice of charging mooring fees that exceeded the operation costs of its harbors and charging higher mooring fees to nonresidents. The trial court held that the park district was permitted to make a profit but that charging nonresidents higher fees pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 333.23n(g) (1987) was unconstitutional. The appellate court upheld the trial court's holding that the park district had a right to make a profit but reversed its determination that § 333.23n(g) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the language of § 333.23n(g) did not limit the amount of fees that the park district was permitted to charge and that the language of § 333.23r(l) indicated that the park district was to operate its harbors at a profit. The court found that the distinction between residents and nonresidents in § 333.23(n)(g) did not violate equal protection because it reflected a reasonable approach to equitably distributing the costs of providing harbor facilities to residents who already supported the facilities through payment of taxes, and nonresidents, who did not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision that the park district's practice of charging mooring fees in excess of the expenses and costs actually incurred was permissible. The court also affirmed the appellate court's conclusion that the park district's imposition of a surcharge upon nonresidents for mooring fees was constitutional.

People v. Pine


Nos. 67436, 67440, 67455, 67468, 67475, 67476 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


129 Ill. 2d 88; 542 N.E.2d 711; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 94; 134 Ill. Dec. 365



July 19, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 67436. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. David G. Bernthal, Judge, presiding.

No. 67440. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County, the Hon. David Sauer, Judge, presiding.

No. 67455. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. William G. Schwartz, Judge, presiding.

No. 67468. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. George Ray, Judge, presiding.

No. 67475. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Edgar County, the Hon. H. Dean Andrews, Judge, presiding.

No. 67476. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. Edward C. Ferguson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant secretary of state challenged numerous appellate court decisions (Illinois), which denied the secretary standing to challenge trial courts' decisions to issue judicial driving permits.


OVERVIEW: This case involved several consolidated actions wherein the trial court issued judicial driving permits (JDP) to drivers whose licenses had been summarily suspended for driving under the influence of alcohol. The appellate court held that appellant secretary of state (secretary) lacked standing to challenge the decisions and dismissed the appeals. On review, appellee bar association argued that the secretary did not have standing to appeal a JDP order because his role in that proceeding was merely ministerial and administrative. However, the court found that the secretary's responsibility and interest in the JDP process and his broad authority in the Illinois Vehicle Code conferred on the secretary standing to appeal the order. Furthermore, the secretary demonstrated that his interest was to insure that the court strictly adhered to its statutory authority in granting JDPs. Therefore, the court reversed the appellate court decisions and remanded the cases with directions to proceed in accordance with the opinion.


OUTCOME: Appellate courts' decisions that denied appellant secretary of state (secretary) standing in judicial driving permit cases were reversed. Secretary had standing because he had an inherent interest in the application of the Illinois Vehicle Code.

 

21 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bastien


No. 67393


Supreme Court of Illinois


129 Ill. 2d 64; 541 N.E.2d 670; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 91; 133 Ill. Dec. 459



June 19, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for a supervisory order.



DISPOSITION: Supervisory order denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state filed a motion for a supervisory order, to which respondents, defendant and trial court judge, objected. Defendant had been charged with aggravated criminal sexual assault and the state filed in the Circuit Court of the 20th Judicial Circuit, Illinois, a motion to record minor victim's testimony on videotape pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 106A - 2 (1987). The circuit court declared the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state sought to record minor victim's testimony on videotape pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 106A - 2 (1987) to present at defendant's trial. The circuit court denied the motion and declared the statute unconstitutional. The court held that the provision was unconstitutional and denied the state's motion for a supervisory order. Under the statute, the videotaped testimony was admissible only if the witness was available to testify at trial; defendant was not permitted to cross-examine the witness during the videotaping, but must be permitted to do so at the trial; and during the videotaping, the witness and defendant were physically present in the same room and could see and hear each other. Such testimony was an out-of-court statement offered to prove the truth of the matter asserted and as such was not have been admissible under the state or federal rules of evidence. The statute, by prohibiting contemporaneous cross-examination, unnecessarily and impermissibly infringed on an accused's right of confrontation. The challenged statute frustrated the truth-seeking function of the confrontation clause because too much time would pass between the videotaping and trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state's motion for supervisory order and held that the challenged provision was unconstitutional.

People v. Harris

Supreme Court of Illinois

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Death sentence vacated; convictions and nondeath sentences conditionally vacated subject to reinstatement; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) jury found defendant guilty of murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(1) (1981), attempted murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8--4 (1981), aggravated battery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12--4(a) (1981), and attempted armed robbery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8--4 (1981). He appealed his convictions and sentences including death under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--(b)(6) (1983).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found statutory aggravating factors and no mitigating circumstances. The court held (1) the appearance a physician who treated a victim would not have changed the trial's outcome, and the victim's inconsistencies were not so severe as to undermine confidence in the outcome of the trial, (2) it could not conclude that counsel's performance failed to meet reasonable professional standards, and even if it so concluded, any defects in counsel's performance were not so severe as to demonstrate a reasonable probability of a different result absent the defects, (3) the prosecutor's closing arguments were not so prejudicial as to deprive defendant of a fair trial, (4) it could not say that an irrelevant 1969 killing and unreliable testimony concerning it were excluded from consideration as they should have been, (5) the state waived its argument that defendant's objection to its exercise of peremptory challenges was untimely, (6) the trial court should not have gone beyond the record to determine the race of two disputed venirepersons, and (7) the trial court must make specific findings of fact and conclusions of law for each strike complained of after a Batson hearing.

People v. Bryant


No. 66620


Supreme Court of Illinois


128 Ill. 2d 448; 539 N.E.2d 1221; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 76; 132 Ill. Dec. 415



May 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. William Cousins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Subsequent to a bench trial, defendant was convicted by the circuit court of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, a Class 2 felony, and sentenced to 3 1/2 years in prison. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) vacated defendant's conviction on the ground that § 4-103(b) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(b), was unconstitutional, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the circuit court of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, and he appealed. The appellate court vacated the conviction, holding that § 4-103(b) of the Illinois Vehicle Code violated the due process and proportionate penalty clauses of the Illinois Constitution. The State appealed. The court found that § 4-103(b) was constitutional, reversed the appellate court, and reinstated the conviction. The court held that the appellate court erred in looking beyond the plain meaning of § 4-103(b) and in concluding that the legislature intended to deter only organized motor vehicle thieves because a reading of the plain language made it clear that the legislature intended to prohibit all persons, not just organized motor vehicle thieves, from possessing stolen motor vehicles. Therefore, the appellate court erred in determining that possessors of stolen motor vehicles were punished more severely than organized motor vehicle thieves. The court also held that defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed because the public defender was entitled to rely on defendant's assurances, rather than the police report, in planning her trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-105(a)(5). Potts v. Illinois Dep't of Registration & Educ.


No. 66739


Supreme Court of Illinois


128 Ill. 2d 322; 538 N.E.2d 1140; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 58; 131 Ill. Dec. 584



April 20, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Illinois Department of Registration and Education (department) challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which found that the Medical Practice Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4400 -- 1 et seq. (1987), which provided for the licensure of doctors of medicine, unconstitutionally deprived appellee naprapath of a property right in the practice of the profession without due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The naprapath filed an application with the department for a license to practice medicine without drugs or operative surgery. The department informed the naprapath that her application had been denied as a matter of law because the licensure of naprapaths was not considered under existing law. The court found that the appellate issues were: (1) whether the Medical Practice Act of 1987 (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4400 -- 1 et seq. (1987), deprived naprapaths of their property right in the practice of naprapathy without due process of law; (2) whether the act violated federal and state equal protection guarantees; and (3) whether the act abridges a patient's right to choose a mode of treatment. The court answered each issue against the naprapath and reversed the lower court. The right to pursue a profession was not a fundamental right for due process purposes and legislation infringing upon that right need only be examined under the rational basis test. The act bore a rational relationship to a proper legislative purpose. The state had a legitimate interest in regulating medical professionals, through licensure, in order to protect the public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, finding that it had erroneously rule in favor of the naprapaths. The Medical Practice Act of 1987 was not unconstitutional.

 

31 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mahaffey


Nos. 61821, 61822


Supreme Court of Illinois


128 Ill. 2d 388; 539 N.E.2d 1172; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 64; 132 Ill. Dec. 366



April 20, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas A. Hett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Co-defendants that were tried together were convicted by a jury of murder, attempted murder, home invasion, rape, armed robbery, residential burglary, aggravated battery and theft. One defendant was found not guilty of deviate sexual assault. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted one defendant's motion for a directed verdict on the deviate sexual assault charge. Both defendants were sentenced to death, and appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two co-defendants were tried together and were found guilty of many crimes that included murder, attempted murder, and home invasion. The jury found that defendants were eligible for the death penalty, and found there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty. Both defendants appealed and raised several issues. One defendant raised the fact that his non-testifying co-defendant's statement was admitted against him. The judge instructed the jury not to consider the confession as to the testifying co-defendant and only to use it against the non-testifying co-defendant. The court held that the instruction was not sufficient. The court reasoned that because one co-defendant testified, the other co-defendant was able to cross-examine him regarding the part that coercion may have played in obtaining his confession. Because the one co-defendant did not testify, the testifying co-defendant's claim of coercion was undercut by his inability to confront the non-testifying co-defendant regarding the accusations contained in his statement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed one defendant's convictions and remanded the case for a new trial. The court affirmed the other defendant's convictions and his sentence to death, and ordered the date on which the sentence of death should have been carried out.

People v. Jihan


No. 66570


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 379; 537 N.E.2d 751; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 48; 130 Ill. Dec. 422



March 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Bill F. Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction of practicing midwifery without a license in violation of the Illinois Medical Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, paras. 4460, 4464 (1985, repealed 1987). The appellate court held that the Act was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define the terms "practice" and "midwifery."


OVERVIEW: Defendant assisted with the delivery of a baby as a midwife at the parents' request. The baby died shortly after its birth. The state charged defendant with involuntary manslaughter, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-3 (1985), and practicing midwifery without a license under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, paras. 4460 and 4464 (1985, Repealed 1987). The trial court dismissed the manslaughter charge and convicted defendant of practicing midwifery without a license and the appellate court reversed defendant's conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, finding that the statute was vague in that it did not define the terms "practice" and "midwifery." The court held that without the definitions of those terms, the statute did not provide a sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct so that a person of ordinary intelligence had a reasonable opportunity to know what was prohibited. Since it was unclear whether unlicensed persons were prohibited from assisting with births or from delivering babies, the court held that it violated the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for practicing midwifery without a license.

 

33 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Orenic v. Illinois State Labor Relations Bd.


No. 66984


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 453; 537 N.E.2d 784; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 51; 130 Ill. Dec. 455



March 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for mandamus or prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, four chief judges, brought an original action for a writ of prohibition or mandamus against respondent, a state labor relations board (the Board), concerning labor law issues. Three Illinois counties and two labor organizations intervened as respondents.


OVERVIEW: The question for the court was whether given their statutory role in funding the circuit courts, counties were to be considered joint employers of those courts' nonjudicial employees for purposes of collective bargaining. The four chief judges contended that the Board lacked jurisdiction over the counties said to be joint employers of court employees in four pending actions over which they presided. The court concluded that the Board could not constitutionally apply a test of joint-employer status so as to result in classifying counties as joint employers with chief judges concerning court employees. The conclusion relied on traditional labor law principles with the scheme of the Illinois Constitution's unified court system and separation of powers and with the nature of public-sector employment. The state, not a county, was the sole employer of all court employees. Any conflict between traditional labor law principles and constitutional principles were resolved in favor of the latter. Treating county boards as joint employers with chief judges in respect of the nonjudicial employees of the courts unduly trenched on the separate and equal status of the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of prohibition.

 

34 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. DeJesus


No. 67641


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 486; 537 N.E.2d 800; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 50; 130 Ill. Dec. 471



March 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. William D. Block, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which sentenced her under the Unified Code of Corrections and held that § 2 -- 7(6)(c) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702 -- 7(6)(a) (1987 Supp.) (now Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805 -- 4(6)(a) (1987)), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile, was tried as an adult for first-degree murder and armed robbery under the "automatic transfer" provisions of the Juvenile Court Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805 -- 4(6)(a) (1987). Defendant was acquitted of murder but convicted of robbery. Thus, the Act required that further proceedings be conducted under the Act, not the Unified Code of Corrections (Code). The state filed a motion to permit prosecution under the criminal laws. A juvenile judge ruled that further proceedings would be under the Act. The matter was transferred for "disposition" to a trial court judge, who sentenced defendant pursuant to the Code, holding that a portion of the Act was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court vacated and remanded, finding that the trial court's comments indicated that it was aware of the prior ruling and either chose to ignore its breadth or dispute jurisdiction. Also, the state's conduct evidenced "judge shopping." The prior ruling was appealable, as it constituted a pronouncement, based upon the plain language of the statute, that the criminal prosecution had terminated. Therefore, the trial court should have declined to rule on the state's motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment that sentenced defendant, a juvenile, under the Uniform Corrections Code was vacated and remanded. The court held that the trial court should have declined to act on the state's motions where a juvenile judge had already ruled on the state's motion to sentence defendant under the criminal laws. The juvenile judge had jurisdiction, and the order was appealable where it terminated the criminal prosecution prior to final judgment.

 

35 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Phillips


No. 64506


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 499; 538 N.E.2d 500; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 40; 131 Ill. Dec. 125



March 29, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Donald Lowery, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), a jury convicted defendant of murder and felony murder in the course of aggravated kidnapping. The circuit court imposed the death penalty and stayed the sentence pending direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murder and felony murder in the course of aggravated kidnapping and sentenced to death. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict because: (1) the testimony of defendant's cellmate asserted facts not known by the general public which, when linked together, supported an inference that the witness' source of knowledge was defendant; (2) the similarities between a prior abduction and the instant abduction were sufficient to warrant the admission of the testimony of the prior abduction; and (3) the prosecutor's statements during closing arguments were properly objected to with adequate instruction or did not cross the boundary of propriety requiring reversal. The court declined to vacate the sentence because the trial court properly considered defendant's emotional disturbance as a mitigating factor, and there was nothing in the record to rebut the presumption that the trial court considered only relevant and competent evidence in sentencing defendant to death. Also, the imposition of the death penalty was not under an impermissible double enhancement.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's implementation of the death penalty as defendant's sentence was affirmed.

Supreme Court of Illinois

Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Flores, 153 Ill. 2d 264, 606 N.E.2d 1078, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 185, 180 Ill. Dec. 1 (1992)
Related proceeding at Gomez v. Ahitow, 29 F.3d 1128, 1994 U.S. App. LEXIS 17292 (7th Cir. Ill., 1994)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James M. Bailey and Hon. Robert V. Boharic, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; dismissed in part. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122 (1985), entered a judgment of conviction, and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of the armed robbery and murder. The court held that (1) defendant failed to demonstrate that his counsel's cross-examination of a state witness denied him effective representation; (2) the denial of defendant's motion on the ground of newly discovered evidence was proper because the alleged information that was not disclosed was not so material that it could not be said that had the evidence been disclosed to the defense, the result of the proceeding would have been different; (3) the trial court's excusing of five jurors for cause after they expressed an unwillingness to impose the death penalty did not deny defendant his right to a jury drawn from a fair cross-section of the community; (4) the jury's conclusion that defendant was subject to the death penalty under Ill. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment as to defendant's murder conviction and death sentence and dismissed as to the conviction for armed robbery. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act.

 

37 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sequoia Books, Inc.


No. 66503


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 271; 537 N.E.2d 302; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 33; 130 Ill. Dec. 235



March 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County, the Hon. Wilson D. Burnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the appellate court affirmed as modified; judgment of the circuit court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment by the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 37-1 and 37-4 (1985) were unconstitutional as applied to stores like appellee adult bookstore that sold sexually explicit material.


OVERVIEW: The state used the statutory provisions to declare the adult bookstore a public nuisance and prevent it from using its building for any purpose for one-year unless they posted a forfeitable bond. The adult bookstore argued that the provisions were unconstitutional under the First Amendment as prior restraints on speech. The court did not reach the question of whether the statute authorized a prior restraint. It found that the restriction regulated elements of both speech and nonspeech because obscene material was not protected speech under the First Amendment. The court did not dispute the state's police power to control the dissemination of obscenity. However, it found that the incidental restriction on protected speech resulting from the statute was far greater than was necessary to achieve the state's substantial interest in suppressing obscenity. The court did not need to reach the question of whether Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 37-1 (1985) was constitutional as applied to obscenity. However, it declared the one-year closure and bond provisions and the ex parte provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 37-1 (1985) to be unconstitutional as applied to obscenity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court as modified, and reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

In re A Minor


No. 66013


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 247; 537 N.E.2d 292; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 32; 130 Ill. Dec. 225; 16 Media L. Rep. 1449



March 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Iroquois County, the Hon. Dwight W. McGrew, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court orders vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Iroquois County (Illinois) on the basis that § 1-20(6) of the Juvenile Court Act, (Act) Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 37, par. 701-20(6) was unconstitutional because it prohibited newspaper from publishing the name of a minor, who had been charged with a crime.


OVERVIEW: During the course of a juvenile proceeding, the trial court ordered that the minor's identity was to be protected and not published. Newspaper had learned of the minor's identity outside of the court proceedings through casual conversations with county officials and had published the minor's name. Thereafter, the trial court ordered that newspaper was banned from the proceedings unless its order prohibiting publication was complied with. On appeal, the state contended that the case was moot, that the order was not appealable and that the prohibition was constitutional. The court held that the case was not moot because newspaper was still subject to the order and thus the issues involved in the trial still existed. Because the substance of the order was injunctive, in that it imposed an interlocutory restraint upon publication, it was reviewable as an interlocutory injunctive order. Finding that the order constituted a prior restraint on newspaper's free speech rights, the court found that the Act was unconstitutional as applied by the order.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the trial court that prohibited newspaper from publishing minor's identity.

 

39 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lindner


No. 66372


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 174; 535 N.E.2d 829; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 25; 129 Ill. Dec. 64



February 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Angelo F. Pistilli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which found in favor of defendant and held unconstitutional Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, paras. 6-204(a)(1), 6-205(b)(2) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty and was convicted of criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Defendant's driver's license was suspended. The trial court held unconstitutional Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, paras. 6-204(a)(1), 6-205(b)(2) (1987), which provided that upon conviction of certain sex offenses, the offender's driver's license was subject to mandatory revocation. The issue on appeal was whether those statutory provisions violated defendant's right to due process of law. The court affirmed the decision and held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-205(a)(3) clearly reflected the legislature's intent that revocation be tied to offenses involving the use of a motor vehicle. Ch. 6-205(b)(2) was wholly inconsistent with that intent. Because a vehicle was not involved in any way in the commission of the offenses for which defendant was convicted, the revocation of his license had no relationship to the public interest in keeping the roads free of drivers that threaten the safety of others and drivers who abused the privilege to drive by doing so illegally.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of defendant because the challenged provision was an unreasonable and arbitrary exercise of the state's police power in violation of the constitutional guarantee of due process. Keeping drivers off the roads who committed offenses not involving vehicles was not a reasonable means of ensuring that the roads were free of drivers who operated vehicles unsafely or illegally.

People v. Jimerson


No. 62845


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 12; 535 N.E.2d 889; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 24; 129 Ill. Dec. 124



February 22, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Will Gierach, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) after he was convicted of the murder of two persons and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death, he appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence, the effectiveness of his counsel, prosecutorial remarks made during his trial, and the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute. The court found that there was sufficient evidence that defendant was a participant in brutal offenses and acted with reckless indifference to human life. The court noted that defendant could not show that there was a reasonable probability that, but for his counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different. A reasonable probability was defined by the court as a probability sufficient to undermine confidence in the outcome. The same analysis was applied to allegedly improper evidence and prosecutorial misconduct. First, the court noted that defendant's counsel failed to object and preserve the issue for review. However, the evidence was not so prejudicial that it could be characterized as plain error. The court acknowledged the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute and found that the crime merited the punishment imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder.

 

42 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Eckhardt


No. 66066


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 146; 535 N.E.2d 847; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 26; 129 Ill. Dec. 82



February 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Daniel Locallo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with various vehicular offenses and, seeking supervision for these offenses, filed a motion to declare Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, pars. 1005-6-1(d) (1985) of the Unified Code of Corrections unconstitutional. Appellant State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that § 1005-6-1(d) violated equal protection guarantees and was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pled guilty to reckless driving pursuant to a plea agreement. About two and one-half years later, defendant was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol, improper lane usage, and driving while license was suspended. Under § 5-6-1(d), the trial court was not authorized to impose supervision where defendant, within the last five years, had pleaded guilty to reckless driving under a plea agreement. The trial court held that the statute violated equal protection guarantees because defendants who had pled guilty to a reckless driving were treated differently than those who entered a blind plea of guilty to reckless driving. On appeal, the court reversed, noting that the equal protection clauses of neither the Federal nor State constitutions prevented the State from treating different classes of people in different ways and that a person who has plea bargained to a charge of reckless driving was in a different position from a person who has entered a blind plea to such charge. The court held that § 5-6-1(d) was rationally related to the state's legitimate goal of promoting highway safety and did not violate equal protection guarantees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded.

Gibellina v. Handley


Nos. 65781, 66010, 66197 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


127 Ill. 2d 122; 535 N.E.2d 858; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 18; 129 Ill. Dec. 93



February 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 65781. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Richard A. Lucas, Judge, presiding.

No. 66010. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Edwin A. Berman, Judge, presiding.

No. 66197. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Richard A. Lucas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant litigants sought review of judgments of the Appellate Courts for the First District and for the Second District (Illinois), which denied their pretrial motions for summary judgment and granted appellee claimants' motions for voluntary dismissal pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2, § 1009(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: The litigants alleged that their summary judgment motions should have been heard in advance of the motions for dismissal and that the court should adopt Fed. R. Civ. P. 41(a), which permitted voluntary dismissal only prior to the filing of an answer or motion by a defendant. The court held that § 1009(a) was legislatively intended to allow the claimants to dismiss their suits without prejudice at any time before the trial began. Although it had concurrent jurisdiction and the authority to promulgate procedural rules, the court refused to get involved in the legislative process and unequivocally alter the statutory protection by adopting the federal rule. The statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it did not confer a benefit or impose a hardship upon an individual at the expense of others who were similarly situated. Frequent abuses of the statute prompted the court to rule that effective as of the date of the opinion and prospectively, the trial court could hear and decide a motion which had been filed prior to a § 1009 motion when that motion, if favorably ruled on by the court, could result in a final disposition of the case.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

44 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Caballero


No. 64252


Supreme Court of Illinois


126 Ill. 2d 248; 533 N.E.2d 1089; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 1; 128 Ill. Dec. 1



January 18, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at People v. Caballero, 152 Ill. 2d 347, 604 N.E.2d 913, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 142, 178 Ill. Dec. 390 (1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was charged along with a co-defendant with the murders of three teenage males. He was found guilty and sentenced to death. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), denied his petition challenging his conviction and sentence under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 122-1 et seq. (1985), without a hearing. The petitioner claimed ineffective assistance of counsel at the trial and sentencing stages.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner claimed that his defense counsel erred by antagonizing the jury in his opening statement, presenting a weak and incoherent closing argument, and failing to "life-qualify" the jury during voir dire. The court held that the standards for determining whether petitioner had received effective assistance of counsel at trial or at the death penalty hearing was whether: (1) his counsel made errors so serious, and his performance was so deficient, that he was not functioning as the "counsel" guaranteed by the Sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution, and (2) those deficiencies so prejudiced the petitioner as to deprive him of a fair trial, a trial whose result was reliable. The court held that the petitioner failed to show that the state's evidence was insufficient or that he was prejudiced by the trial strategy of his counsel. The court concluded, however, that the decision of counsel not to use mitigating witnesses in the sentencing stage just because the witnesses approved of the death penalty in appropriate situations might have been a departure from professional norms, which could not be attributed to a reasonable trial strategy and required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court in part, but reversed and remanded on the argument that counsel was ineffective at the sentencing stage by not using mitigating witnesses. The circuit court was directed to hold a hearing to determine whether there was a reasonable probability that the jury would have concluded that the factors did not warrant death.
