People v. Bainter


Nos. 65362, 65953


Supreme Court of Illinois


126 Ill. 2d 292; 533 N.E.2d 1066; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 7; 127 Ill. Dec. 938



January 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 65362. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. William B. Starnes, Judge, presiding.

No. 65953. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Knox County, the Hon. Daniel J. Roberts, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed. Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The first defendant appealed from the order of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) ruling that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4 (1983) was unconstitutional. The second defendant appealed from the order of Circuit Court of Knox County (Illinois) denying his motion to commute his sentence and ruling that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(f) (1983) was unconstitutional. The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant filed motions under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a), requesting modification of his state sentence to run concurrently with the federal sentence. The motions were denied, and the appellate court ruled that a portion of para. 1005-8-4(a) was unconstitutional. The second defendant filed a motion under para. 1005-8-1(f), seeking to have a state sentence commuted to time served while he was in federal custody. The trial court denied the motion and ruled that para. 1005-8-1(f) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that para. 1005-8-4(a) and para. 1005-8-1(f) were constitutional because they did not infringe upon any judicial authority in violation of the separation of powers doctrine. It was a proper exercise of the legislature's authority to revest a court with jurisdiction over a final order of sentence in special circumstances, and the subsequent imposition of a sentence in another jurisdiction was such a circumstance. The court remanded the second defendant's motion for modification of sentence for consideration because the trial court did not provide an alternative ground for his denial of the motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order that had ruled that the statute permitting defendant to seek modification of sentence was unconstitutional. The court reversed the order of the trial court denying defendant's motion to commute his sentence and remanded the cause for consideration of the motion.

Bank of Aspen v. Fox Cartage, Inc.


No. 65832


Supreme Court of Illinois


126 Ill. 2d 307; 533 N.E.2d 1080; 1989 Ill. LEXIS 6; 127 Ill. Dec. 952



January 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. James F. Quetsch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a second appeal in supplementary proceedings to discover assets under Ill. Code Civ. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1402 (1985), plaintiff, judgment creditor bank, challenged a decision by the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) that the third-party citation respondent, a second bank, had a superior interest in stock that was the subject of the citation to discover assets.


OVERVIEW: A debtor in default to the judgment creditor bank pledged stock as collateral to obtain new loans from the second bank. When the debtor defaulted to it too, the second bank foreclosed on the stock and notified the judgment creditor bank of its plan to sell it. Before it could so, however, the judgment creditor bank served it with a citation to discover assets pursuant to § 2-1402, which contained language prohibiting the second bank from transferring or otherwise disposing of the debtor's property. The appeals court found that the citation to discover assets that was served upon the second bank was a wrongfully issued injunction that deprived the second bank of procedural due process. The court reversed because the citation did not constitute an injunction; it simply informed the citee of the penalties that could occur if it transferred or disposed of property belonging to the debtor. Nor did the record indicate that the second bank was deprived of due process. However, the court affirmed the determinations that the second bank had superior rights to the stock in question because it was secured, because they were not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision that the second bank possessed the superior interest in the stock. The court reversed the appellate court's holding that the citation was, in effect, an injunction that was wrongfully issued and that the second bank was entitled to damages.

48 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kuhn


No. 66308


Supreme Court of Illinois


126 Ill. 2d 202; 533 N.E.2d 909; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 191; 127 Ill. Dec. 827



December 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Thomas E. Callum, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which declared the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-1(d)(3) (1987), unconstitutional under the equal protection clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. Defendant had entered guilty pleas on various driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) charges and asked for court supervision.


OVERVIEW: The statute precluded court supervision as a sentencing alternative for DUI offenders who had, within five years, pled guilty to a charge of reckless driving. Defendant admitted that he was charged with DUI within five years and pled guilty. However, the court found that the record was not clear as to whether or not there was a plea agreement at that time. The state contended that the trial court had to find implicitly that defendant's prior plea of guilty was pursuant to a plea agreement. The court disagreed, as the court did not find any evidence that it could have been inferred that no plea agreement was involved. However, the court vacated the decision on the grounds that it did not have jurisdiction. The court stated that in criminal cases, there was no final judgment without a sentence. Because an appeal required a final judgment, and defendant was not sentenced in the underlying action, the court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order declaring the statute unconstitutional was vacated and defendant's case was remanded. The court had no jurisdiction over the state's appeal.

People ex rel. Daley v. Joyce


Nos. 65487, 65678, 65679 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


126 Ill. 2d 209; 533 N.E.2d 873; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 193; 127 Ill. Dec. 791



December 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petitions for writs of mandamus, prohibition or supervisory order.



DISPOSITION: Writs denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a writ of mandamus, prohibition, or supervisory order requesting to compel respondent judge to adhere to the provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. 1ch. 38, para. 115 - 1(1987) and proceed to conduct jury trials for certain accused persons. The judge had accepted jury waivers submitted by the accused persons who were indicted under the Illinois Controlled Substance Act and denied the jury request by the state.


OVERVIEW: The accused persons argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1ch. 38, para. 115 - 1(1987), which required the state also to waive jury trial in addition to the accused persons charged with a drug-related offense, violated the state's constitutional guarantee of the right to trial by jury. They contended that federal and state constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process were violated, and the statute, as applied to the accused persons, was an ex post facto law. The state countered the arguments, asserting that the right to a jury trial did not encompass the right to waive it. The court held that the statute deprived the accused persons of the full protection guaranteed under Ill. Const. art. I, § 13. The court ruled that the legislature could not deny the accused persons of any part of the constitutionally protected right short of any constitutional amendment to that effect.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state's petition for a writ of mandamus, prohibition, or supervisory order.

 

50 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Odle


No. 63753


Supreme Court of Illinois


128 Ill. 2d 111; 538 N.E.2d 428; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 189; 131 Ill. Dec. 53



December 21, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, the Hon. Donald E. Garrison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence in the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois) for the murders of his parents and siblings. He alleged that mitigating factors precluded the imposition of the death penalty and that the Illinois statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the murder of his parents and three siblings and sentenced to death. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court exercised its sound discretion in refusing to grant defendant a surrebuttal argument because he pointed to no error of law or actual prejudice, and finding no error in its mention of another state's definition of extreme mental or emotional disturbance where it was referenced merely to give the term its plain, ordinary, commonsense meaning. The court agreed that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty where defendant's assertion that he suffered from extreme mental or emotional disturbance was contradicted by his methodical efforts to conceal the crimes and his calm manner with friends after the murders. Defendant's argument that he was motivated by a history of child abuse was inconsistent with the murders of his siblings and his demeanor during the confession was evidence of his lack of remorse. The court declined to reconsider the validity of Illinois' death penalty statute, which provided for adequate comparative review, and narrowing of the group of persons eligible for death.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence for the murders of his parents and siblings was affirmed upon a finding that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty when defendant's methodical and calm manner during and after the murders belied his contention that he suffered from extreme mental or emotional disturbance and his demeanor during the confession was the best evidence of his lack of remorse.

Chicago Tribune Co. v. Downers Grove


No. 65418


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 468; 532 N.E.2d 821; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 178; 126 Ill. Dec. 950; 15 Media L. Rep. 2459



December 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper filed a claim against defendant village in an action that sought injunctive relief. The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed the circuit court that entered summary judgment and declared the ordinance in question unconstitutional. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village passed an ordinance that regulated door-to-door solicitation of both a commercial and noncommercial nature. The ordinance classified solicitation of funds for charitable, religious, and political organizations under the noncommercial solicitation article of the ordinance. Solicitations for the sale of goods, books, magazines, or any other article or thing whatsoever, however, were classified as commercial. The ordinance required all commercial solicitors to pay a fee for a permit and limited the number of permits at any given time to 15. There was also a minimum five-day waiting period while a village official reviewed the permit application. After the police stopped its solicitors, the newspaper filed this action for injunctive relief and to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional. The court affirmed both lower courts and held that although the newspaper was a business, it was also a newspaper and therefore constitutionally protected by the first amendment in its right to sell and circulate its product on the same basis as religious, political, and charitable organizations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower courts judgments that the village ordinance was unconstitutional because it violated free speech and equal protection rights under both the United States and Illinois Constitutions.

National Commercial Banking Corp. v. Harris

Supreme Court of Illinois

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Commissioner of Banks and Trust Companies of the State of Illinois appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared § 3 of the Foreign Banking Office Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, par. 2710 (1985) void and unenforceable on its face for its imposition of the nonreciprocal license fee. The court held that the Act violated federal statutory law and the Constitutions of the United States and Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court held that § 3 of the Foreign Banking Office Act (Act) was unconstitutional as violative of the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution because it conflicted with § 5 of the International Banking Act, 12 U.S.C.S. § 3103. The court agreed with the circuit court's decision that the Foreign Banking Office Act's imposition of the nonreciprocal license fee in § 3 of the Act was void and unenforceable as violative of the supremacy clause. Because the court reached its decision based on preemption, the court did not address other issues presented by the parties.


OUTCOME: Judgment that the nonreciprocal licensing fee was void an unconstitutional was affirmed.

Dineen v. Chicago


No. 64906


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 248; 531 N.E.2d 347; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 156; 126 Ill. Dec. 52



November 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff officers challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the judgment of the trial court striking down defendant city's ordinance requiring officers to take unpaid leaves of absence upon becoming candidates for public office and enjoined its enforcement based on a recently enacted state statute, Ill. Public Act 84 -- 1018.

Officers, who were candidates for office, filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief arguing that Ill. The court further held that officers' new argument introduced a different theory of the case, one that was sharply at odds with their original theory, and therefore was waived for not having been preserved properly.

54 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kluk v. Lang


Nos. 66321, 66323 cons. 66322


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 306; 531 N.E.2d 790; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 157; 126 Ill. Dec. 163



November 21, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an appointed general assembly representative, appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted summary judgment to plaintiff, a candidate for representative in the general assembly, in an action challenging the constitutionality of the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 25-6 (1986 Supp.). Plaintiff resident taxpayer appealed the dismissal of his challenge to the statute for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, resident taxpayer and a candidate for representative in the general assembly, filed consolidated declaratory judgment actions against defendant, an appointed general assembly representative, challenging the constitutionality of the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 25-6 (1986 Supp.), which allowed a political committee to fill a vacancy for the office of general assembly representative. The circuit court dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's claim for lack of standing, but granted plaintiff candidate's motion for summary judgment on the basis of the statute's unconstitutionality. The court reversed the circuit court's order that declared the statute unconstitutional and defendant's appointment invalid. The court held that both plaintiffs had standing because their claim of injury to their voting right constituted an actual controversy. It was also held that the statute's placement of the right to fill legislative vacancies in the hands of a political party was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to private persons because the statute imposed a set of duties on political party committees that arguably conferred indicia of public agency on them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order that granted summary judgment to plaintiff, a candidate for representative in the general assembly, and dismissed, on the basis of standing, plaintiff resident taxpayer's claim in a challenge to the constitutionality of an election statute because although both plaintiffs had standing, the statute did not unconstitutionally delegate the power to fill legislative positions to private persons.

 

55 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zeisler


No. 66301


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 42; 531 N.E.2d 24; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 148; 125 Ill. Dec. 845



October 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McDonough County, the Hon. Charles Wilhelm, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), affirming the trial court's order, which granted defendant's post-conviction petition and vacated his conviction for aggravated arson under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1981) on the ground that the statute had been declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court had not erred by vacating defendant's conviction. Generally, where the state supreme court had declared a statute invalid, it was null and void as of the date of its enactment, and as such, it conferred no rights, imposed no duties, and afforded no protection. It was void ab initio. In this case, the court had declared the aggravated arson statute unconstitutional and, as such, the doctrine of void ab initio was applicable. However, the state could proceed with an action against defendant under the amended arson statute pursuant to § 3-5(a) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3-5(a) (1987), which provided that a prosecution for arson could be commenced at any time. Defendant did not have a claim of double jeopardy because a substantive amendment to an unconstitutional statute could not have retroactive application and as such did not in legal contemplation exist at the time of the offense. Defendant also did not have an ex post facto claim because the amended statute was inapplicable and defendant knew that his conduct was prohibited and that he would be punished for his actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the appellate and trial courts and remanded the cause to the trial court.

 

56 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Federated Distributors, Inc. v. Johnson


No. 66213


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 1; 530 N.E.2d 501; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 149; 125 Ill. Dec. 343



October 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Revenue (department), sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's ruling that granted the department's motion for summary judgment and upheld the constitutionality of the classification and taxation of appellee distributor's beverage as "alcohol and spirits" under the Liquor Control Act of 1934 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 93.9 et seq. (1985).


OVERVIEW: The distributor filed an action challenging the department's ruling that it, as a distributor of a low-alcohol-content beverage, had to pay taxes on that beverage based solely on the method of production of the alcohol it contained. The court found that the distributor's products should be taxed at the same rate as wine and wine coolers, not at the rate that was over eight times higher. The taxation of the distributor's products at the higher rate violated the constitutional guarantees of uniformity under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), because there was no real and substantial difference between the distributor's products and wine coolers. Where the products were virtually identical save for the method of production of their alcoholic content, they could not constitutionally be taxed differently. Therefore, the court held that the distributor's products had to be taxed by the department at the same rate established administratively for wine coolers. To the extent that § 8--1 of the Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 95.03 (1985), did not establish a basis on which to tax such virtually identical products equally, the court declared it unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the appellate court. The court affirmed the finding of unconstitutionality of the higher tax, and reversed as to the appellate court's ruling that held that wine coolers and the distributor's alcoholic beverage had to be taxed at the same rate as wine.

Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Evans v. Briley, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16052 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 8, 2003)

People v. Albanese

Supreme Court of Illinois

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his post-conviction petitions by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois). Defendant had been tried and convicted of separate murders in the two circuit courts. Both post-conviction petitions were consolidated due to the similarity of issues presented for consideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at each trial and at each sentencing hearing, that recent evidentiary discoveries rendered scientific evidence admitted during the trials unreliable, and that the circuit court erred in denying the post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing. OUTCOME: The court affirmed both circuit courts' dismissals of defendant's post-conviction petitions.

 

59 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gacy


No. 64382


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 117; 530 N.E.2d 1340; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 140; 125 Ill. Dec. 770



September 29, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Louis Garippo and Francis J. Mahon, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murdering 33 boys and young men and received the death penalty. His convictions and sentences were affirmed and his writ of certiorari to the Supreme Court of the United States was denied. He appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found no merit in any of defendant's allegations. The court found that the standard for ineffective assistance at a sentencing hearing is the two-prong standard under Strickland, in which the defendant must prove: that his counsel's representation was so deficient that his counsel was not functioning as the "counsel" guaranteed the defendant by the Sixth Amendment; and that this deficient performance so prejudiced the defendant as to deprive him of a fair hearing. The burden of proving incompetence, and of overcoming the presumption that an attorney's decision is the product of "sound trial strategy," rests upon the defendant, not the state. Defendant's trial counsel presented evidence in mitigation during his trial. The court held that defendant did not adequately allege prejudice. The Strickland standard requires a reasonable probability of a different result, not merely a possibility. The court also found that defendant failed to make a substantial showing of a violation of his constitutional rights sufficient for an evidentiary hearing, and that it was not unreasonable for defense counsel to decide not to seek sequestration of the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

People v. Orth


No. 64931


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 326; 530 N.E.2d 210; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 134; 125 Ill. Dec. 182



September 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Henderson County, the Hon. Lewis D. Murphy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court reversed; cause remanded; summary suspension reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Henderson County (Illinois), which granted defendant motorist's request to rescind the summary suspension of his driver's license for driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: The motorist filed a request to rescind the State's summary suspension of his driver's license for driving under the influence of alcohol. The trial court granted the motorist's request. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that a driver who suffered the summary suspension of his license had the burden of proving that the suspension should be rescinded. On balance the court determined that placing the burden of proof upon the suspended motorist did not violate the Due Process Clause of either the federal or state Constitutions. However, the State had the burden of showing the reliability of test results if the motorist first made a prima facie showing that the results were unreliable. The court's holding considerably reduced the risk that placing the initial burden of proof upon all suspended motorists would result in the erroneous deprivation of any one motorist's license.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial and appellate courts were reversed, and the case was remanded with direction that the summary suspension of motorist's driver's license be reinstated.

 

61 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. M.A.


No. 64476


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 135; 529 N.E.2d 492; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 117; 124 Ill. Dec. 511



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a minor, was arrested and charged with unlawful use of weapons on school grounds, contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24 -- 1(a)(12) (1985). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) held that the automatic transfer provision of the Juvenile Court Act under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702 -- 7(6)(a) (1985) was unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the unlawful possession of weapons on school grounds. Pursuant to the automatic transfer provision of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, par. 702 -- 7(6)(a) (1985), defendant's case was transferred to criminal court so that he could have been prosecuted as an adult. Following a hearing, the trial court held that the automatic transfer provision was unconstitutional. The state directly appealed. On appeal, defendant argued that the automatic transfer provision was invalid because it deprived him of due process and equal protection of the laws. The court noted that courts have routinely held that age was not a suspect class for purposes of equal protection analysis, and thus the rational basis standard applied. The court held that even if the classification resulted in some inequality, it was not unconstitutional because it was rational for the legislature to conclude that juveniles that were charged with unlawful use of weapons on school grounds posed the greatest threat to the school environment. The court thus reversed the trial court's decision and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that prosecuting a juvenile as an adult for unlawful use of weapons on school grounds did not deprive the minor of due process or equal protection of the law.

People v. Fierer


No. 65010


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 176; 529 N.E.2d 972; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 127; 124 Ill. Dec. 855



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. Richard E. Eagleton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision by the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's murder conviction against defendant wherein he was found guilty but mentally ill for the murder of his wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for murder after witnesses saw him fatally stab his wife. Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty but mentally ill (GBMI). The conviction was overturned by the appellate court and a new trial was ordered because of erroneous jury instructions on the burden of proof for the GBMI and insanity verdicts. The state filed a petition for leave to appeal. The state contended that defendant waived the issue of error, the instructions were harmless, and the modifications were necessary to avoid constitutional infirmities. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision because the trial judge's modification of the GBMI instruction conflicted with the unambiguous "beyond a reasonable doubt" language of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115 -- 4(j) (1985). The court held that (1) defendant did not waive the issue by failing to raise it in his post-trial motion because the misstated instruction was worthy of review; (2) the modification was not harmless because it probably affected the outcome; and (3) the modification could not be construed to interpret "beyond a reasonable doubt" as meaning "by a preponderance of the evidence."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision granting defendant a new trial based on misstated jury instructions on guilty by mentally ill and insanity verdicts.

 

63 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 65895


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 300; 529 N.E.2d 558; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 123; 124 Ill. Dec. 577



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Shelvin Singer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a ruling of the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) that held the statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114 - 5(c) (1987), that permitted the state to request substitution of the trial judge to have been unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the trial court's ruling that the statute that permitted the state to request the substitution of the trial judge was unconstitutional. The court noted that the trial court declared the statute unconstitutional as a violation of the separation of powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970), and interfered with the judicial powers granted under Ill. Const. art. IV, §§ 7(c), 16. The court reversed and remanded and noted that while all legislation carried a strong presumption of constitutionality, the legislature was not permitted to enact statutes that solely concerned court administration or the day-to-day business of the court. But the legislature was permitted to enact legislation that complemented the authority of the judiciary. The court noted that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, § 114 - 5(a) permitted defendant to request a substitution of the trial judge only after the case had been assigned to a judge pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(b), General Orders. 107 Ill. 2d R. 21(b). Section 114 - 5(c) did nothing more than § 114 - 5(a). The court also held that defendant a right to a fair trial, but did not have a right to the judge of his choice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded because the legislature could enact legislation that complemented the authority of the judiciary.

Thies v. State Bd. of Elections


No. 66389


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 317; 529 N.E.2d 565; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 120; 124 Ill. Dec. 584



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Rita B. Garman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Board of Elections appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which held that statutory amendments found in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 72.2c(2) (1987) related to qualifications of circuit judges were unconstitutional, in a declaratory action brought by plaintiff citizen opposing the amendments.


OVERVIEW: Recent statutory amendments provided that a candidate for a circuit judgeship had to be a resident of a particular county but had to run for the office throughout the entire circuit. The citizen brought an action against the board seeking declaration that the amendments were unconstitutional. The lower court concluded that the state constitution did not permit the creation by the legislature of such a circuit judgeship and it declared that the amendments were unconstitutional. The legislature could not require the additional qualification that a candidate reside in a particular part of the unit which selected the judge and Article VI could not be viewed as a grant of power to add such qualifications.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that statutory amendments requiring circuit judge candidates to reside in a specific area were unconstitutional, in an action brought by a citizen against the board challenging their requirements.

 

65 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Landmarks Preservation Council v. Chicago


No. 66582


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 164; 531 N.E.2d 9; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 122; 125 Ill. Dec. 830



September 22, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, historical preservation associations, brought claims for a declaratory judgment in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to set aside a decision by defendant city through its city council to withdraw landmark status to a building after the owner had obtained landmark status. The trial court dismissed the associations' complaints for failure to state a cause of action and the associations appealed.


OVERVIEW: The historical preservation associations claimed that the city failed to comply with the procedures under the Chicago Landmarks Ordinance, codified at Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code §§ 21-67-73 (1987), when it repealed an ordinance designating a building as a Chicago landmark. The city and city council claimed that the associations did not have standing to complain about the action taken by the city. The court affirmed the trial court's order and held that all but one of the associations did not have standing to bring their claims against the city, as they lacked a sufficient interest in the status of the building as a landmark, but the remaining association had standing under § 468C of the Historic Sites, Buildings, and Antiquities Act, specifically at 16 U.S.C.S. § 468C, because it was authorized to sue to carry out the function established for it by Congress under 16 U.S.C.S. §§ 468-468e. The court further held that it could not review the ordinance-passing decision making by the city council, as the council had been acting in a legislative capacity rather than an administrative capacity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the associations' claims by the trial court, because only one association had standing to bring the historical preservation claims against the city and the one remaining association was claiming that the city council had not exercised the use of the ordinance process appropriately. The court lacked jurisdiction to review the legislative function of the council.

Bilyk v. Chicago Transit Authority


No. 65735


Supreme Court of Illinois


125 Ill. 2d 230; 531 N.E.2d 1; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 128; 125 Ill. Dec. 822



September 22, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Willard J. Lassers, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Chicago Transit Authority, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that an immunity statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 111 2/3, para. 327, was unconstitutional. The section immunized the authority from tort liability for any failure to protect passengers from criminal acts of third parties.


OVERVIEW: Appellee claimant had filed a complaint charging appellant, the Chicago Transit Authority, with negligence and wilful and wanton misconduct. The claimant alleged that, as a result of the authority's driver's inaction, he was severely beaten by the other passengers and suffered permanent injuries. The authority had moved to dismiss the complaint, claiming that the action was barred by Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 111 2/3, par. 327, which absolved the authority of liability in tort for criminal acts of third parties. The circuit court denied the authority's motion and held the statute invalid. The court stated that the authority was created by statute as a municipal corporation for the purpose of owning and operating a public transportation system whose function was to provide transportation to the public at large, rather than to guarantee the safety of every individual passenger and complete uniformity between the immunity given to it and municipal entities whose primary purpose was to protect citizens from crime, was not required. Therefore, the court reversed because it concluded that the statute did not violate the equal protection guarantee or constitute special legislation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed.

People ex rel. Sheppard v. Money


No. 65710


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 265; 529 N.E.2d 542; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 132; 124 Ill. Dec. 561



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John R. Ryan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of appellee father.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought, through the state's attorney's office, an action against the father seeking an order withholding income for child support pursuant to § 20 of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984 (Act). Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2520 (1987). The mother appealed the judgment of the trial court that § 20 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment from the trial court. The court held that the Act provides sufficient procedural safeguards and passes constitutional muster. The court further held that the Act provides for prejudgment and post-judgment notice and opportunity to be heard. The Act provides an efficient and constitutional mechanism for enforcement of child support obligations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with directions.

 

68 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Russell Stewart Oil Co. v. State


No. 63630


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 116; 529 N.E.2d 484; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 114; 124 Ill. Dec. 503



September 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Illinois (state) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion for summary judgment filed by plaintiff oil company on the ground that the amended Retailers' Occupation Tax Act and the Use Tax Act discriminated against interstate commerce in their "purpose and effect," and, therefore, were unconstitutional under the commerce clause.


OVERVIEW: Amendments to both the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 440 et seq. (1985), and the Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.1 et seq. (1985), established a different tax rate for sales of gasohol containing ethanol, which was distilled in Illinois or in a state which offered Illinois reciprocal tax benefits and changed the definition of "gasohol." On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the statutes violated the commerce clause because on their face and in plain effect they discriminated against interstate commerce in favor of local interests. The statutes legislated expressly in terms of state boundaries giving tax preference to gasohol containing Illinois distilled ethanol. The amended definition of "gasohol" was invalid because it discriminated against and unduly burdened interstate commerce in that virtually no in-state ethanol producers were excluded from the tax benefit while a significant portion of out-of-state producers were excluded. The allowance of a tax benefit for gasohol without regard to the raw materials in the ethanol used would have had the same effect of encouraging the use of gasohol without its discriminatory effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the oil company in its action alleging that the amended tax statutes discriminated against interstate commerce in their "purpose and effect," and, therefore, were unconstitutional under the commerce clause.

Mulligan v. Joliet Regional Port Dist.


No. 65317


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 303; 527 N.E.2d 1264; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 113; 123 Ill. Dec. 489



August 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which denied plaintiff's request for declaratory relief. Plaintiff sought to prevent defendant, the Joliet Regional Port District, from acquiring an airport facility without referendum approval as required by an 83 Ill. Laws 1102, an amendment to the district's enabling act. The district appealed the dismissal of its counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: 83 Ill. Laws 1102 amended the district's authority to develop an airport and added a requirement of voter approval. Plaintiff asserted that the amendment took effect on January 5, 1984, prior to the transaction. The trial court found that the amendment did not become effective until July 1, 1984 and that the district had done everything necessary to exercise its authority to acquire, operate and expand the Lewis University airport prior to the effective date. The court affirmed and found that the last legislative act necessary so that the bill could become law took place on November 1, 1983, when the senate voted to accept the governor's recommendations for change. Thus, for the purpose of Ill. Const. of 1970 art. IV, § 10 the bill was "passed" on November 1, 1983. Under § 2 of "An Act in relation to the effective date of laws," Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 1, para. 1202 (1983), therefore, the law became effective on July 1, 1984 and was not applicable to the transaction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the amendment did not become effective until July 1, 1984 and that the district had done everything necessary to exercise its authority.

People v. Britz


No. 62677


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 446; 528 N.E.2d 703; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 109; 124 Ill. Dec. 15



July 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Richard E. Mann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) proceedings, § 9--1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1 (1985), defendant was sentenced to death after the jury unanimously found that he had attained the age of 18, that statutory aggravating factors existed, and that no mitigating factors existed. The sentence was stayed pending the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant guilty of murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a)(1), (a)(2), (a)(3) (1985), and other felonies. The court held (1) defendant's statements did not reveal that his loss of control was based on a long-standing chronic illness but rather one night of voluntary intoxication, (2) defense experts could only testify to conclusions reached through objective tests and any opinions based on defendant's statements were inadmissible, (3) if defendant had taken any drugs or alcohol, he did so voluntarily and not because of a permanent or fixed mental disorder, (4) the degree of publicity was typical for such a case and the circuit court examined each potential juror very extensively regarding any opinions regarding defendant's guilt and a newspaper article in order to provide defendant a fair trial, (5) the state's comments at sentencing did not inject extraneous inflammatory and prejudicial considerations before the jury and did not deny defendant a fair sentencing hearing, and (6) defendant failed to prove intentional discrimination, and the court ruled that the death penalty statute was not arbitrary, capricious, or racially discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, and directed the clerk of the court to enter an order setting the date on which the sentence of death was to have been implemented. The court ordered execution by lethal injection.

 

71 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Parker


No. 65036


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 204; 526 N.E.2d 135; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 96; 121 Ill. Dec. 941



June 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), reversing defendant's conviction for the offense of "sexual relations within families" under former Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11--11 (1985), finding former § 11--11 ambiguous and thus inapplicable to stepparents.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of "sexual relations within families" under former § 11--11, after engaging in oral sex with his 18-year old stepson. The appellate court found that former § 11--11 was ambiguous as to whether it included the relationship of stepparent/stepchild and was to be strictly construed against the state. The court reversed, finding that stepparents were clearly within the group of persons covered by the statute if they knew that the victim was their stepchild and that the legislature intended former § 11--11 to include "stepparents," even though that specific word was not included. The amendment of former § 11--11 to include the terms "stepfather or stepmother" was not intended as a change to former § 11--11 but to provide a fuller description of the group of persons to whom the statute was applicable. Penal statutes could not be construed so rigidly as to defeat legislative intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

People v. Baker


No. 65708


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 233; 526 N.E.2d 157; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 92; 122 Ill. Dec. 17



June 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cass County, the Hon. Arthur R. Strong, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which ruled that defendant, who had pleaded guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol, need not undergo a professional alcohol evaluation before sentencing because it would violate his right against self incrimination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol and was ordered to undergo an alcohol evaluation prior to sentencing. Defendant refused to obtain the evaluation, claiming that it violated his Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The trial court found him guilty of contempt. Defendant appealed, and the intermediate court reversed, holding that the evaluation was a Fifth Amendment violation. The state appealed that ruling, and the court reversed, holding that the regulation concerning submitting to an alcohol evaluation was permissive, rather than mandatory, and that defendant could be sentenced without having undergone the evaluation. The court also reversed the trial court's finding of contempt, and remanded the case to the trial court for sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the intermediate court and partially reversed the trial court. In remanding, the court held that the statute regarding undergoing an alcohol evaluation was permissive and that defendant could be sentenced without it.

 

73 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Health Clubs, Inc. v. Picur


No. 65386


Supreme Court of Illinois


124 Ill. 2d 1; 528 N.E.2d 978; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 94; 124 Ill. Dec. 87



June 20, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George A. Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health clubs appealed an order from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which held that an amendment to the Chicago Amusement Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 104-104-8 (1985) was constitutional. The health clubs' action had sought both to declare the ordinance unconstitutional and to obtain an injunction preventing defendant city from enforcing the amendment.


OVERVIEW: The amendment extended what the city termed an amusement tax to health clubs and racquetball clubs. The city contended that the amendment was properly enacted pursuant to its home rule power. The clubs contended, among other things, that the amendment was an "occupation tax", which according to the Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e) (1970), could not be enacted by a home rule unit without legislative authority. The court held that the amendment was in fact an occupation tax and that the city ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to health and racquetball clubs. The city's assertion that the tax could not be an occupation tax because it was assessed on the patrons of the club facilities was without merit. In fact, the clubs were responsible for assessing and collecting the tax. They were responsible for payment of the tax even if their patrons did not or refused to pay it and they were liable for substantial penalties for late payments of the tax. The tax was based on the occupation of the club owners. And, based on the wide variety of services the clubs provided, the tax could not be an amusement tax allowed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, par. 11-42-5 (1985).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's finding that the ordinance was constitutional. The court affirmed the circuit court's order that held the ordinance unconstitutional as applied to the health and racquetball clubs and that had entered a preliminary injunction preventing enforcement of the ordinance against the clubs.

 

74 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 62883


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 387; 528 N.E.2d 648; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 84; 123 Ill. Dec. 944



May 26, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, the Hon. Terrence J. Hopkins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, burglary, and aggravated battery after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois). He challenged the death sentence imposed by the trial judge. He claimed that the denials of motions for automatic substitution of judge and mistrial were error, that testimony was impermissible, and that the prosecutor's comments and his sentencing were improper.


OVERVIEW: During a burglary, defendant stabbed a woman to death and brutally injured her husband. Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, residential burglary, and aggravated battery. He waived his right to a jury for purposes of a death penalty hearing, and the trial judge sentenced him to death. Defendant petitioned for direct review. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114--5(a) (1981) allowed defendant to seek substitution of judges only once during his trial. The trial court did not err in allowing the testimony of the victim despite his apparent lack of competence. Defendant was not denied his right to confront this witness. The value of the testimony outweighed whatever prejudicial effect it may have had. Defendant was not denied a fair trial by the prosecution's comments. The trial judge's decision to impose the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate. The death sentencing scheme in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1 (1981) did not violate the U.S. Constitution or the Illinois Constitution, and it was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, residential burglary, and aggravated battery, and his death sentence. The trial court properly allowed defendant only one motion to seek substitution of judge. The testimony of the victim was permissible. The motion for mistral was properly denied. The prosecutor's comments did not deny defendant a fair trial. The death sentence was proper.

Am. Re-Ins. v. Washburn (In re Liquidations of Reserve Ins. Co.)


No. 66033


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 555; 524 N.E.2d 538; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 72; 120 Ill. Dec. 508



May 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. David J. Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion allowed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, director of the insurance company (director), filed a petition in separate liquidation proceedings. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ordered that all claims against appellee reinsurers were claims of general creditors within the meaning of Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 73, par. 817(1)(d). The reinsurers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to reinsurance agreements, the reinsurers contracted with other insurance companies to cover claims paid by those reinsureds on policies of direct insurance or reinsurance which the reinsureds issued to third parties. The resinsurer became insolvent and was placed into liquidation. Pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 73, par. 805, the director acted as the liquidator of both reinsurers. Numerous reinsureds which had not been paid by the reinsurers under their reinsurance agreements timely filed claims with the director. Claims also were filed by other creditors of the reinsurers and other state guaranty funds. The court concluded that if the legislature had intended to include reinsurance agreements under priority in Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 73, par. 817(1), it would have explicitly mentioned reinsurance agreements. However, because Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 73, par. 817(1)(c) was limited to certain claims covered under insurance policies and insurance contracts and did not include claims under reinsurance agreements, the court held that all claims against the reinsurers were claims of general creditors under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 73, par. 817(1)(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

County of Cook v. Renaissance Arcade & Bookstore


No. 64750


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 123; 522 N.E.2d 73; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 64; 118 Ill. Dec. 618



March 30, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Frank G. Sulewski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult businesses appealed a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed a judgment enjoining the businesses from operating at their locations in violation of zoning ordinance of appellee county.


OVERVIEW: The county sought injunctions prohibiting the businesses from operating in violation of zoning ordinances that allowed specified adult uses to operate only in certain zoned areas. The appellate court reversed the trial court's granting the injunction. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the appellate court applied a standard more demanding than that which was required. In order for a content-neutral zoning ordinance, which regulated adult uses to withstand constitutional scrutiny, the county was required to refrain from effectively denying the businesses a reasonable opportunity to operate. The ordinance did not have the effect of virtually banning adult uses. Evidence established that the ordinance provided the businesses with a reasonable number of suitable sites in which to relocate. Even though they might have been forced to expend a certain amount of money to relocate, they were affected no differently from any other commercial enterprise that suffered economic detriment as a result of land-use regulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and affirmed the judgment enjoining the businesses from operating at their locations in violation of the county's zoning ordinance.

 

77 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Daley v. Strayhorn


No. 63322


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 470; 521 N.E.2d 864; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 57; 118 Ill. Dec. 387



March 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writ of mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Illinois, filed an action for mandamus and prohibition, or for a supervisory order to compel respondent trial judge to vacate his orders. The trial judge had refused to hold a death penalty hearing, had sentenced respondent, a criminal defendant, to 40 years' imprisonment, and had denied the state's motion to reconsider.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 1 (1985). The state requested the trial judge to conduct a death penalty hearing, believing that defendant was eligible for the death penalty on the basis of another conviction for murder in the State of Rhode Island. The trial judge refused to conduct a death penalty hearing and sentenced defendant to 40 years' imprisonment. The state sought a writ of mandamus and prohibition, or a supervisory order to compel the trial judge to vacate his orders. The court awarded the writ of mandamus. The first phase of a death sentencing hearing was never held, and the trial judge was without a basis to refuse to hold such a hearing. As a hearing was never held, defendant's double jeopardy rights would not be violated if a death penalty sentencing hearing were conducted. The evidence included a copy of the Rhode Island murder conviction. Rhode Island's murder statute, under which defendant was first convicted, was substantially similar to Illinois's murder statute for purposes of the multiple-murder aggravating factor in para. 9 -- 1(b)(3). Accordingly, the trial judge had no basis to refuse to conduct the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of mandamus and directed the trial judge to vacate defendant's sentence of 40 years' imprisonment and hold a bifurcated death penalty hearing in accordance with the Illinois statutes.

 

78 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Muskat v. Sternberg


No. 64930


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 41; 521 N.E.2d 932; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 51; 118 Ill. Dec. 455



March 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Alan E. Morrill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant litigant filed a malpractice action against appellee opponents one day before the statute of limitations expired. Two years went by with no service, and the action was dismissed for want of prosecution. On the litigant's refiling, the opponents filed a motion to dismiss under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 107 Ill. 2d 103(b). The trial court denied the motion, and the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed and remanded.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the appropriate period of time by which to measure the litigant's diligence under Rule 103(b) commenced with the refiling. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court could consider any lack of reasonable diligence in obtaining service in the original lawsuit in ruling on the Rule 103(b) motion. On review, the court agreed with the appellate court judgment, finding that nothing was more critical to the judicial function then the administration of justice without delay. In order to fulfill the mandate of rendering justice fairly and promptly and to comply with the language of Rule 103(b), the trial court had to consider the litigant's exercise of diligence regardless of whether the lack of diligence occurred in the original action or after refiling. A dismissal and refiling under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13 -- 217 did not insulate the litigant from the lack of diligence displayed prior to dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded for the trial court to consider the litigant's initial delay in service in ruling on the opponents' motion to dismiss.

 

79 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Rivard v. Chicago Fire Fighters Union, Local No. 2


Nos. 63713, 63787 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 303; 522 N.E.2d 1195; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 53; 119 Ill. Dec. 336



March 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant firefighters' union appealed a judgment from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) that reversed a trial court's decision and ruled that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 -- 290.1 (1985) applied retroactively and that therefore plaintiff administrators' suits for damages for deaths and injuries suffered in fires were not barred.


OVERVIEW: The administrators sued the union for damages arising from the deaths and injuries suffered in fires that occurred during a strike called by the union in 1980. At the time the injuries occurred, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 -- 290.1 (1985), which permitted voluntary, unincorporated associations to sue and to be sued in their own names, was not in effect. The trial court therefore granted the union's motion to dismiss on the grounds that, under the common law, a voluntary unincorporated association could not be sued in its own name in an action at law. The appellate court ruled that the statute applied retroactively and reversed the trial court. On appeal, the court reversed and ruled that the statute did not apply retroactively to causes of action that arose before the statute's effective date. The court ruled there was no express language or necessary implication in the statute that indicated clearly that the legislature intended a retroactive application. The court ruled that the statute was not merely a change in procedure or remedies and thus the presumption of prospectivity applied, a presumption which only the statute itself could, but failed to, rebut.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the circuit court's decision.

 

80 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Geever


Nos. 64173, 64466 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 313; 522 N.E.2d 1200; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 59; 119 Ill. Dec. 341



March 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 64173. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.

No. 64466. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Themis N. Karnezis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state directly appealed orders of the Circuit Courts of Cook and Dupage Counties, Illinois, that held that the state could not, consistent with the constitutional guarantees of the First and Fourteenth Amendments, U.S. Const., amends. I, XIV, proscribe defendants' knowing possession of child pornography in their homes.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with possession of child pornography in violation of § 11-20.1 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20.1(a)(2), and the law was declared unconstitutional by courts in two counties. In reversing and finding the statute constitutional, the court held that the state could, consistent with constitutional guarantees of the First and Fourteenth Amendments, proscribe the knowing possession of child pornography in the home. The constitution protected the right to receive information and ideas, and statutes regulating obscenity did not reach into the privacy of one's own home, but the state's interest in safeguarding the physiological and psychological well being was compelling. When a definable class of material bore heavily and pervasively on the welfare of the children involved in its creation and production, the balancing of competing interests was struck and the materials were without protection of the First Amendment. In prohibiting without restriction possession of child pornography, the legislature sought to remove the final link in the chain of distribution of such material.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissals of the indictments, as the state had a compelling interest in the protection of the health and welfare of children, and was entitled to greater leeway in the regulation of pornographic depictions of them.

 

81 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Spreitzer


No. 63423


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 1; 525 N.E.2d 30; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 60; 121 Ill. Dec. 224



March 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Du Page County, the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought direct review of his death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court for the Du Page County (Illinois). Defendant claimed that the prior involvement of the public defender as a previous prosecutor in defendant's case disqualified all assistant defenders from representing defendant. Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute.


OVERVIEW: The prosecutor's office charged defendant with murder. One of the prosecutors who was involved with charging defendant left his position and accepted a position as assistant public defender, and eventually became the public defender. The circuit court found defendant guilty of murder and aggravated kidnapping. The state requested the death penalty, and the jury found defendant eligible. The jury found no mitigating factors to preclude a sentence of death. The circuit court imposed the penalty of death and 60 years in prison for aggravated kidnapping. Defendant sought direct review of his death sentence. The court affirmed the conviction and the death sentence, but reduced the kidnapping sentence to 30 years. The court found no per se conflict in the new public defender's involvement with the case in the prosecutor's office. The court found no potential or actual conflict in the assistant public defender's performance. The court found that certain inflammatory comments by the prosecution were not so prejudicial as to affect to fairness of the sentencing hearing. The court rejected defendant's arguments regarding the constitutionality of Illinois' death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder and aggravated kidnapping convictions, reduced the kidnapping sentence to 30 years, but affirmed the death penalty. The court found no conflict in the public defender, who was involved in charging defendant when he was in the prosecutor's office, and no conflict in the performance of the assistant public defender. The court found that comments by the prosecutor did not make the sentencing hearing unfair.

 

82 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Richardson


No. 60213


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 322; 528 N.E.2d 612; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 55; 123 Ill. Dec. 908



March 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that, following a jury trial, convicted him of murder, felony murder, and armed robbery and that sentenced him to death after finding the existence of a statutory aggravating factor during the death penalty hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a clerk during a store robbery and after he was convicted of murder, felony murder, and armed robbery, he was sentenced to death. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that evidence of another armed robbery was highly relevant and thus admissible to determine defendant's identification. Although the trial court did err in admitting evidence of a third armed robbery, the admission of limited evidence did not require a reversal because defendant's conviction was not based on the error. Defendant failed to prove that the pretrial physical lineup procedure was impermissibly suggestive, and identification testimony at trial was admissible because it had independent origin in the witnesses' memories and was sufficient to leave no reasonable doubt as to defendant's guilt. The jurors were properly instructed regarding the other-crimes evidence when all of the instructions were viewed together, and there were no errors requiring reversal in the prosecution's argument. The court found no reversible errors in the sentencing phase of the trial because the evidence sufficiently supported the finding of a statutory aggravating factor and the lack of mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction and death sentence for murder, felony murder, and armed robbery because there were no reversible errors in the admission of evidence of other crimes or identification testimony, the jurors were properly instructed, and there was sufficient evidence to support the death sentence based on a statutory aggravating factor.

People v. Stewart


No. 62086


Supreme Court of Illinois


123 Ill. 2d 368; 528 N.E.2d 631; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 50; 123 Ill. Dec. 927

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois dismissed appellant inmate's petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing. Defendant had entered pleas of guilty to charges of murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to death. The convictions and sentences were affirmed and certiorari was denied and he then sought relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122--1 et seq. The inmate contended that res judicata should not have applied because the instant claim was distinguishable from the claim raised on direct appeal. Any allegations relating to the inmate's subjective confusion or lack of understanding could have been supported by affidavits at the motion-to-vacate stage. Because they were not, the court found that the issue had been waived. The court concluded that the petition for post-conviction hearing and the documents filed in support of the petition did not make a substantial showing that the manner in which the prosecutorial discretion was exercised under our death penalty statute rendered the statute unconstitutional. The inmate failed to identify any authority indicating that any court had found the instant claim to be meritorious. He also failed to show that an Eighth Amendment violation had arisen in any of the several executions by lethal injection that had taken place in other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

84 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Esposito


No. 63868


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 491; 521 N.E.2d 873; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 48; 118 Ill. Dec. 396



March 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John L. Peterson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence of alcohol and with driving with a blood-alcohol concentration in excess of 0.10. The Secretary of State (Secretary) suspended defendant's driving privileges. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) held that the statutory provisions authorizing summary suspension of driving privileges and the issuance of judicial driving permits were unconstitutional. The Secretary appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the summary suspension procedure of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1985) violated the state and federal constitutions and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-206.1 (1985), which authorized the issuance of judicial driving permits, violated the separation of powers doctrine of the state constitution. The court held that (1) the standard for judging the constitutionality of the statute was the rational basis test because the challenged classification did not affect a fundamental right or discriminate against a suspect class; (2) the statutory classification, which applied the implied-consent concept and statutory summary suspension only to persons driving on public highways, was rationally related to public safety and did not violate the equal protection guarantees of the state or federal constitutions; (3) although defendant had a property interest in her driver's license, she was not entitled to a hearing prior to its suspension; and (4) defendant, who was granted a judicial driving permit for work-related driving, lacked standing to challenge the validity of para. 6-206.1 because she was not prejudiced by the application of the provision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

85 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Badoud


No. 65485


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 50; 521 N.E.2d 884; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 52; 118 Ill. Dec. 407



March 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Courts of Kankakee and Iroquois Counties, the Hon. Roger Benson, Edward McIntire and Dwight McGrew, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions, the state appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which affirmed the vacations of defendants' summary suspensions for driving under the influence of alcohol, under § 11-501.1(d) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1(d) (1985).


OVERVIEW: When defendants were arrested, the arresting officers signed the police reports below a notation stating that they solemnly affirmed that the requirements of § 11-501.1 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1 (1985), were met. Defendants each requested a judicial hearing be held before the effective date of the suspensions. The suspensions were vacated because the reports were not sworn to under oath. The appellate court affirmed. The court reversed and remanded the judgment. Although, § 11- 501.1 was unconstitutional because driving privileges could be lost based on an unsworn report at a hearing, the temporary suspensions based on such reports did not violate procedural due process. An officer's good-faith failure to initially swear to a report was curable given the seriousness of the public hazard that summary suspensions addressed. The summary suspension provisions were to be liberally construed to protect public safety. No impropriety resulted from swearing to the reports at the hearings when the legislature intended suspension hearings to be expedited, and requiring prehearing amendments to the reports would delay the hearing dates.


OUTCOME: In the state's criminal action, the court reversed and remanded the judgment that affirmed the vacations of the summary suspensions of defendants' drivers' licenses.
