People v. Easley


No. 64968


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 535; 519 N.E.2d 914; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 33; 116 Ill. Dec. 699



February 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Clay County, the Hon. Robert Stocke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part; sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which upheld defendant's sentence, finding the pertinent provision of § 5-4-1(b) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-4-1(b) (1985), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to have violated his sentence of probation and that probation was revoked. In a subsequent sentencing hearing, a judge other than the judge who had presided over defendant's trial sentenced defendant. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed that part of the order of the appellate court that upheld the sentence imposed, but vacated that part of the appellate court's order that found § 5-4-1(b) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-4-1(b) (1985), to be unconstitutional. The court held that the language of § 5-4-1(b) referred to the particular division of the particular county court in which the trial was held and not to a specific judge. The court determined that the General Assembly did not intend to require a circuit judge to return to a county court or a particular division in which he formerly presided solely to conduct a sentencing hearing. The court held that the appellate court should not have addressed the constitutionality of § 5-4-1(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the appellate court's order that affirmed defendant's sentence. The court vacated that part of the appellate court's order that held a portion of the Unified Code of Corrections to be unconstitutional.

People v. Walker


No. 63966


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 465; 519 N.E.2d 890; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 34; 116 Ill. Dec. 675



February 11, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which denied her motion for substitution of a judge pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-5(a) (1985) on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional as an undue infringement on judicial administrative authority.


OVERVIEW: Three days following her arraignment for battery and aggravated battery and the assignment of a judge, defendant filed a motion for substitution of the judge under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-5(a) (1985). The lower court denied her motion and ruled that the statute was unconstitutional as an undue infringement on judicial administrative authority. The court allowed the defendant's motion for leave to appeal and reversed and remanded the lower court. The court determined that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court stated that the legislature had the power to enact laws concerning judicial practice which did not unduly infringe upon the inherent powers of the judiciary. The court ruled that there was no conflict between Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(b), 107 Ill. 2d R. 21(b), and the statute because the rules of the circuit stated that the authority for their promulgation were based on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 1-104(b) (1983) and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(a), 107 Ill. 2d R. 21(a). Further, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-5(a) did not attempt to preclude assignment to an entire class of judges or assignment to any single judge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's ruling that the statute that allowed for the substitution of judges was unconstitutional. The court stated that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine or unduly infringe upon the inherent powers of the judiciary.

People ex rel. Bernardi v. Highland Park


No. 62419


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 1; 520 N.E.2d 316; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 30; 117 Ill. Dec. 155; 28 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 886; 108 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,859



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff director of labor challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which affirmed a grant of defendant city's dismissal motion in plaintiff's suit, which sought to enjoin defendant from awarding a contract for a public works project without first complying with the provisions of the Prevailing Wage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 39s--1 - 39s--12 (1985).


OVERVIEW: The intermediate court affirmed a grant of defendant city's dismissal motion in plaintiff director of labor's suit to enjoin defendant from awarding a contract for a public works project without first complying with the Prevailing Wage Act's (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 39s--1 - 39s--12 (1985), requirements. The court reversed that judgment on appeal and remanded the case. The court concluded that the act addressed issues that pertained to statewide affairs and that defendant had to comply with its requirements, even though it was a home rule unit. The court also held that it could not say that no real present question involving actual interests and rights existed even if defendant's duties under the act were no longer controverted because the controversy could have been classified as being capable of repetition yet evading review. The court further determined that departing from the prevailing wage was beyond defendant's home rule unit authority because it directly affected matters and individuals that were outside defendant's boundaries. Establishing minimum requirements to attain the act's goals was traditionally a matter of state concern.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment, which affirmed a grant of defendant city's dismissal motion in plaintiff director of labor's suit to enjoin defendant from awarding a public works project contract without complying with the Prevailing Wage Act, and remanded. The court held that defendant exceeded its home rule authority because its action directly effected matters that extended beyond its boundaries and were a state concern.

People v. Ashford


No. 63394


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 55; 520 N.E.2d 332; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 37; 117 Ill. Dec. 171



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Raymond L. Terrell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) for four counts of murder, four counts of felony-murder based on armed robbery, and one count of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering four persons in the course of an armed robbery. Finding no mitigating factors, the trial court sentenced the defendant to death for the murder convictions. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. With regard to the guilty phase, the court found that the state's use of a prior consistent statement was admissible to rebut the charge that the witness had a motive to fabricate the statement. Further, defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to call certain witnesses and regardless, counsel's performance was not prejudicial in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. With regard to the sentence phase, the note in the presentence report that defendant was hostile did not impermissibly refer to defendant's right to remain silent. Also, the judge was under no duty to inform the defendant that the jury's decision to impose the death penalty had to be unanimous; defendant knowingly and intelligently waived capital jury sentencing. Finally, defendant's sentence of death was not disproportionate to the life sentence his codefendant received given the fact that there was ample evidence that defendant was the trigger man.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence was affirmed because counsel was not ineffective for failing to call certain witnesses; presentence report did not violate defendant's Fifth Amendment right to remain silent; and, defendant knowingly waived capital sentencing jury.

In re Enis


No. 63986


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 124; 520 N.E.2d 362; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 35; 117 Ill. Dec. 201



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Richard C. Christian and Charles F. Scott, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's denial of appellee parents' motion to strike the allegation that they were unfit parents pursuant to section 1(D)(f) (Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(f)) of the Illinois Adoption Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 40, para. 1501 et seq., because it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: When appellant state filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of appellee parents, whose daughter was in foster care, the parents moved to strike the allegation that they were unfit parents under the Illinois Adoption Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 40, para. 1501 et seq., because § 1(D)(f) of the Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 40, para. 1501(D)(f), deprived them of their due process rights. While the circuit court denied the motion, the appellate court reversed, holding that the parents were denied due process. The court affirmed the ruling, finding that § 1(D)(f) of the Act did not satisfy the requirement of due process because it authorized the termination of parental rights upon proof of physical abuse by a preponderance of the evidence. The court held that the proper standard for termination of parental rights was clear and convincing evidence, as the lessor standard created a risk of error that rendered the proceeding unreliable. A second finding of abuse did not eliminate the risk of error, nor did it in itself constitute clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that a provision of the Illinois Adoption Act regarding determination of "unfit" parents violated appellee parents' due process because it authorized termination of parental rights upon proof of physical abuse by a preponderance of the evidence. The court held that the proper standard was clear and convincing evidence. A second finding of abuse did not constitute clear and convincing evidence.

 

92 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Madison


No. 64584


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 195; 520 N.E.2d 374; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 21; 117 Ill. Dec. 213



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in the court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Iroquois County, the Hon. Dwight W. McGrew, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with 26 counts of possession of a motor vehicle certificate of title with incomplete assignment, in violation of § 4-104 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-104 (1983) . The Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) affirmed the suppression of evidence of the incomplete titles because the evidence resulted from an illegal search and seizure. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether, when police officers discovered evidence of a crime during the course of a lawful administrative inspection conducted pursuant to § 5-403 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 5-403 (1983), the officers had to obtain a warrant before seizing the evidence. The State argued that the trial and appellate courts erroneously interpreted the warrant requirement of § 5-403, and therefore the evidence seized by the officers should not have been suppressed. The court held that the plain language of the statute contemplated that officers should obtain a warrant before seizing any evidence discovered during the course of an inspection. Therefore, any evidence seized by police officers without a warrant during an administrative inspection under § 5-403 was evidence seized outside the officers' limited authority under the statute and had to be excluded. The state statute imposed additional restrictions on the manner in which warrantless searches were to be conducted, and the court could not ignore the language of the statute or interpret it in such a way as to render the restrictions meaningless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

OVERVIEW: The victim was abducted by defendant, who eventually drove her to a park and raped her. Defendant later released her. The victim was then taken to a hospital. People v. Orange


No. 62144


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 364; 521 N.E.2d 69; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 39; 118 Ill. Dec. 1



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him to death for murder, concealment of a homicidal death, and aggravated arson. Defendant's execution was stayed pending direct review under Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VI, § 4(b); 107 Ill. 2d R. 603, 609(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced him to death for murder, concealment of a homicidal death, and aggravated arson. The court considered several contentions on appeal, including some that defense counsel failed to raise in the post-trial motion. Further, the consideration of juvenile adjudications at capital sentencing proceedings was appropriate. The court reversed the conviction for arson because the statute was subsequently invalidated, but this did not change the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and concealment of a homicidal death, and affirmed the sentence of death for several reasons. The conviction for aggravated arson was reversed because the statute under which defendant had been convicted had been invalidated. Defendant was to be executed by lethal injection.

People v. Porter


Nos. 63274, 63384, 63716 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 64; 521 N.E.2d 1158; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 27; 118 Ill. Dec. 465



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 63274. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. William Cousins, Jr., Judge, presiding.

No. 63384. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.

No. 63716. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur J. Cieslik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Judgments reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants claimed that the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2.1 (1985), was unconstitutional because it permitted the dismissal of a post-conviction petition, if a trial court deemed it frivolous, prior to the appointment of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' post-conviction petitions were dismissed by the trial court as "patently without merit." In one instance on appeal the lower appellate court reversed claiming that the dismissal without the appointment of counsel was unconstitutional. In two instances the lower appellate court affirmed the trial court's decisions. In affirming in one case and reversing in two cases on appeal, the court held that (1) the denial of counsel in frivolous post-conviction proceedings did not conflict with court rules providing for the appointment of counsel in direct appeals because the provisions provided for appointment of counsel at different stages of the post-conviction process, (2) the right to counsel at post-conviction proceedings was a matter of legislative grace and did not conflict with judicially promulgated rules, (3) fundamental fairness did not require the appointment of counsel in post-conviction proceedings, (4) the defendants' rights to due process and equal protection were not violated, but (5) because the lower appellate court failed to rule on two of the petitions within the period required, the rulings were void.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower appellate court in the two cases that were not decided within the allowable 30-day period were reversed and the causes remanded to the trial court for further consideration. The judgment of the lower court upholding the trial court's order dismissing the defendant's post-conviction case within the allowable 30-day period was affirmed.

People v. Crews


No. 62785


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 266; 522 N.E.2d 1167; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 38; 119 Ill. Dec. 308



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County, the Hon. Carl H. Becker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois), which, after defendant pleaded guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) to one count each of murder and attempted murder, sentenced defendant to death for the murder conviction and imposed a 30-year prison term for the conviction for attempted murder. Defendant argued that the legislature did not intend that the death penalty be a possible punishment for GBMI.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had attacked two correctional officers, killing one with a shank, while he was an inmate serving a 20-to-60-year term for an earlier murder conviction. He initially pleaded not guilty to the charges, but later asked to change his plea to GBMI, which was accepted by the trial court. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 5-2-6(b) (1983) provided that the court could impose any sentence upon defendant which could be imposed pursuant to law upon a defendant who had been convicted of the same offense without a finding of mental illness. That language left available for GBMI offenders the full range of sentences, including the death penalty, that could be imposed on persons who are guilty of offenses and who are not mentally ill. The court also determined that the sentence did not violate defendant's Eighth or Fourteenth Amendment rights. The court then concluded that evidence of defendant's mental illness was admissible at the capital sentencing hearing regardless of the relationship between the GBMI provisions and the statutory mitigating circumstance of extreme mental or emotional disturbance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court, which, after defendant pleaded GBMI to one count each of murder and attempted murder, sentenced defendant to death for the murder conviction and imposed a 30-year prison term for the conviction for attempted murder.

 

98 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Free


No. 64667


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 367; 522 N.E.2d 1184; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 36; 119 Ill. Dec. 325



February 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of murder, attempted murder, and attempted rape, challenged the dismissal of his second post-conviction petition in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois). The circuit court held that the assistance of defendant's counsel at his sentencing hearing was not ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the probation officer's testimony at the death penalty hearing was inadmissible and that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to it on grounds that it was prejudicial and inflammatory. After oral arguments were heard in defendant's case, the United States Supreme Court held in another case that victim impact evidence was not admissible at a capital sentencing hearing. The court, however, found that the only portion of the transcript of the sentencing hearing included in the record contained the probation officer's testimony. Without a more complete record, it was unable to ascertain the full effect of the presentation of the victim impact evidence, and of trial counsel's procedural default in failing to preserve the issue for review. The court also noted that the probation officer testified as to defendant's remorse and that she described favorable information that her presentence investigation had revealed concerning the defendant. Therefore the court held that application of the plain error standard to defendant's procedurally defaulted claims would deny the state's legitimate interest in the finality of the defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment denying post-conviction relief to the defendant.

 

99 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Gasoline Dealers Asso. v. Chicago


Nos. 64427, 64458 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 391; 519 N.E.2d 447; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 14; 116 Ill. Dec. 555



January 25, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gasoline association filed an action against appellee city contesting the city council's adoption of a vehicle fuel tax. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) upheld the challenged tax and granted summary judgment for the city. The gasoline association appealed from the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The gasoline association argued that the ordinance was invalid because it contained an invalid delegation of the council's taxing power and because the fuel tax was an unauthorized occupation tax that violated the state constitution. The court concluded that the gasoline association failed to demonstrate that the vehicle fuel tax ordinance violated the state constitution or any state statute and affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The tax was not invalid because its real estate taxing provisions permissibly delegated the council's taxing power to the city comptroller. The ordinance merely involved a factual determination by the comptroller to calculate the revenues received by the city from the vehicle tax. The ordinance vested no discretionary powers in the comptroller. Likewise, the ordinance did not impose an impermissible tax upon occupations in contravention of the state constitution. The vehicle tax was substantially similar to other home rule taxes that had been upheld and was declared by the court to be a proper home rule tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment in favor of the city.

People v. Thompkins


No. 56977


Supreme Court of Illinois


121 Ill. 2d 401; 521 N.E.2d 38; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 17; 117 Ill. Dec. 927

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Dwight McKay, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which imposed the death penalty under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1. Defendant claimed the court committed reversible error in allowing discovery violations, denying defendant's motions to suppress evidence and statements, admitting prejudicial hearsay, denying defendant counsel of his choice, and improperly instructing the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, sentenced to death, and appealed. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed. The court determined that the prosecutor did not misstate the testimony he expected to elicit from a witness and the reasonable inferences to be drawn therefrom. The court found no discovery violation under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 412 in the prosecution's failure to turn over reports of an Alabama police officer that interviewed defendant because the Illinois court had no jurisdiction over that officer. The court found that a hearsay statement was properly admissible as a spontaneous declaration and that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel under Strickland. Defendant was not denied his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI because adversarial proceedings had not begun and his uncounseled custodial statement was properly admitted because he had waived his right to counsel. The court found the search warrant was supported by probable cause, the jury was properly instructed, and defendant was properly sentenced to death under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1.


OUTCOME: The court determined that defendant received a fair trial, that he was not denied effective representation of counsel, and that he was properly sentenced under the Illinois death penalty statute. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

Pre-Sch. Owners Ass'n of Ill. v. Dep't of Children and Family Serv.

Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 268; 518 N.E.2d 1018; 1988 Ill. LEXIS 9; 116 Ill. Dec. 197



January 19, 1988, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Children and Family Services sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which granted summary judgment to appellee day-care center owners in an action which challenged the constitutionality of certain provisions of the Child Care Act of 1969, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, paras. 2211 through 2230 (1969).


OVERVIEW: A group of day-care center owners brought an action challenging the constitutionality of certain provisions of the Child Care Act of 1969, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, paras. 2211 through 2230. The circuit court granted summary judgment to the day-care center owners and the Department of Children and Family Services appealed. The court found that the exemptions did not provide a preference for religious day-care centers because the statute had a secular legislative purpose, its principal or primary effect was one that neither advanced nor inhibited religion, and it did not foster an excessive government entanglement with religion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the circuit court that granted summary judgment in favor of the day-care center owners.

People v. Hicks


No. 64702


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 29; 518 N.E.2d 148; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 271; 115 Ill. Dec. 623



December 30, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County, the Hon. Mark M. Joy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court convicting him of burglary, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1983), and theft, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: In challenging the judgment that convicted him of burglary and theft, defendant claimed that the appellate court erred in failing to find error in the admission of his prior theft conviction at trial. Defendant alleged that though the theft statute in question, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(e)(1), elevated the offense from a misdemeanor to a felony based on the prior conviction, the conviction should have been introduced only at his sentencing. He claimed introduction of the prior conviction at his trial violated due process and unduly prejudiced the jury. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, holding that where a prior theft conviction elevates the offense from a misdemeanor to a felony, the prior theft conviction was an element of the felony theft which must be alleged and proved during the evidentiary phase of the trial. In so holding, the court noted that subsequent to the conviction, § 16-1(e)(1) was amended to prohibit the introduction of prior theft convictions at trial. The court declared that under the rule of statutory construction the addition of the new provision indicated its absence from the act prior to the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that affirmed defendant's conviction for theft and burglary.

People v. Emerson


No. 61915


Supreme Court of Illinois


122 Ill. 2d 411; 522 N.E.2d 1109; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 285; 119 Ill. Dec. 250



December 30, 1987, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court stayed execution pending its direct review of defendant's death sentence after a jury conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of one count each of murder, attempted murder, and aggravated arson, and two counts of armed robbery, in his second trial for these offenses. In an earlier appeal, the court reversed defendant's convictions and granted him a new trial, which became the subject of the instant appeal.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the death sentence for murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery, but reversed his conviction for aggravated arson, and ordered that the sentence be carried out. The court had also previously rejected defendant's constitutional challenges to the Illinois death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Although the court agreed with defendant that his conviction for aggravated arson had to be reversed because the statute defining the offense had been invalidated, a new capital sentencing hearing was not required because the invalid conviction played no role in the jury's determination that the defendant was eligible for the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery and reversed the conviction on aggravated arson.

People v. Caruso


No. 65048


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 376; 519 N.E.2d 440; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 268; 116 Ill. Dec. 548



December 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Robert A. Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing child abduction charges against defendant after finding them to be an unconstitutional ex post facto application of the law. Instead, the court of appeals court found that the law was not applied ex post facto and that Illinois had criminal jurisdiction over the child abduction counts against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with child abduction, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(1) (Supp. 1984), and unlawful restraint, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-3 (1977) involving his daughters. On appeal, defendant only questioned whether Illinois could assert criminal jurisdiction over him after he harbored his children outside Illinois and failed to return them to their mother in alleged violation of an Illinois court order. The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. After considering several factors, the court held that Illinois had criminal jurisdiction over defendant, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1-5(c) (1985) because the offense as charged was based on an omission to perform a duty imposed by the law of Illinois. In addition, the court held that given the substantial interests involved in the prohibition of child abduction, and given the fault or wrongdoing inherent in defendant's conduct, it would not be fundamentally unfair to hold defendant criminally liable for that conduct. Therefore, the court concluded that the child abduction counts were improperly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the court of appeals reversing the judgment from the trial court dismissing the child abduction charges against defendant.

People v. Davis


No. 61538


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 61; 518 N.E.2d 78; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 274; 115 Ill. Dec. 553



December 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Patrick J. Fleming, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which dismissed defendant's petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (1983), alleging constitutional errors in connection with defendant's murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal, and the United States Supreme Court denied his petition for certiorari. Defendant then filed a petition under the Act, which the trial court dismissed. The court affirmed. Defendant could not make a substantial showing of a violation of his federal constitutional rights. Defendant claimed that the prosecution's use of peremptory challenges to exclude black men from the jury violated his right to a fair trial. The Batson rule, however, was inapplicable, since defendant's case was not pending on direct appeal at the time Batson was decided. Defendant also claimed that the victim's race made it more likely that he would receive a death sentence. Defendant relied on a study concluding that a suspect accused of killing a white victim in Illinois is four times more likely to receive the death penalty than is a suspect accused of killing a black victim. The court found the United States Supreme Court concluded that a similar study in Georgia did not demonstrate a constitutionally significant risk of racial bias affecting the capital-sentencing process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief in connection with defendant's murder conviction and death sentence.

 

107 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Foster


No. 62192


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 69; 518 N.E.2d 82; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 275; 115 Ill. Dec. 557



December 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John L. Nickels, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder by a jury in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois). The circuit court found that there existed a statutory aggravating factor in that the murder was committed in the course of an aggravated criminal sexual assault, and that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death sentence. The court sentenced defendant to death, but the sentence was stayed pending direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was arrested without probable cause, that his inculpatory statements were inadmissible, and that the death penalty was excessive punishment. The court affirmed. The circumstances known to the officers when they arrested defendant were sufficient to give rise to probable cause to believe that he had obstructed justice. Defendant's right to remain silent was "scrupulously honored." Defendant stated that he understood his Miranda rights and confessed that he had beaten the victim to death. After giving the statement, defendant signed a statement in which he waived his right to remain silent, and signed a typed confession. Given the extreme heinousness of the beating and the sexual assault, the prosecutor did not abuse his discretion in asking for the death penalty. The record clearly established that the defendant killed the victim "in the course" of committing an aggravated criminal sexual assault. The aggravating felony was not an isolated or incidental part of the beating which caused the victim's death. Given the record of extreme aggravation and the scant evidence in mitigation, the trial court did not abuse discretion in imposing a sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder and his death sentence.

Board of Trustees v. Burris


No. 63737


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 465; 515 N.E.2d 1244; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 258; 113 Ill. Dec. 937



November 23, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff college challenged an order from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) that found that defendant comptroller was not required to release funds for veterans' scholarships without an appropriation in an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief for reimbursement and that the State Mandates Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 2201 et seq. (1983), did not apply to those programs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff college made expenditures to fund veterans' scholarships when the state did not appropriate sufficient amounts to cover those costs. In an action for reimbursement, the circuit court held that defendant comptroller was not required to release funds without an appropriation and that although the State Mandates Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 2201 et seq. (1983), applied, the state's obligation under the Act was satisfied by partial payments. The intermediate appellate court reversed that part of the order finding that the Act applied to these programs, and on appeal, the court affirmed the intermediate appellate court. The court first determined that the court of claims did not have exclusive jurisdiction over this action because it was not an action against the state. It then concluded that a new school funding amendment was to be applied prospectively, and even if it were to be applied retroactively, the amendment was not intended to allow defendant comptroller to disburse funds without an appropriation. Finally, the court concluded that the Act did not apply to the veterans' scholarships because they were not a service mandate as defined by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the intermediate appellate court's order holding that defendant comptroller was not required to release funds for veterans' scholarships because the legislature did not intend the funding of programs without an appropriation. The court also found that the State Mandates Act did not apply to those programs because they were not service mandates.

People v. Inghram


No. 63830


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 140; 514 N.E.2d 977; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 231; 113 Ill. Dec. 65



October 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County, the Hon. Paul A. Kolodziej, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) denied a petition filed by defendant, who requested limited driving privileges as authorized by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6 -- 206.1 (1985) (the driving privilege statute) following suspension for driving under the influence. The trial court denied the petition and found the driving privilege statute unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found the driving privilege statute improperly assigned to the judicial branch the responsibility for the issuance of hardship driver's licenses on the ground that that was a function normally performed by the Secretary of State as a member of the executive branch of government. On appeal, the court reversed and found no violation of the Separation of Powers doctrine. The court held that a circuit court could perform certain nonjudicial functions, as provided by a statute, without violating the Separation of Powers doctrine and the issuance of a Judicial Driving Permit a circuit court neither conferred undue power to one branch of government, usurped the executive branch's powers, nor unduly burdened the judicial branch with a nonjudicial function. Certainly, in ascertaining the intent of the legislature, a circuit court was allowed to examine relevant legislation and seek to determine the objective the statute sought to accomplish and the conditions it wished to remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court ruling because giving the judiciary authority to grant of deny Judicial Driving Permits did not violate the Separation of Powers doctrine.

 

114 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roos


No. 64215


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 203; 514 N.E.2d 993; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 236; 113 Ill. Dec. 81



October 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Jane D. Waller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant had been charged with practicing medicine without a license. The circuit court agreed with defendant that the Illinois Medical Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4401 et seq. (1985), was unconstitutional as applied to the practice of acupuncture.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the unlawful practice of medicine in violation of § 25 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4460 (1985), after she engaged in the practice of acupuncture without applying for a license from the Illinois Department of Registration and Education. The circuit court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case to the circuit court. The court found that the Act did not require acupuncturists to have a medical degree under § 5(1)(b) of the Act, and that those who wished to practice acupuncture could obtain a limited license under § 5(2). The court reasoned that acupuncture does not constitute "operative surgery" within the meaning of the Act, and, therefore, acupuncture was covered by § 5(2). The court rejected the circuit court's finding that acupuncture was not Western medicine and therefore was not covered by the Act. The court found instead that the Act did not in any way indicate that it was limited to Western medicine, and, therefore, the court would not conclude that it was.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the state, and remanded for a new trial.

 

115 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Monroe


Nos. 63723, 63724 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 298; 515 N.E.2d 42; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 244; 113 Ill. Dec. 233



October 5, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Mary Jane Theis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenge the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted defendants' motion to dismiss the charges filed against them for violations of the Drug Paraphernalia Control Act (act) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, pars. 2101-2107 (1985). The lower court held that the act was vague and, therefore, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the state argued that the lower court found that the act was unconstitutionally vague because of a variance between the mental state requirements in the definition of drug paraphernalia in § 2(d) of the act and the statement of legislative intent in § 6 of the act. Defendants argued that the act was unconstitutionally vague because the definition of drug paraphernalia in § 2(d) of the act and the penalty provision in § 3(a) of the act contained contradictory mental state requirements. The court agreed because while the legislature apparently intended that scienter be included in the definition of drug paraphernalia, the penalty section allowed for convictions based upon the constructive knowledge of the seller. As a result of the conflict, citizens were not afforded fair notice of what conduct was prohibited and law-enforcement personnel were not provided clear standards in applying the law. Therefore, a danger of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement existed. Accordingly, the court found that the act was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of defendants' drug paraphernalia charges was affirmed.

 

116 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Witherell v. Weimer


No. 64440


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 321; 515 N.E.2d 68; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 246; 113 Ill. Dec. 259



October 5, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. John A. Gorman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendant physician for failure to diagnosis and treat a medical condition. The jury returned a general verdict for the patient that was reduced for contributory negligence. The Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) determined that equity required a new trial. The patient filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: A physician gave his patient, who suffered from a blood clotting disorder, oral contraceptives for an ovarian deficiency. The trial court awarded damages in a malpractice action, but reduced the award for comparative negligence. The court of appeals ordered a new trial. On appeal, the patient maintained that her award should not have been reduced for negligence on her part. The physician argued that the trial judge erred in failing to order separate trials as to the statute of limitations and liability issues and that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence. The court reversed the decision because (1) the physician made representations to the patient that alleviated her concerns about the birth control pill and blood clots, (2) the patient was entitled to rely on her physician's opinion, and the physician could not avoid estoppel by pointing to other sources that the patient could have consulted, and (3) the patient's experts produced substantial testimony that the physician departed from the standard of care. The court also held that the jury's instructions concerning the physician's burden of proving comparative negligence was in accordance with the current law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court in a medical malpractice action by a patient against her physician for the physician's failure to diagnose and properly treat a disorder. The court remanded the case with directions to deduct a sum from the damage award for the patient's contributory negligence.

 

117 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Watson


No. 63120


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 62; 514 N.E.2d 167; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 223; 112 Ill. Dec. 701



September 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Bill F. Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant the state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which ruled that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12--4(b) (1983) was unconstitutional in that it violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and the Equal Protection Clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. of 1970, art. I, § 2. Defendant was charged with aggravated battery under the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assaulted a county public aid employee on public property. The statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12--4 (1983), elevated the crime of battery upon a state or county public aid worker to aggravated battery, but did not so elevate the crime when the battery was committed upon a local public employee. For this reason, the circuit court held the statute unconstitutional in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution, and the Equal Protection Clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. of 1970, art. I, § 2. The court reversed, holding that although defendant had standing to challenged the constitutionality of the statutory provisions, the statute was not unconstitutional because the general assembly saw it necessary to protect state and county public aid workers who have broader powers and duties than their local counterparts. Because of the increased risk they undertake in dealing with, state and county public aid workers are deserving of heightened protection. The general assembly's classification was therefore reasonably related to a legitimate governmental objective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court, which held that the statute elevating the crime of battery to aggravated battery for assault on a state or county public aid worker was unconstitutional.

 

118 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Buddell v. Board of Trustees


No. 64296


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 99; 514 N.E.2d 184; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 227; 112 Ill. Dec. 718



September 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. Nicholas G. Byron, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Board of Trustees of the State University Retirement System of Illinois, brought an appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which, on administrative review of the board's final decision in the case, ruled in favor of appellee university employee and held that the limitation clause of § 15 -- 113(i) of the Illinois Pension Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 15 -- 113(i) (1983), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee went to work for the university after having served in the military. At the time, § 15 -- 113(i) (1969), provided that he could purchase military service credit under the university retirement system. The statute was amended in 1974 to make such credit available only to individuals who had applied for it by a certain date. The employee did not apply by the date specified and, when he did apply, his application was denied by the board as untimely. The employee appealed to the circuit court, which held the statute unconstitutional under Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5 (1970). On further appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the right to purchase service credits had been embodied in the pension code at the time the employee was hired and on the date the 1970 constitution took effect. Since, under § 5, the contractual right to purchase service credits could not be altered, modified or released except in accordance with usual contract principles, the court held that the portion of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 15 -- 113(i) that denied the employee the right to purchase military service credits after the date specified in the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of the employee.

 

119 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Haywood


Nos. 63082, 63539, 63540, 63541 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


118 Ill. 2d 263; 515 N.E.2d 45; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 241; 113 Ill. Dec. 236



September 21, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 63082. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County, the Hon. E. C. Eberspacher, Judge, presiding.

Nos. 63539, 63540, 63541 cons. -- Appeals from the Circuit Court of Fayette County, the Hon. Richard G. Hodson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual assault under the Illinois Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13, 12-14 (1985). The Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of Fayette County (Illinois), respectively, dismissed the charges, holding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The state sought review and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that there was no standard to determine the nature or quality of force constituting an offense under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13 (1985). The court held that due process required clear definitions in a penal statute and that, in construing a statute, the court was required to consider the language and the legislative intent. The court found that the statute recodified prior law and that the legislature intended to retain the prior definition of force. Thus, the court rejected the defendants' claim of vagueness and found that the statute proscribed only those acts of sexual penetration accomplished by the use of force. Although the statute did not specifically refer to compulsion or consent, the court held that these terms were relevant because proof of force implicitly showed non-consent. The court also rejected the lower courts' holding that the definition of bodily harm for the offense of aggravated criminal sexual under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14 (1985) lacked a sufficiently objective standard. The court held that this term had a well-known legal meaning and that the court could assume that this meaning was intended by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower courts' judgments.

In re Loss


No. M.R. 3972


Supreme Court of Illinois


119 Ill. 2d 186; 518 N.E.2d 981; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 264; 116 Ill. Dec. 160



August 17, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for admission to the bar.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, applicant for admission to the bar, filed his application with the State Board of Law Examiners and, after a hearing, the full commission approved his application. The board recommended to the court that he be admitted. The court reviewed the record as rendered the opinion below.


OVERVIEW: The record established that the applicant had a long record as a juvenile and as an adult of delinquency, theft, and drug related offenses, as well as a dishonorable discharge from the military. He had an excellent academic record, and many professors, students, and others testified as to his community participation and good conduct. He had not had a conviction in 11 years, and alleged that he had been rehabilitated and was not dependent upon illegal drugs. The court denied his admission but, because a future showing of rehabilitation was possible, the court held the matter open for re-application. The court held that the determination of the committee did not bind the court. It had the inherent power to regulate the admission to the bar and a duty to protect the public from dishonesty and incompetency. The applicant had failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that he was now fit to practice law. The court pointed out that there were inconsistencies in his application. Lastly, the court held that the applicant had not been denied due process of law by the process and the court's review.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for admission to the bar and suggested that the applicant file a new application.

Stelzer v. Matthews Roofing Co.


No. 63229


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 186; 511 N.E.2d 421; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 206; 110 Ill. Dec. 449



July 13, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant roofer appealed an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the granting of its motion to dismiss plaintiff homeowners' complaint for breach of contract, determining that the homeowners' cause of action was not barred by Ill. Rev. Stat. 110/13--214, but was within the term as expressly provided in the contract of guarantee, and, therefore timely.


OVERVIEW: The roofer installed a roof on the homeowners' house for the predecessor in interest and gave a 10-year warranty. Nine months after purchasing the house and over two years after the roof was installed the homeowners noticed that it leaked. The homeowners had the roof replaced and brought suit against the roofers to recover the cost three years later. The appellate court reversed the dismissal of the homeowners' action and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the action was filed within the term of the roofer's guarantee and, as such, was timely for purposes of the Construction Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 110/13--214 (1983). The court held that it was unable to discern the important governmental interest served by impairing a preexisting express guarantee of less than 12 years while, at the same time, preserving the effect of a preexisting express guarantee of longer than 12 years.


OUTCOME: The order reversing the grant of the roofer's motion to dismiss the homeowners' complaint for breach of contract was affirmed and the issue was remanded to the trial court.

Penkava v. Kasbohm


No. 61665


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 149; 510 N.E.2d 883; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 202; 109 Ill. Dec. 815



June 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendants physician's estate, hospital, and nurse. The trial court granted the defendants' motions to dismiss on the ground that the claims were barred by the statute of limitations. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed the dismissal of the claims against the estate and the hospital, but reversed the claim against appellant nurse, and she sought review.


OVERVIEW: The patient underwent a total hysterectomy at the hospital, and two foreign objects were permitted to remain in her body. The patient's claim for negligent failure to exercise due care in performing the surgery was brought eight years after the surgery. The appellate court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the complaint only as to the nurse because it held the nurse was not within the benefit of the statute of limitations for medical malpractice. The nurse argued the appellate court erred in interpreting an amendment to the statute of limitations. Prior to the amendment, the statute enumerated physicians, dentists, and hospitals. The amendment added registered nurses as protected by the statute. The court found the legislative intent of the first statute was to extend the reach of the protection of the statute of limitations to registered nurses employed by hospitals. The court found it was inconceivable that the legislature intended to protect only physicians, dentists and "hospitals" in a narrow, unreal sense, leaving nurses exposed to liability for later discovered malpractice. The complaint against the nurse was barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that reversed the order that dismissed the claim against the nurse.

La Salle Nat'l Bank v. Cook Cnty. Treasurer (In re Rosewell)


No. 63171


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 479; 512 N.E.2d 1256; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 218; 111 Ill. Dec. 619



June 29, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 5, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county collector sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's denial of appellee taxpayer's application to vacate the default judgment of sale of appellee's property entered pursuant to § 235a of the Revenue Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716a (1983), commonly known as the Scavenger Act.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court entered a default judgment of sale of appellee taxpayer's property pursuant to the Scavenger Act, § 235a of the Revenue Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716a (1983). The circuit court denied appellee's request to vacate the judgment of sale. Appellee contended that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction because appellant county collector did not mail notice of the proceedings. On appeal, the appellate court held that notice by mail was required and reversed the circuit court judgment. On further appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. Although the court found that the case was moot because appellee had paid the taxes, the court decided the appeal because of the public importance of the issues involved. The court held that neither the Scavenger Act, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, nor 1970 Ill. Const. art. IX, § 8(a) required notice by mail of scavenger proceedings. The court found that the proceedings utilized guaranteed personal and mailed notice and an opportunity to be heard prior to the loss of property interests, and the fact that one hearing in the process might occur without notice by mail was not constitutionally significant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court because notice by mail of an application for judgment and order of sale pursuant to the Scavenger Act was not required.

Independent Voters v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 62850


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 90; 510 N.E.2d 850; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 199; 109 Ill. Dec. 782



June 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Paul W. Schnake, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court had previously held that appellee Illinois Commerce Commission had improperly allowed certain expenses and deductions to a telephone company when it set utility rates. On remand, intervenor voters organization petitioned that all "overcharges" should be refunded to the telephone company's customers. The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed the denial of the petition and the organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organization had petitioned that all overcharges received by the telephone company under portions of the invalid rate order be refunded to the company's customers. The commission ruled against the organization, and that ruling was affirmed by the circuit court and the appellate court. The organization challenged those decisions under § 68 of the Public Utilities Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 72 (1971). The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. It found that the telephone company was required by statute to collect the new rates, which were found just and reasonable by the commission, and the company had received no unlawful charges of which it should be "disgorged" under restitution principles. As such, the court's prior decision holding that certain expenses and deductions allowed in the rate order were improper was final. Therefore, the portion of the rates that was held to be erroneously set by the commission was to be refunded to the customers who paid them from the time of the prior decision until the new rates took effect. But, there was no entitlement to refunds for the period preceding the reversal of the rate order.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed in part and reversed in part and the cause was remanded.

 

127 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ryan


Nos. 63402, 63403, 63404, 63405 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 28; 509 N.E.2d 1001; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 194; 109 Ill. Dec. 162



June 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County, the Hon. Carl Becker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) that dismissed charges against each of the four inmates of unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1. The trial judge ruled that the statute was unconstitutional and that the charging instruments failed to allege an offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were inmates of a correctional facility when they allegedly committed their offenses. Each was charged with possession of homemade weapons that were found in cells in the course of searches conducted by prison authorities. The inmates argued that the statute violated due process because it was vague. But in each case, the dangerous weapon was found in the inmate's cell, a place clearly within the intended reach of the statute. The defendants failed to show that the statute was vague as applied to them, and accordingly their argument that the statute was facially vague failed. If their contention was that the statute was unconstitutional simply because it prohibited innocent conduct, then their complaint was not one of vagueness, but rather one of substantive due process. The court believed that the statute provided a single offense, which could be committed in a variety of ways. Contrary to the inmate's argument, no unlawful intent was required with respect to an imprisoned felon's possession of a dangerous weapon.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the circuit court were reversed, and the causes were remanded for further proceedings.

Searle Pharmaceuticals, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


Nos. 63151, 63228


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 454; 512 N.E.2d 1240; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 217; 111 Ill. Dec. 603



June 10, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 5, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 63151. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.

No. 63228. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Robert E. Manning, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; cause remanded. Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parent-subsidiary taxpayers, challenged separate orders from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of Peoria County, which upheld the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, par. 2, § 203(e)(2)(E) of the Illinois Income Tax Act, which prevented the carryback of net operating losses by parent-subsidiary affiliated groups electing to file a consolidated federal corporate income tax return.


OVERVIEW: The parent-subsidiary taxpayers both elected to file consolidated federal corporate income tax returns and then attempted to carry back their losses to reduce their state income taxes. The Director of Revenue denied their requests, finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, par. 2, § 203(e)(2)(E) of the Illinois Income Tax Act required that any member of a parent-subsidiary affiliated group of corporations electing to file a consolidated federal return could only carry forward losses for purposes of reducing state tax liability. On appeal of the lower courts' denial of their separate claims that such a law was in violation of Equal Protection and of uniformity of taxation, Ill. Const. art IX, § 2, the court ruled that the Act violated Ill. Const. art IX, § 2. The court found that there was no real and substantial difference between a corporation which was a member of an affiliated corporate group that elected to file a federal consolidated return and a corporation which was a member of an affiliated corporate group that did not elect to file a consolidated federal return and that the classification bore no reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation or to public policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders from the lower court, holding that appellee Director of Revenue's interpretation of the law at issue violated the Illinois Constitution.

People v. O'Donnell


No. 63813


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 517; 508 N.E.2d 1066; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 286; 108 Ill. Dec. 489



May 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County, the Hon. Paul A. Kolodziej, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor Secretary of State appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) declaring unconstitutional certain provisions of Illinois' drivers' license summary suspension and reinstatement procedures.


OVERVIEW: After a defendant driver's license was summarily suspended for having a blood alcohol level exceeding .10, she filed a petition for restoration of her driving privileges, and the trial court declared the statutory provisions regarding reinstatement and the collection of fees unconstitutional. The Secretary of State intervened and appealed the finding. In reversing, the court held that a review of § 6-208.1(b) in the context of the entire drivers' licensing law (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-101 et seq. (1985)) led to the conclusion that the challenged provision was clear enough to permit uniform enforcement, and it was therefore constitutional. The court further found that the collection and forwarding of fees by the judiciary essentially involved little more than inter-branch communication and administrative cooperation. The court did not consider the collection of reinstatement fees to be an essential power belonging exclusively to one branch, nor was it persuaded that the procedure would detract from the exercise of judicial functions in any significant sense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that declared that the provisions of the driver's license law related to summary suspension and reinstatement of driving privileges were unconstitutional.

Catlett v. Novak


No. 62837


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 63; 506 N.E.2d 586; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 166; 106 Ill. Dec. 786



April 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Anthony J. Bosco, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorist brought personal injury claims against defendant driver and employer in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which were dismissed by the trial court for lack of diligence in obtaining service of process on the employer, which was attempted after the limitations period had expired and the claims against the driver had been voluntarily dismissed. The motorist sued the driver again, and then appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist claimed that he had previously voluntarily dismissed his claim against the driver under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1009 (1983) and refiled against the driver and the employer under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-217 (1983) without the limitations period expiring. The driver and employer claimed that the motorist had not been diligent in obtaining service of process and his claims should have been dismissed under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 87 Ill. 2d R. 103(b). The court reversed and remanded, holding that Rule 103(b) took priority over the legislative provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, paras. 2-1009, 13-217 (1983) and that under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 103(b), 87 Ill. 2d R. 103(b), the motorist was required to show that he had used reasonable diligence in obtaining service prior to the expiration of the limitations period. The court further held that the trial court was required to conduct a hearing on the question of whether or not the motorist did use reasonable diligence in serving process on the driver and the employer and on remand, was to consider the motorist's prior diligence when he previously dismissed his claims.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded to the trial court for a hearing, because the motorist was required to use reasonable diligence in obtaining service on the employer and the trial court was required to make a factual determination of that diligence.

 

132 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Erickson


No. 59058


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 271; 513 N.E.2d 367; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 209; 111 Ill. Dec. 924



April 2, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 5, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael P. Toomin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment in accordance with a jury verdict convicting defendant of intentional murder, knowing murder, felony murder predicated upon rape, rape, unlawful restraint, concealment of a homicidal death, and four counts of armed violence and sentenced defendant to death for murder, as well as an extended term of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded not guilty to the charges against him. The State indicated that it would seek the death penalty in the event defendant was convicted of murder. Before the start of trial, defendant attempted to waive his right to a sentencing jury, but the trial court refused the waiver. After he was convicted, defendant again tendered a waiver of the sentencing jury, and the trial court accepted the waiver. On appeal of his convictions and sentences, defendant raised 16 issues: three concerned the conduct of the trial, nine concerned the conduct of the death penalty hearing, and four raised issues challenging the constitutionality of the death penalty statute. The appellate court rejected defendant's contentions and affirmed, finding no error in the conduct of defendant's trial or sentencing hearing and finding defendant's arguments concerning the constitutionality of the death penalty statute to be without merit. The appellate court specifically held, inter alia, that although defendant attempted to waive a sentencing jury, the state was nevertheless allowed to query prospective jurors concerning the imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Shum


No. 61446


Supreme Court of Illinois


117 Ill. 2d 317; 512 N.E.2d 1183; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 210; 111 Ill. Dec. 546



April 2, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 5, 1987.
Writ of certiorari denied Shurn v. Illinois, 484 U.S. 1079, 98 L. Ed. 2d 1022, 108 S. Ct. 1060, 1988 U.S. LEXIS 874, 56 U.S.L.W. 3570 (1988)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Cause remanded by People v. Shum, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 781 (Ill., May 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James J. Heyda, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant sought review of his conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court of Cook County, (Illinois) for the crimes of murder, attempted murder, feticide, and rape.


OVERVIEW: Two women were raped and shot in an apartment one evening. One of the women was pregnant, and both she and her baby died as a result of the gunshot wounds. The other lived, which led to the apprehension of the defendant. He was charged with murder, feticide, attempted murder, and rape. He was tried by a jury that found him guilty on all counts. He then waived his right to sentencing by the jury and opted for the sentencing by the court. The court sentenced him to death for the aggravating factor of the murder which occurred in the course of the rape, another felony. He appealed based upon a multitude of errors. The court affirmed the conviction after finding the feticide statute to be constitutional and not arbitrary and capricious. The sentence of death was also affirmed due to the aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions on all counts and affirmed the death penalty given to him by the lower court.
