People v. Christiansen


No. 59870


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 96; 506 N.E.2d 1253; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 168; 107 Ill. Dec. 198



February 20, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Leonard R. Grazian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of numerous crimes, including murder, and sentenced by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to death. Defendant appealed from the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the murder of a store employee while robbing the store. A witness picked defendant out of a lineup and identified him as the person he saw leaving the store. Defendant was convicted of the murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court held that: (1) a finding of guilty but mentally ill was not warranted because the facts and evidence presented at trial did not suggest that defendant was suffering from alcohol-induced blackouts but instead was acting in accordance with a preconceived plan; (2) the prosecutor's testimony that defendant, when asked if he wished to reduce his oral statement to writing, responded that he did not wish to do so, was not an impermissible comment on defendant's right to remain silent because defendant waived that right when he gave two oral statements after being apprised of his Miranda rights; and (3) the trial court's failure to consider alcoholism as a statutory mitigating factor at his capital sentencing hearing was not in error because the record indicated that the trial court examined the evidence in support of defendant's claim and, after careful review, found that it was not sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding defendant guilty of numerous crimes, including murder, and sentencing defendant to death.

 

135 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. White


No. 62926


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 171; 506 N.E.2d 1284; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 171; 107 Ill. Dec. 229



February 20, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of White County, the Hon. Henry Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Circuit Court, White County (Illinois), which dismissed an information charging defendant with a violation of § 29--14 of the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 29--14 (1983), for distributing an anonymous leaflet advocating support of a political candidate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 20--14 (1983) after she distributed anonymous leaflets urging voters to support a political candidate. The trial court dismissed the charge on the ground that the statute violated the First Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 4 (1970). On appeal, the court affirmed and explained that the statute did not prohibit the anonymous distribution of all leaflets, but only political literature soliciting votes for or against any candidate or regarding any public question to be submitted for ballot. The court held that the statute was not well-tailored to serve the goal of an informed electorate. By banning anonymity, the law deterred many from expressing their opinions, decreasing the flow of information to the public. Further, the law was too broad in that it criminalized not only false and malicious statements concerning candidates, but also true ones, and even anonymous literature which was laudatory of a candidate. Thus, the statute unnecessarily restricted protected expression and could not be considered the least drastic alternative for preventing or remedying character assassination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court invalidating an Illinois statute prohibiting the anonymous distribution of handbills and leaflets concerning political candidates or issues to be submitted for a ballot as unconstitutional.

County of Kane v. Carlson


Nos. 63084, 63116


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 186; 507 N.E.2d 482; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 172; 107 Ill. Dec. 569; 124 L.R.R.M. 2720



February 20, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 63084. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.

No. 63116. -- Original action for mandamus or prohibition.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county sued defendants, county clerk, chief judge, state labor relations board (board), union, and officers, challenging the board's granting of a representation petition. Plaintiff chief judge sought a writ of mandamus or prohibition against the board declaring the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, pars. 1601 through 1627 (1985), unconstitutional and inapplicable to judicial employers.


OVERVIEW: The county's complaint sought a declaration that deputy circuit clerks were not covered under the act, that the act was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to the county, and that the county was the sole employer of the deputy clerks. The circuit court found that the deputy circuit clerks were not within the scope of the act, and the board had no jurisdiction over a representation petition. The appellate court reversed. In the other action, the chief judge sought to bar the board from proceeding on unfair labor practice charges filed against him, asserting that the complaining probation officers were judicial, not state, employees, and the act was being unconstitutionally applied to judicial employers. On review, the court held that the deputy clerks were within the act and were employees of the circuit clerk, rather than the chief judge, and that the probation officers were considered state employees. The court further held that judicial employees were within the scope of the act, and that their inclusion did not by itself violate the separation-of-powers principle or trench on the administrative and supervisory authority granted by the constitution to the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment finding the deputy clerks covered by the act was affirmed. The chief judge's petition for writ of mandamus or prohibition was denied.

People v. Lego

Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 323; 507 N.E.2d 800; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 180; 107 Ill. Dec. 647

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of multiple counts of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on four counts of murder. Defendant was sentenced to death on all four counts. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence, alleging numerous points of error. Defendant specifically argued that adverse pretrial media coverage denied him of a fair trial. The court found that defendant received a fair and impartial jury because there was no evidence that the jury was prejudiced, and the trial court had admonished the jury to avoid media coverage. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred in entering judgment on each of the four murder counts because there was only one homicide. The court held that when multiple convictions were obtained for offenses arising out of a single act, a sentence should have been imposed only for the most serious offense.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the portion of the judgment based on the felony counts, but otherwise affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant.

People v. Whitehead


No. 59050


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 425; 508 N.E.2d 687; 1987 Ill. LEXIS 186; 108 Ill. Dec. 376



February 20, 1987, Filed

139 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Guest


No. 58728


Supreme Court of Illinois


115 Ill. 2d 72; 503 N.E.2d 255; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 358; 104 Ill. Dec. 698



December 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Maurice Pompey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motions allowed; judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part; order entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for intentional murder, knowing murder, felony murder, attempted murder, aggravated battery, and unlawful use of weapons. Defendant was sentenced to death under the multiple-murder aggravating-factor provision of the death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: After being stopped by a store security guard for concealing merchandise in his pocket, defendant fired at several employees and shot the guard. Defendant then fled and another employee was found with a fatal gunshot wound in a portion of the store in which defendant had been. On appeal, the court held that there was sufficient evidence that defendant had shot the victim to support his murder conviction. Although the incident was not witnessed, it was unreasonable to think that anyone else shot the victim. The court held that the death penalty was justified because defendant previously had been found guilty of murder in California. The requirement that each murder conviction be based upon either intent or knowledge was met. Both the Illinois and California murder statutes required intent or knowledge in order for a killing to constitute murder. The difference between Illinois and California in the manner of imposing the death penalty subsequent to conviction was not relevant. The court held that defendant's convictions for knowing murder and felony murder had to be vacated because only one person was murdered and only the most serious conviction, intentional murder, could stand.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions for knowing murder and felony murder, and affirmed the remainder of his convictions. The court stayed the order of execution pending notification as to whether other states wished to waive their rights to penal custody of defendant.

People v. Sanchez


Nos. 61239, 63683


Supreme Court of Illinois


115 Ill. 2d 238; 503 N.E.2d 277; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 368; 104 Ill. Dec. 720



December 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. William D. Block, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; death sentence stayed. Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder and other offenses stemming from an abduction and slaying. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) convicted defendant, and defendant filed a petition under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, par. 2 -- 1401. The petition was dismissed without an evidentiary hearing, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended, among other things, that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions, the trial court erred in denying his motion for a continuance, he was denied a fair trial because of the pretrial publicity, the trial court erred by denying his motion for change of venue, the prosecution's actions during the trial denied him a fair trial, and the trial court erred by refusing to give a jury instruction and by denying his petition for relief. The court held that (1) the evidence was sufficient; (2) the denial of the motion did not result in prejudice to defendant; (3) the trial court did not err by denying the motion for change of venue because the level of awareness of the case on the part of the venire was not so great as to deny defendant a fair trial; (3) defendant was not prejudiced by the prosecution's actions; (4) the trial court's refusal to give the instruction did not constitute error because a general mitigating factor instruction was given; (5) the trial court erred by refusing the petition for relief without an evidentiary hearing because it had to make a determination of whether the witness was legitimately invoking the Fifth Amendment.


OUTCOME: Judgment of one conviction was affirmed, but execution of the death sentence was stayed. Judgment of another conviction was reversed and the case was remanded.

Springfield Rare Coin Galleries, Inc. v. Johnson


No. 62552


Supreme Court of Illinois


115 Ill. 2d 221; 503 N.E.2d 300; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 367; 104 Ill. Dec. 743



December 19, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff taxpayer's motion for summary judgment in an action for injunctive and declaratory relief as to the use and the occupation tax's allegedly unconstitutional exclusion of South African currency from an exemption for domestic and foreign currency.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the taxpayer's summary judgment motion in its injunctive and declaratory relief action that asserted that the state unconstitutionally excluded South Africa from a tax exemptions in the Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, paras. 439.8. 439.9 (1985), and the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 440 et seq. (1985), for foreign and domestic currency. The court affirmed that grant on appeal. The court reasoned that the legislative history showed both that avoiding the appearance of encouraging South African investment was the exclusion's plain purpose and that that exclusion was severable. The court also held that an executive order that banned the importation of Krugerrands did not make the taxpayer's claim moot because it did not effect the trading of Krugerrands that were already in the country. The court further determined that the exclusion impermissibly encroached on the federal government's exclusive authority to conduct foreign affairs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a grant of the taxpayer's summary judgment motion in its action for declaratory and injunctive relief as to an exclusion of South African coins in an exemption for foreign and domestic currency in the Use Tax Act and the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, holding that the federal government's exclusive control as to foreign relations was impermissibly infringed.

People v. Tosch


No. 62096


Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 474; 501 N.E.2d 1253; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 347; 103 Ill. Dec. 715



December 3, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John E. Bowe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant government sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared unconstitutional § 11-1006 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 11-1006 (1985), under which the defendant had been charged.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was arrested after police officers observed her standing in the roadway, stopping vehicles containing men, and engaging them in conversation. The officers arrested her for violation of § 11-1006 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 11-1006 (1985), which prohibited standing in the roadway to solicit rides, employment, business, or contributions, except contributions to certain registered charities under certain safety conditions. The trial court dismissed the charge on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's ruling. The court held that the statute was a reasonable restriction of the time, manner, and place of speech and therefore permissible under the First Amendment to the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. I, and that the distinction it made between solicitation by charities and other types of solicitation did not violate the defendant's right to equal protection under the United States or Illinois constitutions because it was reasonably related to the legitimate governmental objective of balancing safety considerations against the relative social value of the activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's determination that the statute prohibiting solicitation of rides, employment, or contributions on the public highway was unconstitutional and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Schlenz v. Castle


No. 62093


Supreme Court of Illinois


115 Ill. 2d 135; 503 N.E.2d 241; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 360; 104 Ill. Dec. 684



November 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Robert K. McQueen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District, which affirmed the order of the lower court that dismissed the taxpayers' complaint against defendant government officials, attacking the practices of the officials responsible for the assessment and equalization of property pursuant to the Revenue Act of 1939 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 482 et seq. (1985).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers and taxpayers' association attacked the assessment of property taxes, and the complaint was dismissed as to the individual taxpayers. They appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that a private citizen has no authority to bring a suit for the collection of taxes. The court noted that the complaint was in many respects unintelligible, but that because the government officials had never argued the legal insufficiency of the complaint, the court would not decide that issue. The court determined that the complaint alleged that property belonging to persons other than the taxpayers had either been underassessed or improperly exempted from taxation. The court noted that the taxpayers' only stake in the underassessment of other types of property was its effect on their taxes and that the taxpayers' inability to force the government officials to increase other assessments did not render the tax-objection proceeding an inadequate remedy. The court also determined that the taxpayers' specific allegations regarding tax-exempt property in one county were deficient due to inadequate description of the exempt properties and a vague request for relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the circuit and appellate courts and remanded to the circuit court with directions that the complaint be dismissed as to the taxpayers' association as well.

Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 39s-1 et seq. (1985), the appellate court (Illinois) affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the director's complaint. The director appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city was a home rule unit that had issued contract specifications for a public works project involving a water treatment plant. The city did not comply with the Act when soliciting and accepting bids for the project because it contended that as a home rule unit, it was not required to comply with the Act. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the director's complaint.

People v. Clark


No. 61732


Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 450; 501 N.E.2d 123; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 345; 103 Ill. Dec. 102



November 20, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. E. C. Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the affirmance of his convictions by the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) for aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1981); arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1 (1981); and possession of an incendiary device, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-2 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended his confession following his arrest was improperly admitted into evidence and that the conviction under the former version of the aggravated arson statute was invalid. A doctor testified that defendant had a crushed trachea that resulted from a blunt trauma to defendant's neck and upper chest area. The court held that the evidence did not clearly establish that defendant was injured while in police custody. Although symptoms of defendant's injuries were noticed while he was in custody, defense did not demonstrate when the injury occurred. Defendant's cough was the single external indication of his injury. Because defendant failed to establish that he was injured while in police custody, and because this point was not conceded by the state, the court declined to require the prosecution to demonstrate by clear and convincing evidence that defendant's injury was wholly unrelated to his confession. However, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1981) had been declared unconstitutional. Because the aggravated-arson conviction had to be reversed, the court remanded the cause for sentencing on the arson conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the appellate and trial courts were affirmed with respect to the defendant's conviction for arson and conviction and sentence for possession of an incendiary device. The judgments were reversed with respect to defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated arson. The cause was remanded to the trial court for sentencing on the arson conviction.

In re Marriage of Bogan


No. 62724


Supreme Court of Illinois


116 Ill. 2d 72; 506 N.E.2d 1243; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 375; 107 Ill. Dec. 188



November 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Susan Snow Ruffolo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of the order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which dismissed the wife's appeal from a bifurcated judgment of dissolution of marriage entered by the circuit court that dissolved her marriage to appellee husband.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed a petition for the dissolution of her marriage to the husband. The husband filed a motion for summary judgment and for entry of a bifurcated judgment. After a hearing, the circuit court decided in favor of bifurcation and entered a judgment of dissolution. The circuit court reserved all other issues, including property division, maintenance, and attorney fees, for future consideration. The wife appealed the entry of the bifurcated judgment. The appellate court dismissed the appeal, holding that a judgment of dissolution was not final and appealable, and the court granted the wife leave to appeal. The court reversed the order of the circuit court and remanded the matter for further proceedings, holding that it was not persuaded that the husband's inability to perform the social functions expected by his employer in connection with his job constituted an appropriate circumstance for bifurcation. Consequently, the circuit court abused its discretion by entering a bifurcated judgment of dissolution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that dismissed the wife's appeal from the circuit court, which entered a bifurcated judgment of dissolution. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

147 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


No. 62778


Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 69; 499 N.E.2d 470; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 323; 101 Ill. Dec. 882



October 17, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. John Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed a charge of aggravated arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1983) against defendant. The trial court held that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1983). The information was dismissed by the trial court on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional, prompting an appeal by the State. The court noted that certain subsections of the statute had previously been found to be unconstitutional by the Illinois Supreme Court. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(3) (1983) was held to be unconstitutional on the ground that the statute, which defined aggravated arson, did not require an unlawful purpose in setting a fire, and therefore swept too broadly. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1) (1983) was similarly unconstitutional. The court noted that while the legislature intended subsections (1), (2), and (3) of the statute to constitute enhancements of the arson offense, the underlying charge had not been properly defined.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the information against defendant on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional.

People v. Johnson


No. 60826


Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 170; 499 N.E.2d 1355; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 331; 102 Ill. Dec. 342

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for murder, aggravated kidnapping, deviate sexual assault, and attempted murder. The circuit court imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: After his motion for change of venue was granted, defendant was convicted of the murder of a man during a robbery in which the man was shot and his girlfriend abducted and raped. Defendant was sentenced to death after the trial court found that the necessary aggravating factors existed and that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty. On direct appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that having prevailed on his first motion for a change of venue, the defendant could not be heard to complain that distinctive groups in the original county were not proportionately reflected in the venire in the new county. The defendant failed to carry his burden of establishing that he held a reasonable expectation of privacy in a pickup truck at the time it was searched and seized. In view of overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, the prosecutor's improper comment did not constitute a material factor in defendant's conviction. Evidence of defendant's involvement in a similar murder was properly admitted at the sentencing phase held before the judge without a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People ex rel. Skinner v. Hellmuth, Obata & Kassabaum, Inc.


Nos. 62418, 62422 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 252; 500 N.E.2d 34; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 335; 102 Ill. Dec. 412



October 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. John L. Hughes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, as chairman of the Capital Development Board, filed suit against various defendants, contractors and sureties, alleging breach of an express contract, breach of an implied warranty of habitability, and faulty construction of a college building, and defendants appealed a ruling of the Illinois Appellate Court for the Second District that the applicable statute of limitations was invalid as special legislation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contracted for construction of college buildings, and more than two years after problems with the building were discovered, filed suit against the builder, architect, and surety. The court reversed the appellate court ruling that § 13-214 was special legislation, holding that it was not unreasonable to classify construction activities separately for purposes of the statute of limitations. The court ruled that the contractor's bonding company was liable for any breach of contract, if proven, as the statute of limitations against sureties was ten years, as provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-206 (1983).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the holding that the two-year statute of limitations on claims against the principals was invalid as special legislation, but held that the applicable limitations period against the provider of the contractor's surety bond was 10 years.

People v. McWhorter

The State appealed.

151 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kohrig


Nos. 62719, 62799, 63075, 63224 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 384; 498 N.E.2d 1158; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 309; 101 Ill. Dec. 650



October 1, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 62719. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County, the Hon. Richard H. Brummer, Judge, presiding.

No. 62799. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County, the Hon. Dennis L. Berkbigler, Judge, presiding.

No. 63075. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. John R. DeLaMar, Judge, presiding.

No. 63224. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County, the Hon. Richard G. Hodson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion allowed; judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, in four consolidated cases, challenged judgments of the Circuit Courts of Marion County, Effingham County, Champaign County, and Fayette County (Illinois), which concluded that § 12--603.1 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 12--603.1 (1985), was unconstitutional and dismissed defendant drivers' traffic citations for failure to wear seat safety belts while operating their motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed from trial courts' findings that § 12--603.1, which required the use of seat belts, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that regulations that limited a person's constitutional right to privacy could be justified only by a "compelling state interest," and the legislation was required to be narrowly drawn to express only the legitimate state interests at stake. It could not have been said that a driver's claimed right to decide whether or not to wear a safety belt on a public highway resembled those liberties identified by the United States Supreme Court as being included in the right of privacy protected by the fourteenth amendment. The court held that the statute did not infringe upon a driver's right of privacy protected by the fourteenth amendment or by the state constitution. The court also held that the statute did not violate the due process clauses of the state or federal constitutions. The legislature could have rationally determined that the seat-belt use law served the public safety and welfare by reducing the likelihood that a driver would lose control of his vehicle and jeopardize other motorists or pedestrians.


OUTCOME: The judgments below holding unconstitutional the state statute requiring the use of seat belts were reversed, and the causes were remanded.

 

152 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lang


No. 61368


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 407; 498 N.E.2d 1105; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 310; 101 Ill. Dec. 597



October 1, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision by an Illinois appellate court, which held that respondent, committed individual, was entitled to a formal fitness hearing concerning his competency to stand trial for murder. The appellate court also decided to defer consideration of the challenged hearings on involuntary admission in light of its resolution of the fitness issue.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal by the state, was whether the trial court erred in refusing to grant the committed individual a new fitness hearing in regard to his fitness to stand trial for murder. The committed individual was subjected to involuntary admission after an initial fitness hearing and further involuntary admission hearings were held as the committed individual continued to be confined. The committed individual asserted that he was entitled to a new fitness hearing and an appellate court also agreed. The court affirmed that decision, but held that the involuntary admission hearings were proper based upon their evidence. The court held that the issue of whether the committed individual was fit to stand trial was totally unrelated to the issue of whether he was subject to involuntary admission. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1985, ch. 38, para. 104-23(b)(3), was not dispositive of the issue. The court then concluded that the guarantee of fundamental fairness inherent in the due process clause required periodic review of the committed individual's fitness status, so as to determine if he was fit to stand trial, thereby ensuring that his speedy trial rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in part and reversed and remanded it in part. The court held that the committed individual was indeed entitled to periodic review of his fitness status so as to determine if he was fit to stand trial to ensure that his due process rights were not violated. The court also found that the involuntary admission hearings were proper because sufficient evidence had been presented to justify the decisions.

People v. Upton

Supreme Court of Illinois


114 Ill. 2d 362; 500 N.E.2d 943; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 342; 102 Ill. Dec. 842



September 17, 1986, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for distribution of a "look-alike" substance. The appeals court had reversed the conviction based on a finding that Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1982 Supp.), was violative of the due process requirements under the constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had argued that the fact that the fines were higher for those who sold "look-alike" drugs then they were for those who sold controlled substances violated due process requirements. At issue was whether certain legislation previously held unconstitutional could be upheld if, when reenacted, it was accompanied by a preamble which expressed a new and different legislative intent. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the appellate court's decision to vacate defendant's conviction and fine. The court held that the legislature, in the preamble, had explicitly asserted an intention to penalize the sale look-alike substances more harshly then the sale of some controlled substances and therefore the statute was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the appellate court to vacate defendant's conviction.

People v. Szabo


No. 60062


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 83; 497 N.E.2d 995; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 285; 100 Ill. Dec. 726



June 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. John F. Michela, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which, upon remand from the court, reinstated defendant's murder convictions and sentenced him to the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of various counts of murder, and a jury sentenced him to death. On remand from the court, the lower court reinstated the murder convictions and resentenced defendant to the death penalty. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court held that the lower court's erroneous conclusion that certain witness statements in plaintiff's possession was protected work product did not prejudice defendant and was not reversible error because the disclosure of the statements would not have aided defendant's case. The court further held that the lower court's admission, at the sentencing hearing, of plaintiff's transcripts of prior testimony was not plain error because the testimony bore sufficient indicia of reliability. The court also held that certain remarks, which were made by the prosecutor during closing argument to the sentencing jury, did not amount to plain error. Finally, the court held that the lower court's denial of defendant's motion in limine to restrict his cross-examination was not plain error because defendant's right to testify on his behalf was subject to plaintiff's right to impeach his testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the lower court, which, upon remand from the court, reinstated defendant's murder convictions and sentenced him to the death penalty. The lower court's conclusion, that certain witness statements in plaintiff's possession was protected work product, did not prejudice defendant and was not reversible error.

Bernier v. Burris


No. 62876


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 219; 497 N.E.2d 763; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 295; 100 Ill. Dec. 585



June 20, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of plaintiff individual, which held that a number of provisions of the Ill. Code Civ. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, paras. 1-101 through 19c-101, concerning medical malpractice actions, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The individual brought an action challenging the constitutionality of various provisions of a public law which made significant changes to the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure in medical malpractice actions. The court affirmed in part the decision of the lower court and reversed in part. The court affirmed the lower court's finding of unconstitutionality of a provision for review panels, consisting of a judge and two laymen, in cases of healing-art malpractice, because the judicial member was forced to share his authority with the nonjudicial members. The court reversed the lower court's finding of unconstitutionality of provisions related to periodic payment of damages, discounting of the damages, posting of security, modification of the collateral source rule, prohibition against punitive damages, and limitation on attorney fees. The court held that, in attempting to remedy a perceived ill, i.e., the medical malpractice crisis, the legislature was not limited to choosing the single, most effective remedy against the problem but rather could decide to attack it along several fronts simultaneously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision in part and reversed in part, holding that the review panel provision was unconstitutional but the balance of the changes to the civil rules were constitutional.

 

158 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Jones


No. 61694


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 126; 497 N.E.2d 738; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 288; 100 Ill. Dec. 560



June 6, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Robert E. Manning, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lottery winners sought review of the order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), arising from their claim that the defendant, Director of the Illinois State Lottery, breached an agreement with lottery players and otherwise engaged in fraud.


OVERVIEW: The lottery winners had won one of several winning tickets in a drawing. They alleged that they were entitled to the full amount of the prize that was advertised, among other claims. The trial court dismissed for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The appellate court reversed upon the grounds that the complaint generally sounded in fraud, and, as such, the claim was excepted from the operation of the doctrine of exhaustion of remedies. The court reversed the appellate court, holding that the director and the agency were protected by sovereign immunity. There were two exceptions to sovereign immunity, it did not apply when the complaint alleged that a statute was unconstitutional, or when it alleged that an official was acting beyond his authority. The lottery winners' complaint primarily alleged that the director breached his contract with them, and that claim had to be brought before the Court of Claims. Secondly, the court held that the complaint did not state an action in fraud because it did not plead the elements of fraud, thus it did not avoid the operation of the rule that the lottery winners had to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, and affirmed the dismissal of the action by the trial court.

 

159 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Oak Lawn v. Rosewell


No. 61293


Supreme Court of Illinois


113 Ill. 2d 104; 497 N.E.2d 734; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 286; 100 Ill. Dec. 556



June 6, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George A. Higgins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the village's action against defendants, county and county officials, challenging the constitutionality of § 224 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 705 (1984 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: The village alleged that para. 705, which authorized the county to collect and retain interest on delinquent real estate taxes, violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) (1970), as well as its constitutional right to equal protection. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, and the appellate court affirmed. The court allowed plaintiff's petition for leave to appeal and affirmed, holding that the county's retention of the interest penalty on delinquent taxes collected by the county for other governmental units was not a fee within the meaning of Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) (1970). The court found that, absent the statute in question, the village was not entitled to interest on delinquent taxes. The penalty funds existed only because the statute created a penalty for the delinquent payment of taxes. The statute did not deprive the village of the interest it would have received had the taxes been promptly paid over to the units by the county, and the proceeds placed at interest. With respect to the equal protection challenge, the court held that a rational basis existed upon which to distinguish counties from other taxing units for purposes of receiving fiscal benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court affirming the trial court's dismissal of the village's challenge to a statute authorizing the county to retain interest charged on delinquent property taxes collected on behalf of the village.

Bd. of Certified Safety Prof'ls of the Ams., Inc. v. Johnson


No. 61862


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 542; 494 N.E.2d 485; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 277; 98 Ill. Dec. 363



June 6, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. George Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a not-for-profit corporation (the corporation), appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) that affirmed decisions from respondent, the Illinois Department of Revenue (the department), that denied the corporation's request for a tax exemption. The circuit court ruled, among other things, that § 19.10 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.10 (1983), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The corporation issued certificates to safety professionals who passed examinations that the corporation conducted. The corporation's application for a partial real estate tax exemption was denied, with the circuit court ultimately concluding that, § 500.10, the chief exemption relied upon by the corporation, which provided an exemption for property used for "mechanical" purposes, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court ruled: (1) § 500.10 was unconstitutional because it purported to provide an exemption not specifically provided for in Ill. Const. art. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.1 (1983) "school" or "other educational purposes" exemption because the corporation's sponsors were not exempt and the state did not license or register safety professionals and; (3) the corporation did not qualify for the Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.7 (1983) "charitable" exemption because the corporation's activities benefited only a particular class of people, the safety professionals, and only indirectly the general public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that affirmed the department's denial of the corporation's request for a tax exemption and that declared that a certain statutory tax exemption was unconstitutional.

People v. Dale


No. 62264


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 460; 493 N.E.2d 1060; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 267; 98 Ill. Dec. 39



May 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Saline County, the Hon. Michael Henshaw, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a criminal case filed by the People of the State of Illinois, appellant-intervenor defense attorney challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) that affirmed the denial of his motion for attorney fees. He argued that his fee claim had priority over the "street value" fine imposed on his client, and that the street value fine provision, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(h) (1983), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7 (1983), defendant deposited 10 percent of his bail to be released on bond. The bond stated that if a fine or court costs were adjudged, the remainder of the deposit was to go to the fine or costs. Before trial, defendant assigned his right to the bail deposit to the defense attorney. Defendant was convicted of a drug offense. The trial court increased his bail bond. Defendant deposited more money to meet the new 10 percent. As a sentence, defendant was assessed a fine under § 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1983), based on the street value of the drugs. The trial court denied the defense attorney's motion to apply the bail bond deposit to attorney fees. It ordered the deposit applied to the fine and court costs. The court affirmed the judgment. Bail deposits were not intended to pay attorney fees. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(h) (1983) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(f) (1981) did not conflict. The pretrial assignment of the deposit to the defense attorney was irrelevant. The issue of the street value provision's constitutionality was not preserved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that affirmed the denial of the defense attorney's motion for attorney fees.

Metro. Life Ins. Co. v. Washburn

Supreme Court of Illinois

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state officials, challenged a decision of the Circuit Court (Illinois) that entered preliminary injunctions, which required the state officials to maintain the entire protested privilege tax payments, and any further payments properly made under protest, in the protest fund.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, 14 foreign insurance companies licensed to do business in Illinois, made payments of privilege taxes under protest and then, in 3 separate but similar actions filed in the trial, challenged the constitutionality of the tax. Relying on § 441.1(4), the state officials argued that portions of the protested payments could be released from the protest fund into the state's general revenue fund. OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the trial court's holding that found that the statutory authority relied on by the state officials did not require the release into the general revenue fund of alternative retaliatory taxes that the insurance companies indicated were being protested. The court concluded that the issue of the statute's constitutionality did not come into question and therefore vacated that portion of the trial court's decision.

People ex rel. Eppinga v. Edgar


No. 61638


Supreme Court of Illinois

April 18, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver sought review of the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment to defendant, the Secretary of State (secretary), in the driver's action that sought restoration of his driving privileges and a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 1-100 et seq. (1983), under which his license was revoked, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the driver was charged with the offense of driving under the influence of alcohol pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(2) (1981), the state's attorney requested an administrative revocation of the driver's license. The secretary revoked the driver's license pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-206(a)(1) (1983) and Ill. Admin. Code tit. 92, ch. II, § 1040.35 (1984). The driver brought an action against the secretary that sought restoration of his driving privileges and a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 1-100 et seq. (1983) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the secretary, and the driver sought review. On appeal, the driver contended that, because he was not given a pre-revocation hearing, he was denied due process of law. The court applied the three factors for determining whether a prior hearing was required to afford due process and held that the driver was not denied due process. The court affirmed the summary judgment because the application of the statute and the secretary's guidelines to the driver was proper and not contrary to governmental interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the secretary for the secretary's revocation of the driver's license and driving privileges prior to the driver's trial on the charge of driving under the influence of alcohol.

People v. Morgan


No. 58729


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 111; 492 N.E.2d 1303; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 245; 97 Ill. Dec. 430



April 18, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Robert L. Massey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment with two murders, rape, and aggravated kidnapping. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted the defendant of all charges pursuant to a jury verdict and sentenced the defendant to death and to concurrent extended prison terms of 60 and 30 years for rape and aggravated kidnapping, respectively. The defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with two murders and the rape and kidnapping of a woman. At trial, expert testimony showed that a revolver, recovered from defendant upon his arrest, had fired the bullets recovered at the apartment house where the murders took place. The trial court convicted defendant of all charges and sentenced him to death for the murders, 60 years for rape, and 30 years for kidnapping. The defendant appealed, challenging the composition of the jury, prosecutorial conduct, the sufficiency of the evidence, and his sentences. On appeal, the court held that the defendant received a fair trial, that the evidence was sufficient to convict, that the defendant had ample opportunity to consult with counsel regarding his decision to waive the jury for purposes of sentencing, that the death sentence was properly imposed, and that there was no evidence of any brutal or heinous behavior which accompanied the kidnapping and rape. The exceptionally brutal and heinous behavior was involved only in the murders, and could not have applied to the other sentences.


OUTCOME: The defendant's conviction and the sentence of death were affirmed. The extended terms of imprisonment imposed for the charges of rape and aggravated kidnapping were vacated. The sentence for rape was reduced to 30 years and the sentence for aggravated kidnapping to 15 years.

Kemner v. Monsanto Co.


Nos. 61691, 61749


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 223; 492 N.E.2d 1327; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 252; 97 Ill. Dec. 454; 56 A.L.R.4th 1191



April 18, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Richard P. Goldenhersh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; cause remanded. Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chemical company challenged the orders of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which upheld the trial court's orders that denied its motion to dismiss for forum non conveniens and prohibited the company from communicating with the media, in appellee victims' consolidated suits for chemical exposure damages which arose from a railroad-tank-car derailment in another state.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the chemical company's motion for dismissal based on forum non conveniens and issued a gag order prohibiting the chemical company from contact with the media. The appellate court concluded that it lacked jurisdiction to consider the chemical company's third appeal for reconsideration of forum non conveniens because the motion was time barred and upheld the gag order. The chemical company appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court remanded the forum non conveniens issue to the appellate court because the last motion on forum non conveniens raised new matters and was therefore timely. The victims' arguments were unpersuasive. The gag order was unconstitutional under the First Amendment because the mere possibility of juror influence made the order an impermissible prior restraint on speech. The order was also unconstitutionally overly broad because it restrained all media contact, vague because it was unclear what conduct and utterances were proscribed, and unnecessary because counsel had assured the court no further contact would occur, and less restrictive alternative measures like contempt of court were available.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court order and remanded the motion for forum non conveniens for the appellate court's determination. The trial court's order prohibiting the chemical company from contact with the media was reversed.

 

168 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Olinger


No. 58652


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 324; 493 N.E.2d 579; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 259; 97 Ill. Dec. 772



April 18, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Whiteside County, the Hon. Edward Keefe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Whiteside County (Illinois), which convicted defendant and his co-defendant of armed robbery, armed violence, and conspiracy. A jury was waived for sentencing, and defendant was sentenced to death, while his co-defendant was sentenced to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence of death, holding in part that where the State introduced a part of defendant's statement, he was entitled to have additional portions admitted if needed to prevent the jury from being misled. However, he had no right to introduce unrelated exculpatory statements in an attempt to avoid taking the stand. Defendant failed in his responsibility to specify what portion of his statements had to be admitted to avoid the jury from being misled. Defendant waived any potential claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, based on a potential conflict of his lawyer allegedly tampering with a witness, when he was apprised of the potential conflict when it arose and he allowed the representation to continue. The court held that denying defendant's motion to sever on the basis of antagonistic defenses was addressed to the sound discretion of the trial court, and any antagonism was not so severe as to deprive defendant of a fair trial. The use of a death-qualified jury was permissible, and the Illinois death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence to death. The court set the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out by lethal injection.

 

169 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


No. 62311


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 78; 491 N.E.2d 1163; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 242; 96 Ill. Dec. 703



April 4, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. A. A. Matoesian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss the capital sentencing proceedings. The state then filed a motion for direct appeal of the question of whether, on grounds of double jeopardy, it was precluded from attempting to obtain a death sentence a second time for the same conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's original death sentence for his murder conviction was reversed and remanded because of errors, which occurred during the sentencing hearing. At the sentencing hearing on remand, defendant argued that the state was precluded from attempting to obtain a death sentence a second time for the same conviction, on the grounds of double jeopardy. The trial court denied defendant's motion. On direct appeal, the court affirmed. The court agreed with defendant that double jeopardy principles can apply to capital sentencing hearings, even though they do not generally apply to sentencing determinations. The court found, however, that because the reversal of the sentencing was for trial error, rather than evidentiary insufficiency, it did not bar a second capital sentencing hearing. The court refused to apply the rule suggesting that the prosecution's deliberate provocation of a motion for mistrial would bar retrial because there was no evidence that the state had attempted to provoke a mistrial and defendant had failed to file a motion for mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the capital sentencing proceedings and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Free


No. 60911


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 154; 492 N.E.2d 1269; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 246; 97 Ill. Dec. 396



April 4, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-1 et seq. (1983), after defendant's conviction for murder had been affirmed by the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and the death penalty was imposed. After exhaustion of his state appellate rights, defendant filed a post-conviction petition, which was dismissed. The court affirmed the order that dismissed defendant's petition. The court held that: (1) the prosecutor did not abuse his discretion when he sought the death penalty because there was evidence of two aggravating factors and no evidence of any mitigating factors; (2) defendant failed to establish that his venire did not represent a fair cross-section of the community because he did not identify any independent evidence to support his allegation that the county engaged in discriminatory housing policies or that such policies resulted in a venire that did not represent a fair cross-section of the community; (3) the circuit court correctly concluded that an assistant defender from the public defender's office could represent defendant because the possibility of a conflict of interest was remote and unlikely, and defendant failed to show actual prejudice; and (4) qualification of jurors to impose the death penalty did not result in a conviction-prone jury so as to deny defendant his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed affirm the judgment of the circuit court that denied defendant's post-conviction petition. The court set an execution date and ordered that defendant be executed by lethal injection.

People v. Montgomery


No. 59138


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 517; 494 N.E.2d 475; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 275; 98 Ill. Dec. 353



April 4, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Samuels, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) alleging, inter alia, that there lacked probable cause for two arrests, that defendant's statements following the second arrest were the product of police confrontation with illegally obtained evidence, and that the lower court relied upon improper impeachment in rejecting defendant's suppression hearing testimony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and appealed the conviction on the grounds that there was a lack of probable cause to support his arrests, that fingerprints were unlawfully obtained and admitted into evidence, and that to support a finding that defendant was arrested outside of his home, the lower court erred in relying upon an improperly admitted statement impeaching defendant's suppression-hearing testimony. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that there was probable cause to support the first arrest because shortly after the murders, defendant appeared before the police in physical appearance that was both highly unusual and consistent with his having committed the crimes. The court held that defendant's fingerprints were lawfully obtained because defendant's person was subject to a full search incident to his first arrest. The court also held that the fingerprints provided the probable cause for the second arrest. The court held that the finding that defendant was arrested outside of his home was not based on improper evidence, as defendant's prior statements that he was outside at the time of the arrest were not made in support of a suppression motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

172 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Manor Healthcare Corp.


No. 61705


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 350; 489 N.E.2d 1374; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 205; 95 Ill. Dec. 510



February 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Creed Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Champaign County, Illinois, granted defendant nursing home's motion to dismiss plaintiff nursing home patient's request for treble damages under the Nursing Home Care Reform Act of 1979, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, par. 4151 -- 101 et seq., (1983). The patient appealed directly to the court, pursuant to 94 Ill. 2d R. 302(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: A nursing home patient alleged that her amputated leg was caused by the staff members' mistreatment. The court found that the Act's treble damages provisions did not violate due process by authorizing a double recovery for a single injury. The court held that treble damages were punitive damages and that the patient was entitled to proceed under two theories -- her statutory rights and common law action. The court found that the treble damages embraced the "private attorney general" concept and gave patients power to police abuses. The court found that if the jury found for the patient and returned a verdict that awarded the patient both recoveries, the trial court was to enter judgment on the two verdicts in the alternative so that the patient recovered only one satisfaction. The court found that the act was not "special legislation" and did not violate equal protection under the state or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that treble damages under state nursing home law were allowed, along with a common law action for wilful and wanton misconduct. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the nursing home law did not violate due process.

 

173 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Belmont Fire Protection Dist.


Nos. 61724, 61725 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 373; 489 N.E.2d 1385; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 206; 95 Ill. Dec. 521



February 21, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated cases, respondent fire districts challenged the constitutionality of An Act to add § 19a to An Act in relation to fire protection districts, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127 1/2, para. 38.2a (1983 Supp.). The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) found § 19(a) unconstitutional and dismissed referendum petitions filed thereunder. Petitioners took a direct appeal pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a)(1) (94 Ill. 2d R. 302(a)(1)).


OVERVIEW: The Illinois legislature added a provision to the statutes governing fire districts (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127 1/2, para. 38.2(a) (1983 supp.). This provision allowed for the adjustment of district lines when two or more districts lay within municipal boundaries, but applied only to one county in the state due to a population classification. In affirming a ruling that the amendment was unconstitutional, the court held that in considering the special-legislation proscription of the Illinois constitution, there had to be a reasonable basis for the classification and it had to bear a rational and proper relation to the evil to be remedied and the purpose to be attained by the legislation. The court agreed with the fire districts that there was no reasonable basis for the population classification, for there was no basis, in reason and principle, for regarding Du Page County as a distinct and separate class. If a real need existed to eliminate the alleged disadvantages and dangers of multiple fire protection districts serving one municipality, then the same need to remedy the evil also existed in other counties as well, regardless of the level of the population of the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that the legislation was unconstitutional special legislation.

 

174 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Boynton v. Kusper


Nos. 61314, 61315, 61324 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


112 Ill. 2d 356; 494 N.E.2d 135; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 260; 98 Ill. Dec. 208



February 21, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action brought by plaintiff marriage license applicants against defendants, county and state officers, to challenge the validity of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, par. 73 (1983), defendant advocacy group was permitted to intervene. On cross motions for summary judgment, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found the provision unconstitutional. The county, the state officers, and the advocacy group appealed directly to the court.


OVERVIEW: Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, par. 2403, 2403.1 (1983) required clerks in counties with a population exceeding one million to pay $ 10 of the $ 25 fee collected for issuing a marriage license into a domestic violence shelter and service fund. The marriage license applicants brought a class action challenging the validity of the provisions, maintaining that this portion of the license fee was an unconstitutional tax. The trial court found that the provision was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the statute was unconstitutional as a violation of the due process guarantee of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The imposition of a tax on the issuance of a marriage license did not bear a reasonable relation to the public interest sought to be protected and the means adopted was not a reasonable means of accomplishing the desired objective. The imposition of the special tax upon the issuance of a marriage license imposed a direct impediment to the exercise of the fundamental right to marry and had to be subjected to the heightened test of strict scrutiny. The court held that the state had not demonstrated a compelling state interest that would satisfy the strict-scrutiny test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that found that the provision was unconstitutional.

 

175 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mega v. Holy Cross Hospital


Nos. 60027, 60038 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 416; 490 N.E.2d 665; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 220; 95 Ill. Dec. 812



February 6, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 60027. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Brian B. Duff, Judge, presiding.

No. 60038. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital, in this consolidated appeal, challenged the rulings of the Appellate Court of the First District (Illinois) that reversed the trial court's findings that appellee patients' causes of action arising from medical treatment were barred by the four-year statute of repose set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-212 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Although patients' actions were based upon acts that occurred before the four-year repose provision took effect, they were untimely because they were commenced more than four years after that date. The new four-year repose provision shortened the limitations period, leaving patients no time in which to file their actions; thus, they were allowed a reasonable time to bring their actions. However, such a reasonable time did not extend beyond that provided by the new repose period. The repose period was intended to terminate the possibility of liability after a defined period of time regardless of a potential plaintiff's lack of knowledge of his cause of action. The court also rejected the constitutional challenges to the repose provision. It restricted the time within which an action could be brought, it did not eliminate an entire category or type of action. Further, it was extended for fraudulently concealed causes and causes in which equitable estoppel applied. In addition, the constitutionally established policy of providing a remedy for every wrong inflicted was tempered by the policy of barring actions brought after the period of time in the interests of justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

People v. Coleman


No. 61709


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 87; 488 N.E.2d 1009; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 216; 94 Ill. Dec. 762



January 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Edwin J. Richardson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of § 11-501(a) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a) (1983). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendant's request for a term of supervision. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol. He had previously been sentenced years before for the same type of offense and received court supervision. Defendant again requested court supervision, and the trial court granted it. Since defendant's first conviction, § 5-6-1(d) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-1(d) (Supp. 1984) was enacted, which provided that courts could not grant supervision to a defendant charged with driving under the influence of alcohol if the defendant had, within the previous five years, received supervision for the same offense. The lower court held that § 5-6-1(d) violated the ex post facto clause. The court reversed the lower court's determination that the statute was ex post facto. The court held that a statute that increased the sanction for a second offense was not ex post facto merely because adjudication of the first offense occurred before the statute was enacted or became effective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's sentence of a term of supervision and remanded for resentencing of defendant.

Walgreen Co. v. Illinois Liquor Control Com.


Nos. 60999, 61081 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 120; 488 N.E.2d 980; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 219; 94 Ill. Dec. 733



January 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, retail liquor licensees, state liquor control commission and an intervening defendant, appealed the determination of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that vacated its prior orders of summary judgment in the licensees favor and that permitted a local-option question of whether to prohibit liquor sales to be put on the ballot with only 10 percent of registered voters' signatures.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff licensees originally filed actions to challenge the validity of petitions to initiate a referendum as to whether certain liquor sales could be banned. The circuit court entered summary judgment in their favor but, after appellee intervening defendants' action in federal court was abstained from and sent to the circuit court, summary judgment was reversed. The circuit court found the Liquor Control Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 167 (1983), to be unconstitutional and held that the election code provisions applied to the petitions. The court granted appellants' motion to stay effects of the election results and permitted them to remain in operation pending the final disposition of their appeal. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the signature requirements of the Act did not deprive voters of equal protection or impinge upon their first amendment rights. Because neither a fundamental right nor a suspect class was involved, the statute needed only bear a rational relationship to the ends sought to be achieved by the state or to promote the interest the state had in protecting the economic stability of a legally authorized industry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the determination in favor of appellees opposition in appellant liquor licensees' action regarding the constitutionality of a liquor control act.
