Chicago Park Dist. v. Chicago


Nos. 60879, 61058 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 7; 488 N.E.2d 968; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 192; 94 Ill. Dec. 721



January 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Paul F. Elward, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant park district challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed a trial court's denial of a preliminary injunction against appellee city enjoining the collection of a mooring tax. Appellant challenged the size of the tax and argued that the ordinance permitting the tax was unconstitutional because appellee was a home rule unit and did not have the authority to impose the tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant park district filed a complaint for declaratory judgment to have appellee city's mooring tax declared unconstitutional. The trial court denied appellant's motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining collection of the tax and the appellate court affirmed. The court affirmed the affirmance of the denial of a preliminary injunction because the simple existence of statutes that demonstrated a legislative intent to exclude harbors from the "government and affairs" of appellee did not show that appellee was deprived of the authority to enact the ordinance under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(g). The court held that the presence of the statutes did not show that the legislature intended to establish and maintain an "exclusive statewide dominion" over harbors. Furthermore, Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(h) did not preclude appellee from having any governmental participation in recreational harbors because a home rule unit's taxing power was outside of the constitutional provision. With respect to the size of the tax, the court held that the term "incidental burden" did not refer to the amount of the tax but rather to the question of tax collection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant district's request for a preliminary injunction because appellee city was not deprived of the authority to enact a mooring tax under the state constitution. The court also held that with respect to the size of the tax, the term "incidental burden" did not refer to the amount of the tax but rather to the question of tax collection.

People v. King


No. 55703


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 514; 488 N.E.2d 949; 1986 Ill. LEXIS 208; 94 Ill. Dec. 702



January 23, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1986.
Motion denied by, US Supreme Court certiorari denied by King v. Illinois, 479 U.S. 872, 107 S. Ct. 249, 93 L. Ed. 2d 173, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 4161 (1986)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by People v. King, 192 Ill. 2d 189, 735 N.E.2d 569, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1220, 248 Ill. Dec. 918 (2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. King, 2017 IL App (1st) 122172-U, 2017 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 580 (Mar. 22, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Howard Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant claimed the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his inculpatory statements in its application of the Illinois felony murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(6) (1979), and in its imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review after he was convicted of murder and the death sentence was imposed. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed. The court held that the trial court's determination that defendant's inculpatory statements were voluntary was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court determined that the Illinois felony murder rule was properly applied to defendant who had knowingly performed the acts that had created a strong probability of death to the victim. The court ruled that defendant's pretrial waiver of a jury at the sentencing stage was not error even if defendant was never advised of the unanimity requirement for a jury to impose a sentence of death. The court held that defendant's waiver of the jury was knowing and voluntary. The court declined to consider the constitutionality of Illinois' death penalty statute as it had recently considered and overruled all the objections to the statute raised by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant was properly convicted of murder and the death penalty was properly imposed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and set a date for defendant's execution by lethal injection.

People v. Walker


No. 59212


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 484; 488 N.E.2d 529; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 339; 94 Ill. Dec. 530



December 20, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. John J. Hoban, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the imposition of the death sentence by the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) as a result of his conviction of two counts of murder and one count of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty as to two counts of murder and one count of armed robbery. The sentencing jury found the existence of statutory aggravating factors (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, pars. 9 - 1(3), (6) (1983)) and determined that there were mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death sentence. Accordingly, the court sentenced defendant to death on the murder counts and imposed a 30-year term of imprisonment on the armed robbery count. In affirming the sentence, the court held that, even if the trial court erred in explaining the possible sentence for each charge, defendant's purported belief that he would be sentenced to a term of years was untenable based on the record. Moreover, the court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in denying his post-judgment motion to withdraw his guilty plea and substitute it for a plea of guilty but mentally ill. The court found no error in the prosecutor's introduction, during sentencing, of evidence as to the personal traits of the victims. Lastly, the court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of the death sentence.

 

182 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Neal


No. 57781


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 180; 489 N.E.2d 845; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 341; 95 Ill. Dec. 283



December 20, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Harry D. Strouse, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant took a direct appeal from the orders of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of three counts of murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9 -- 1(a)(1) through (a)(3) (1981), and armed robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18 -- 2(a) (1981). The trial court imposed the death sentence on the murder counts and an extended-term sentence of 60 years on the armed robbery count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to the murder and robbery of a woman. On appeal, the court found that defendant's statement gave the police probable cause to arrest him because the officers did not need evidence sufficient to convict, but only knowledge of facts that would have led a reasonable man to believe that a crime had been committed and that it had been committed by defendant. The court agreed that the confession must be corroborated by some evidence, exclusive of the confession, tending to show that a crime did occur and that the defendant committed it; however, the court found that the physical evidence corroborated his statements. A prosecutor's comment on defendant's lack of remorse, even if taken as a comment on his failure to testify, was cured by a sustained objection and a general instruction to the jury. The court rejected constitutional challenges to the death penalty, particularly to "death-qualification" of the jury as being violative of his right to a jury that was fair cross-section of the community and as yielding a jury that was pre-disposed to convict. The court also held that an extended-term sentence could be imposed on the robbery despite a death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and armed robbery and the imposition of the death sentence and an extended-term sentence.

 

183 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Pavlakos v. Department of Labor


No. 61311


Supreme Court of Illinois


111 Ill. 2d 257; 489 N.E.2d 1325; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 342; 95 Ill. Dec. 461



December 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, buyer of business, appealed a decision for defendant, Department of Labor (department), by the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) in an action under § 2600 of the Unemployment Insurance Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 750 (1979) for unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties.


OVERVIEW: The buyer bought a business. Though the buyer was unaware of any debts owed to the department, the buyer sent the department a notice of the bulk sale pursuant to the Uniform Commercial Code. The department stated that the buyer owed the business' prior unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties. The buyer claimed that § 2600 violated its equal protection rights because of an unreasonable burden to discover the seller's debts owed to the department that was not required with other taxes. The buyer lost at the administrative, trial, and appellate court levels. The court affirmed the decision for the department because § 2600 merely required the seller to produce documentation from the department that there was no money owing. Thus, the buyer was not obligated to discover the department's debts. Also, § 2600 was constitutional because the difference between the taxes was reasonably related to the legitimate purpose of the Act to pay unemployment benefits. The buyer had an opportunity and did contest the claim. The department timely asserted the charges and did not take any actions upon which the buyer could have relied to excuse payment of the charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision against the buyer and ruled for the department in the action for unpaid contributions, interest, and penalties.

 

184 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wawczak


No. 61548


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 244; 486 N.E.2d 911; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 319; 93 Ill. Dec. 378



November 21, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Charles E. Ruth, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which held that (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-1003.1 (1983) of the Illinois Vehicle Code was unconstitutional and dismissed a charge pending against defendant under § 11 -- 1003.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of § 11-1003.1 of the Illinois Vehicle Code. Defendant allegedly drove into the path of a bicyclist who struck the rear of defendant's automobile. The circuit court dismissed the charge, holding that § 11-1003.1 was unconstitutional. Specifically, the circuit court found that § 11-1003.1 was vague and ambiguous because it did not apprise a driver of any way to avoid being cited. The circuit court also held that the statute was invalid in part because the statute required a driver to exercise "due care" but did not define the term. The state appealed and the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings, holding that § 11-1003.1 was not unconstitutionally. The court noted that a statute was not vague merely because it required the trier of fact to determine whether a driver employed that degree of care which a reasonable person would have employed in a similar situation. The court concluded that, when the statute was considered with reference to the judicial definition of "due care," it was not impermissibly vague. The statute was not ambiguous as to what type of vehicle owed a duty of "due care" and to whom the duty was owed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court which dismissed charges pending against defendant under the Illinois Vehicle Code on the basis that the section under which defendant was charged was unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings.

 

185 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Niven v. Siqueira


No. 61137


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 357; 487 N.E.2d 937; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 329; 94 Ill. Dec. 60



November 21, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Edwin M. Berman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, defendant hospital and third parties, a hospital accrediting organization and its president, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which ordered disclosure of documents to plaintiffs and held the president in contempt for failing to make disclosure. The hospital and third parties argued that the requested documents were privileged under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-2101.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against the hospital and also against a doctor and hospital administrators for medical malpractice. On plaintiffs' application, the trial court issued a subpoena to the hospital accrediting organization, seeking discovery of reports and surveys in the hands of the organization relating to accreditation of the hospital. The trial court denied the motions of the hospital and the organization to quash the subpoena and held the president in contempt when he refused to comply with the subpoena. The court granted direct appeal. The version of § 8-2101 in effect when the action was brought provided only that the kind of information sought by plaintiffs was confidential and non-admissible. The statute was amended while the action was pending to provide that such information was privileged and non-discoverable. The court held the amendment applied to the pending litigation because the statute was a matter of procedure. The court held that although the organization was not specifically mentioned in the statute, it fell within the statute's general category of "allied medical societies," and thus the documents were privileged in its hands.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that the accreditation materials were subject to discovery and also the order finding the organization's president in contempt.

 

186 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mueller


No. 61519


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 378; 488 N.E.2d 523; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 331; 94 Ill. Dec. 524



November 21, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cass County, the Hon. Cecil J. Burrows, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed his conviction for homicidal concealment. Defendant contended that § 3 --4(b)(1) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3 -- 4(b)(1) (1981), and principles of double jeopardy barred his prosecution for homicidal concealment in one county after he was acquitted of the charge of murder in another county.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed two people in one county and disposed of their bodies in another. He was acquitted of the murder by reason of self-defense. On appeal, his conviction was affirmed. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3 -- 4(b)(1) (1981) did not bar the second prosecution because that statute only barred a subsequent prosecution for a different offense for which he could actually have been convicted in the first trial. He could not have been convicted of homicidal concealment in the murder trial because it was not a lesser included offense of murder nor was he charged with that offense. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3 --3, the state's joinder statute, did not require that the offenses be prosecuted together. The conviction did not violate his constitutional protection against double jeopardy because he was not twice put in jeopardy for the offense of homicidal concealment. The elements of the two crimes were wholly distinct, each with different necessary elements, requiring proof of different facts. Because the prosecutions were for different offenses, he was not deprived of his double jeopardy rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for the offense of homicidal concealment.

People v. Williams


No. 61071


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 391; 488 N.E.2d 255; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 332; 94 Ill. Dec. 429



November 21, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Francis Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) a petition for post-conviction relief. Following the dismissal of the petition, the state's motion for a direct appeal to the court was allowed, 94 Ill. 2d R. 302(b).


OVERVIEW: The inmate originally pleaded guilty to a charge of murder, inter alia, and was sentenced by a jury to death. The court affirmed the judgment on direct appeal and the United States Supreme Court denied certiorari. In the instant appeal, the inmate, who was black, argued that the state's use of its peremptory challenges unconstitutionally excluded blacks from serving on the jury that sentenced him to death, an argument raised in his original appeal, and that he had a constitutional right to have his appeal heard by the appellate court. The court held that the information provided by the inmate failed to meet the threshold suggested in a Supreme Court case for raising the constitutional issue. Moreover, the requirement that the jury contain a fair cross-section of the community apparently was satisfied in the inmate's case. The circuit court correctly ruled that the post-conviction petition did not warrant a hearing. As to the inmate's assertion that he had a constitutional right to have the appeal heard by the appellate court, the validity of the procedures for a direct appeal had been determined already and the court declined to reconsider its decisions on the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief. The court directed the clerk to enter an order fixing a certain date as the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out.

People v. Wisslead


No. 60863


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 389; 484 N.E.2d 1081; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 285; 92 Ill. Dec. 226



October 18, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McDonough County, the Hon. U. S. Collins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault, vacated defendant's assault conviction as a lesser included offense, and reversed defendant's unlawful restraint conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful restraint, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-3(a) (1983), aggravated assault, and assault, and was sentenced to consecutive probationary terms. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the appellate court and affirmed in part and vacated in part the trial court. The court held that a charging instrument was required to set forth the nature and elements of the offense charged and that the information sufficiently apprised defendant of the offense of unlawful restraint. The court held that para. 10-3(a) was not unconstitutionally vague or overly broad and its classification as a felony and its penalties were a valid exercise of the legislative power. The court also held that unlawful restraint was neither a form of aggravated assault nor a lesser included offense because aggravated assault was concerned with threatened bodily harm and unlawful restraint was concerned with the actual restriction of another's freedom.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the appellate court's upholding of defendant's conviction for aggravated assault and vacating defendant's assault conviction as a lesser included offense. The court reversed in part the appellate court's ruling on defendant's unlawful restraint conviction. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence of defendant for unlawful restraint.

People v. Bossie


No. 60663


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 236; 483 N.E.2d 1269; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 272; 91 Ill. Dec. 634



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County, the Hon. Frederick Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was the State's appeal, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 603, 87 Ill. 2d R. 603, of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which dismissed the State's charges against 21 defendants under §§ 4 and 5 of the Illinois Public Demonstrations Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 85-1 et seq. (1983). The circuit court held § 5 unconstitutional in violation of First and Fourteenth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' charges arose out of an anti-nuclear demonstration in which they were accused of blocking a roadway. On appeal, the State argued that the act was a constitutionally permissible time, place and manner restriction, directed at conduct, or the "nonspeech element" of the demonstration, rather than at its content, or the "speech element." The court noted that § 5 of the statute provided that notice of any march, assembly, meeting or gathering must be given in writing to "the principal law enforcement officer." However, the term was never defined. Correctly identifying the person requiring notice mandated knowledge of whether the demonstration was to be in a municipal or county roadway. For marches that crossed boundaries of several political subdivisions, demonstrators would have had to guess whether notice needed to be given where the march originated, where it terminated, where it passed through, or all of them. The court held that the law was unconstitutional and that its severability clause could not save any portion of the statute because it had no provision that could be given effect in the absence of a clear definition of the term "principal law enforcement officer."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that the law was unconstitutional.

In re Rothenberg


No. 61413


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 313; 484 N.E.2d 289; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 280; 91 Ill. Dec. 730



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Disciplinary proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Reinstatement denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney filed exceptions to the Review Board's (Illinois) affirmance of the hearing board's recommendation that the attorney's petition for reinstatement be denied. However, the review board found that the hearing board panel erred in admitting letters of support submitted by the attorney.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was disbarred after he was convicted in federal court of conspiracy to transport stolen goods in interstate commerce and aiding and abetting the transportation of stolen goods in interstate commerce. The attorney filed his petition for reinstatement in the same month that his probation period ended. In addition to testimony, the hearing board panel also admitted into evidence 30 letters offered by the attorney that were written by a variety of individuals in support of his reinstatement. The attorney argued that the recommendation by the hearing board and review board that his petition for reinstatement be denied was contrary to the weight of the evidence. The court evaluated the factors to be considered in determining the attorney's rehabilitation, good character, and knowledge of the law and found that (1) the attorney was convicted for participation in a scheme to transport stolen jewelry in interstate commerce; (2) the conviction was a further manifestation of a pattern of misconduct that began shortly after the attorney was licensed to practice law; and (3) there was no proof that the attorney made restitution. Finally, it was not error to admit the letters.


OUTCOME: The court denied the attorney's petition for reinstatement. The evidence was insufficient to establish that the attorney had brought to an end the pattern of serious misconduct that began shortly after he was admitted to the bar and culminated in his federal conviction for participating in the scheme to transport stolen jewelry in interstate commerce.

Yellow Cab Co. v. Jones


No. 60579


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 330; 483 N.E.2d 1278; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 281; 91 Ill. Dec. 643



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of an order from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed a trial court's decision setting aside a compensation award, and reinstated the Industrial Commission's decision confirming the compensation awarded to appellee employee for permanent disability.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employee was awarded compensation for permanent disability against appellant employer for accidental injuries arising out of and in the course of his employment. The Industrial Commission (commission) reduced the amount awarded appellee and otherwise confirmed the award. A lower court reversed a trial court's decision setting aside the award, and reinstated the commission's decision. Appellant sought review of the lower court's judgment. The court affirmed, finding no restriction or limitation on the power of the Illinois Supreme Court to designate the number of divisions, to assign judges to those divisions, or determine the number of judges to serve on each division, so long as there were no less than three. The court found no constitutional impediment to the designation of judges in the manner provided in Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 22(g) to serve on the panel, which reviewed the commission's orders. The court found that the provision at issue was reasonable, and held that it did not serve to deprive appellant of either equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a lower court's judgment reinstating a commission's decision confirming appellee employee's compensation award for permanent disability against appellant employer because there was no constitutional impediment to the designation of judges, which reviewed the commission's orders, as provided in an Illinois court rule, and the provision at issue did not deprive appellant of either equal protection or due process.

Chicago Nat'l League Ball Club, Inc. v. Thompson


No. 61630


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 357; 483 N.E.2d 1245; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 283; 91 Ill. Dec. 610



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant baseball club brought suit seeking a declaratory judgment that an amendment to the Environmental Protection Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1025 (1983), and a city ordinance violated various provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The baseball club sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment for appellees, governor, city, and council.


OVERVIEW: A 1982 amendment to the Environmental Protection Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1025 (1983), and a Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 104.1--14.1, by their terms, effectively denied only Wrigley Stadium from holding events at certain times as part of noise emission regulations. The baseball club asserted that because the enactments only applied to Wrigley Field, the classifications were a legislative attempt to correct a private nuisance. The court found that it was within the legislative discretion to have enacted the regulations for the proper purpose of protecting the public against a specific public nuisance. Because the statutes at issue only applied to Wrigley Field, the baseball club asserted that they were violative of the principle of separation of powers and denied them due process. The court that the classifications of population, status of the sporting events, hours of usage, and type of facility, were reasonably related to a legitimate purpose. Thus, the baseball club failed to demonstrate the unconstitutionality of the legislative actions.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding the statute and ordinance to be reasonable exercises of police power was affirmed.

Buzz Barton & Associates, Inc. v. Giannone


No. 60609


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 373; 483 N.E.2d 1271; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 284; 91 Ill. Dec. 636



October 3, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Fredrick Henzi, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employer brought an injunctive action against defendants, present employer and employee. The present employer and the employee filed a petition for the assessment of damages for the wrongful issuance of the former employer's preliminary injunction. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) denied the motion. The present employer and the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee agreed by contract not to solicit the former employer's customers or to work with any of the former employer's competitors for one year after his termination. When the employee violated the terms, the former employer obtained a preliminary injunction to enforce the contract terms against the employee and his present employer. The preliminary injunction was dissolved on appeal. The request for damages against the former employer for the wrongful issuance of the preliminary injunction was denied on the grounds that Ill. Code Civ. P. 11-110, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 10 (1983), was unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded and held that there was no invidious discrimination under the Equal Protection Clause in the application of § 11-110. Where a party was wrongfully granted a preliminary injunction, the wronged party was entitled to damages. There was no violation of due process because Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 was a statement of a philosophy and not a mandate for a remedy. Although § 11-110 did not apply to permanent injunctions, the former employer was clearly granted a preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision and ruled in favor of the present employer and the employee against the former employer for damages from the wrongful issuance of a preliminary injunction.

 

196 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bean


No. 56448


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 80; 485 N.E.2d 349; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 307; 92 Ill. Dec. 538



October 3, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions for murder, armed robbery, home invasion, conspiracy, and solicitation by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a codefendant were jointly tried for a variety of crimes connected with the death of an elderly woman. Evidence showed that defendant offered to murder the victim in exchange for money. The trial court denied defendant's motion for severance. Defendant asserted that he would be prejudiced by the codefendant's planned defense, which placed all blame for the murder on defendant. The trial court overruled defendant's repeated objections to statements made at trial by the codefendant's counsel and denied defendant's motions for a mistrial. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. Defendant's motion for severance should have been granted because his defense and his codefendant's defense were so antagonistic to each other that defendant could not receive a fair trial. Statements by the codefendant's counsel specifically commenting on defendant's failure to testify violated his rights under the U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 155-1. Defendant's motions for severance and mistrial were sufficiently specific to put the trial judge on notice that defendant's rights would be violated if he and the codefendant were tried jointly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial.

 

197 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bales


Nos. 60347, 60348, 60349


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 182; 483 N.E.2d 517; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 266; 91 Ill. Dec. 171



September 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Robert A. Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged by the state with residential burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-3 (1983) in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois). The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, holding the statute violated the constitutional guarantees of due process, and that the mandatory minimum sentence violated the limitation-of-penalties provision of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the phrase "dwelling place of another" did not afford a person of ordinary intelligence a reasonable opportunity to know what conduct was prohibited, law-enforcement authorities were given unreasonable and arbitrary discretion over whether to charge a defendant with residential burglary or burglary, and that the mandatory sentencing provision violated the limitation-of-penalties provision. The court held the statute was constitutional and reversed the trial court. The court analyzed the phrase "dwelling place of another" and looked to the legislative intent, and determined the phrase should be given a meaning accorded to that of burglary at common law, which was an offense against habitation not just an offense against property. Given that construction, the phrase was not unconstitutionally vague and did not provide law-enforcement authorities unreasonable and arbitrary discretion. The protection of interests other than property, and the need for a more stringent penalty provision in order to halt an increase in the commission of the crime were proper factors in determining the sentencing scheme, and it did not violate the limitation-of-penalties provision.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court holding the residential burglary statute unconstitutional was reversed and the causes were remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

198 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harmison


No. 60378


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 197; 483 N.E.2d 508; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 267; 91 Ill. Dec. 162



September 20, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Richard E. Eagleton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for calculated criminal drug conspiracy under § 405(a) of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1405(a) (1981). Defendant argued on appeal that the mandatory fine imposed under § 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 (1981), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of calculated criminal drug conspiracy and delivery of a controlled substance, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1405(a), 1401(b)(2) (1981). In addition to a sentence of confinement, the trial court imposed a fine based on the street value of the contraband. The appellate court reversed the conviction for conspiracy, affirmed the conviction for delivery, and remanded for resentencing. The court allowed the state's petition for leave to appeal, and affirmed. Under para. 1405(b)(2), the conspiracy required the participation of defendant and two or more other persons. The court found that the evidence was insufficient to show that three individuals participated in a common scheme to deliver cocaine to an undercover agent. Defendant did not get the cocaine directly from the supplier and the supplier did not know about defendant's participation in the sale. The court further held that the mandatory fine imposed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1.1 did not deprive defendant of due process and equal protection of the law. The legislature had wide discretion to classify offenses and prescribe penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court reversing defendant's conviction for calculated criminal drug conspiracy. The court also affirmed the mandatory fine imposed in connection with defendant's conviction for delivery of a controlled substance.

People v. Dugan


No. 60560


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 8; 485 N.E.2d 315; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 299; 92 Ill. Dec. 504



September 20, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. William D. Block and William F. Homer, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed defendants' convictions by one trial court for syndicated gambling under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 28-1.1 (1981), because there was no evidence that the gambling bets were recorded, but affirmed the civil forfeiture order for a car of a defendant by another trial court. The two trial court rulings were consolidated on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were operating an private club where patrons bet on card and dice games. After their arrest for syndicated gambling, one defendant stated to a police officer that the car in the parking lot was his, even though it was titled in a friend's name. The court affirmed the trial court's judgments, but reversed in part, and affirmed in part the appellate court's judgment. The court held that the convictions for syndicated gambling were appropriate because the definition of "bookmaking" found in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 28-1.1(d), was broad enough to include defendants' conduct. The court also ruled that record-keeping of the bet was not a required element of the syndicated gambling offensem nor was proof that defendants were engaged in the "business of bookmaking," above the minimum statutory requirements that there was evidence of more than five bets or wagers totaling more than $ 2,000. The court also ruled that the trial court's conclusions that the seized car was used in the commission of a gambling offense and that one defendant owned the car, though it was not titled in his name, was not against the manifest weight of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that order the civil forfeiture of a defendant's car, but reversed the judgment that reversed defendants' convictions for syndicated gambling. The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

Rossetti Contracting Co. v. Court of Claims


No. 61163


Supreme Court of Illinois


109 Ill. 2d 72; 485 N.E.2d 332; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 306; 92 Ill. Dec. 521



September 20, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur J. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subcontractor sought to intervene in an action brought by the contractor against the state to recover under a contract. The court of claims denied the petition. The circuit court denied certiorari on the subcontractor's petition against respondent court of claims. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) dismissed the subcontractor's appeal of that judgment and the subcontractor challenged that judgment as well.


OVERVIEW: The contractor for which the subcontractor did work sought to recover the cost of work performed on contracts with the state. The subcontractor's work was included in the complaint. The state asserted an affirmative defense of fraud on the part of the contractor under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 439.14 (1975) to avoid the claim. The subcontractor, who denied any involvement in the alleged fraud, was denied the right to intervene. The circuit court held that it was without jurisdiction to review the matter. The court allowed the subcontractor's petition to appeal and remanded the cause to the court of claims so that the subcontractor could be afforded the opportunity to be heard. The court held that (1) it had the authority to determine whether the court of claims acted to unconstitutionally deprive the subcontractor if its right to due process; (2) the court of claims, by applying para. 439.14 to the subcontractor without allowing the subcontractor to be heard, deprived it of due process of law; and (3) the Court of Claims Act did give that court exclusive jurisdiction over claims brought against the state, but it did not deny review of those claims by other tribunals.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the subcontractor's claim to the court of claims with directions that the subcontractor be afforded the opportunity to be heard in that forum.
